# RES 2026 题库（含答案与解析）— Paper 1

> 共 180 题。每题附正确答案、解析与易错点。建议先盖住答案作答，再核对。
> 所有数字均按 2026 年现行规定生成并经二次核查；如遇 CEA/IRAS 政策更新，以官方为准。


## P1.1 The Real Estate Agency Industry & Regulatory Framework (CEA, Estate Agents Act)

**Q1.** A new RES candidate is studying the regulatory structure of Singapore's real estate agency industry. Which statement correctly describes the Council for Estate Agencies (CEA)?

- A. It is a statutory board under the Ministry of National Development that administers the Estate Agents Act and licenses estate agencies and registers salespersons
- B. It is a private trade association under MAS that sets commission rates for the industry
- C. It is a department within HDB that approves all HDB resale transactions
- D. It is a self-regulatory body run by the estate agencies themselves with no statutory powers

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> CEA was established on 22 Oct 2010 as a statutory board under the Ministry of National Development (MND) and administers the Estate Agents Act 2010, licensing EAs and registering RESs. B is wrong: CEA is not under MAS and does NOT fix commission (commission is fully negotiable). C is wrong: CEA is separate from HDB and does not approve resale transactions. D is wrong: CEA is a statutory regulator with full statutory disciplinary powers, not a self-regulatory trade body. 中文一句话: CEA 是国家发展部下的法定机构，依《地产代理法令》监管行业。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – About CEA / Estate Agents Act 2010

---

**Q2.** In CEA terminology, which pairing of 'licensed' versus 'registered' is correct?

- A. The individual salesperson is licensed; the estate agency is registered
- B. The estate agency (firm) is licensed; the individual salesperson is registered
- C. Both the firm and the salesperson are licensed
- D. Both the firm and the salesperson are registered

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> An Estate Agent (EA) is the firm and holds a licence; a Real Estate Salesperson (RES) is the individual and is registered with CEA through one licensed EA (single-agency rule). A reverses the two terms, a classic exam trap. C and D incorrectly apply one status to both. 中文一句话: 公司持牌(licensed)，个人注册(registered)，切勿调换。
>
> 📎 Source: Estate Agents Act 2010; CEA

---

**Q3.** From 1 January 2026, CEA's revised CPD framework (under Project ADEPT) requires each RES to complete how many training hours per year, and in what split?

- A. 16 hours total: 4 hours Structured Learning plus 12 hours Self-Directed Learning
- B. 6 credits total over an October-to-September cycle, with no Self-Directed component
- C. 16 hours total: 12 hours Structured Learning (including at least 4 hours of Prescribed Essentials) plus 4 hours Self-Directed Learning
- D. 12 hours total, all of which must be Prescribed Essentials

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> The 2026 framework (effective 1 Jan 2026) requires 16 training hours per year: 12h Structured Learning (SL), of which at least 4h must be the Prescribed Essentials (PE) topic (the 2026 PE topic is PMLPFTF / AML-CFT), plus 4h Self-Directed Learning (SDL). B describes the OLD (pre-2026) regime of 6 credits on an Oct-Sep cycle. A inverts the SL/SDL split. D wrongly makes all 12h Prescribed Essentials (PE is only the minimum 4h within the 12h SL). 中文一句话: 2026年起每年16小时 = 12小时结构化学习(含≥4小时规定必修)+4小时自主学习。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – Transforming Your CPD Journey: Key Changes from 2026 / Project ADEPT

---

**Q4.** RES Daniel and RES Priya both work for the SAME licensed estate agency. Daniel acts for the seller and Priya acts for the buyer in the same condominium transaction. Which statement is correct under CEA rules?

- A. It is allowed only if the agency obtains prior written approval from CEA for each such transaction
- B. This is automatically an offence of dual representation because they share the same employer
- C. It is allowed only if Daniel collects the full commission and shares it informally with Priya
- D. This is permitted and is NOT dual representation, provided both declare in writing they are from the same EA, obtain written consent, and neither RES collects fees from both sides

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> Two RES from the same EA on opposite sides is NOT dual representation, provided neither collects from both sides, both declare in writing that they are from the same EA, and both obtain their respective client's written consent. A captures these conditions. B is wrong: same-EA opposite-side representation is not automatically an offence. C is wrong: it describes a single RES being paid by both sides, which IS the prohibited dual representation. A is wrong: no transaction-by-transaction CEA approval is required; the safeguard is written disclosure and consent. 中文一句话: 同公司两名经纪分别代表买卖双方，只要书面声明、取得同意且各自只收一方佣金，便不构成双重代理。
>
> 📎 Source: CEPCC; CEA conflict-of-interest rules

---

**Q5.** RES Marcus represents the seller of an HDB flat. The buyer is unrepresented, so Marcus also collects a commission from the buyer and shares it with no one. Which statement BEST describes Marcus's situation?

- A. He has committed dual representation, an offence, because a single RES collected and benefited from fees from both sides of the same transaction
- B. He has acted properly because the buyer was unrepresented and consented to pay him
- C. He has acted properly because commission is fully negotiable and not regulated by CEA
- D. He is only in breach if the combined commission exceeds the prescribed statutory cap

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(hard)_
>
> Dual representation occurs when one RES collects (or shares) fees from BOTH sides of the same transaction; it is an offence under Reg 5(1) of the Estate Agents (Estate Agency Work) Regulations 2010 (a real case drew a $9,000 fine, in default 2 months' imprisonment). A is correct. B is wrong: buyer consent does not cure dual representation; a single agent cannot be paid by both sides. C is a trap: commission being negotiable does not legalise collecting from both sides. D is wrong: there is no statutory commission cap that defines the breach; the breach is collecting from both sides at all. 中文一句话: 同一名经纪向买卖双方收费即构成违法的双重代理，与佣金是否封顶或买方同意无关。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – Dual representation prohibition (Reg 5(1) EAW Regulations 2010); CEPCC

---

**Q6.** A complaint is lodged with CEA against an RES, and the consumer also wants to recover $8,500 he claims he overpaid. Which statement is correct?

- A. CEA will both discipline the RES and order the RES to refund the $8,500 to the consumer
- B. CEA handles discipline against the RES but does NOT recover money for the consumer; the consumer may use the CEA Dispute Resolution Scheme (mediation/adjudication) or the Small Claims Tribunals for the monetary claim
- C. The consumer must go straight to the High Court because CEA has no role in such complaints
- D. Only the Small Claims Tribunals can hear the disciplinary complaint, not CEA

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> CEA's role is regulatory/disciplinary; it does NOT recover money for consumers. Monetary recovery is pursued via the CEA Dispute Resolution Scheme (mediation through SMC plus adjudication) or the Small Claims Tribunals (SCT jurisdiction is up to $20,000, or up to $30,000 with both parties' written consent via a Memorandum of Consent), so an $8,500 claim fits comfortably within the SCT. B is correct. A is wrong: CEA disciplines but does not order consumer refunds. C is wrong: CEA does handle the conduct complaint and the High Court is not the required first step. D is wrong: SCT hears the money claim, not the disciplinary complaint, which CEA handles. 中文一句话: CEA 负责纪律处分但不替消费者追讨金钱；追款须经争议解决机制或小额索偿法庭（上限$20,000，双方同意可达$30,000）。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA Dispute Resolution Schemes Regulations 2011; Small Claims Tribunals Act 1984

---

**Q7.** An RES is found by a CEA Disciplinary Committee to have committed a serious (non-AML) breach in a single case. What is the maximum financial penalty the DC can impose on the RES, and on an EA for the same type of breach?

- A. RES up to $200,000; EA up to $100,000
- B. RES up to $5,000; EA up to $10,000
- C. RES up to $100,000; EA up to $200,000
- D. RES up to $50,000; EA up to $250,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> A CEA Disciplinary Committee (at least 3 members from the Disciplinary Panel) can impose a financial penalty of up to $100,000 on an RES and up to $200,000 on an EA for serious breaches. C is correct. B describes the Letter of Censure (LOC) framework cap of $5,000 per case for LESS serious breaches, not DC penalties. C swaps the RES and EA figures. D uses invented amounts. (Note: for AML/CFT breaches under the 2025 Act, these caps apply per breach rather than per case.) 中文一句话: 纪律委员会对经纪最高罚款$100,000，对公司最高$200,000；$5,000 是较轻违规的训诫信上限。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – Disciplinary proceedings; Estate Agents Act 2010

---

**Q8.** In CEA's disciplinary process, after the Statement of Case is served, an RES respondent submits an Admission/Defence, then a Reply and Rejoinder follow. What is the time limit for each of these steps, and the window to appeal a DC decision?

- A. 14 days for each pleading step, and 30 days to appeal to the Small Claims Tribunals
- B. 30 days for each pleading step, and 30 days to appeal to CEA itself
- C. 7 days for each pleading step, and 21 days to appeal to the High Court
- D. 14 days for each pleading step, and 14 days to appeal to the MND Appeals Board

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> Each pleading step (Admission/Defence, Reply, Rejoinder) carries a 14-day window, and an appeal against a DC decision goes to the MND Appeals Board within 14 days of being notified of the decision. D is correct. B uses wrong timing and the wrong appeal body (you do not appeal to CEA itself). C and D use incorrect timeframes and the wrong appellate forum (High Court / SCT are not the DC appeal route). 中文一句话: 各答辩步骤各14天，对纪律委员会裁决须在14天内向国家发展部上诉委员会上诉。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – Disciplinary proceedings / Appeals; Estate Agents Act 2010

---

**Q9.** Which of the following correctly distinguishes the CEPCC from the COPEA?

- A. The CEPCC sets the standard of conduct owed by individuals toward clients and the public; the COPEA is firm-level and covers management, supervision, the Estate Agent Card, complaints procedures and record retention
- B. The CEPCC is firm-level; the COPEA governs only individual salespersons' advertising
- C. Both apply only to estate agency firms, not to individual salespersons
- D. The COPEA is the principal Act, and the CEPCC is a non-binding industry guide

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> The Code of Ethics and Professional Client Care (CEPCC) sets conduct standards owed toward clients/public, while the Code of Practice for Estate Agents (COPEA) is firm-level, covering management and supervision, the Estate Agent Card, claims/complaints procedures, and document/records retention. A is correct. B reverses their levels. C is wrong because the CEPCC applies to individual conduct. D is wrong: neither is the principal Act (that is the EAA 2010); both are prescribed and binding under the Estate Agents (Estate Agency Work) Regulations 2010. 中文一句话: CEPCC 规范个人对客户/公众的职业操守；COPEA 是公司层面的执业守则。
>
> 📎 Source: Estate Agents (Estate Agency Work) Regulations 2010 – CEPCC & COPEA

---

**Q10.** Under the COPEA, for how long must an estate agency retain transaction documents and records, and what prompted the current retention period?

- A. At least 3 years, with paper originals only
- B. At least 5 years, raised from 3 years to align with AML/CFT requirements; electronic records are acceptable
- C. At least 10 years, to match HDB Minimum Occupation Period rules
- D. At least 7 years, set by IRAS for income tax purposes

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> COPEA Para 7(1) requires records to be kept for at least 5 years, raised from 3 years to align with AML/CFT (customer due diligence) requirements; electronic records are permitted. B is correct. A states the old 3-year period. C confuses retention with HDB MOP. D cites an IRAS tax-record period, not the COPEA requirement. 中文一句话: 根据 COPEA，记录须至少保存5年（与反洗钱要求一致），电子记录可接受。
>
> 📎 Source: COPEA Para 7(1), EAW Regulations 2010; AML/CFT record retention

---

**Q11.** A property buyer is from a country with an ABSD-relevant Free Trade Agreement and asks his RES whether he is exempt from Additional Buyer's Stamp Duty. Under the current FTA arrangement, nationals/PRs of which group are accorded the SAME ABSD treatment as Singapore Citizens?

- A. Malaysian citizens and Chinese nationals
- B. All EU citizens and all Commonwealth citizens
- C. US citizens, and citizens and PRs of Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway and Switzerland
- D. Australian and New Zealand citizens only

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> Under Singapore's FTAs (the USSFTA and the Singapore-EFTA FTA), US nationals and the nationals/PRs of Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway and Switzerland are accorded the same stamp-duty treatment as Singapore Citizens (i.e., 0% ABSD on a first residential property). C is correct. B is wrong: there is no blanket EU or Commonwealth exemption. A is wrong: Malaysians and Chinese nationals are treated as foreigners (60% ABSD), though Malaysians have HDB-specific provisions elsewhere. D is wrong: Australia and NZ are not on the FTA list. 中文一句话: 仅美国公民及冰岛、列支敦士登、挪威、瑞士的公民/PR 在 ABSD 上享有等同新加坡公民的待遇。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS – ABSD remission under FTAs (USSFTA, EFTA)

---

**Q12.** A candidate sits Paper 1 of the RES examination on 18 July 2026 and scores 58 out of 100. She also completed 80% attendance of her RES course. Which statement is correct about her result?

- A. Her score is irrelevant because both papers are marked together as a single combined total
- B. She has PASSED because 75% attendance is the pass mark and she exceeded it
- C. She has PASSED Paper 1 because anything above 50/100 is a pass
- D. She has FAILED Paper 1 because the exam pass mark is 60/100; the 75% figure relates to course attendance, not the exam

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> The exam pass mark is 60/100 per paper (each paper passed independently), so 58/100 is a fail. The 75% figure is the minimum RES course attendance requirement (needed to be eligible to sit the exam), not the exam pass mark. D is correct. B confuses attendance with the exam pass mark. C invents a 50% threshold. A is wrong: each paper is passed independently, not combined. 中文一句话: 考试及格线是每卷60/100，58分不及格；75% 是课程出席率而非考试及格线。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – Prepare for the RES Examination

---

**Q13.** A salesperson wants to become a Key Executive Officer (KEO). Which of the following is NOT a requirement to be a KEO under CEA rules?

- A. Holding a current valid RES registration concurrently with another estate agency while serving as KEO
- B. Being at least 21 years old and having at least 3 years' experience as a salesperson
- C. Having handled at least 30 transactions in the past 3 years, including at least 10 private and at least 10 HDB
- D. Possessing at least 4 GCE 'O' Level passes and a valid REA examination pass, and being fit and proper

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> The question asks which is NOT a requirement. A KEO CANNOT concurrently be an RES, sole proprietor, partner or director of another EA, so A correctly identifies the disqualifier (it is prohibited, not required). B, C and D are all genuine KEO eligibility requirements: at least 21 and at least 3 years' experience; at least 30 transactions (at least 10 private, at least 10 HDB) in the past 3 years; 4 'O' Level passes plus a valid REA exam pass (or equivalent) and fit-and-proper status. 中文一句话: KEO 不可同时兼任其他公司的 RES/独资经营者/合伙人/董事，其余三项皆为任职条件。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – KEO eligibility requirements

---

**Q14.** Which statement BEST describes the legal effect of the Anti-Money Laundering and Other Matters (Estate Agents and Developers) Act 2025?

- A. It replaced the Estate Agents Act 2010 entirely as the new principal statute for the industry
- B. It became operational on 1 July 2025, strengthening AML/CFT obligations and raising maximum penalties (with certain AML caps applying on a per-breach basis)
- C. It abolished the Council for Estate Agencies and transferred its functions to MAS
- D. It removed the requirement for estate agencies to conduct customer due diligence

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> The Act was passed in April 2025 and came into operation on 1 July 2025, strengthening AML/CFT measures and raising maximum penalties, with certain AML-related penalty caps now applying per breach. It amends the Estate Agents Act 2010, the Housing Developers (Control and Licensing) Act 1965 and the Sale of Commercial Properties Act 1979. B is correct. A is wrong: the EAA 2010 remains the principal statute; the 2025 Act amends/supplements it. C is wrong: CEA was not abolished and functions did not move to MAS. D is the opposite of the truth: the Act reinforces, not removes, CDD obligations. 中文一句话: 2025年反洗钱法令于2025年7月1日生效，强化反洗钱义务并提高罚款上限，并非取代《地产代理法令》。
>
> 📎 Source: AML and Other Matters (Estate Agents and Developers) Act 2025

---

**Q15.** Which of the following is a correct statement about RES registration and the single-agency rule?

- A. An RES may operate independently without being attached to any licensed estate agency
- B. An RES may be registered with up to three estate agencies simultaneously to maximise listings
- C. An RES may be registered with only ONE licensed estate agency at any one time, and must not engage in moneylending or unauthorised moonlighting
- D. An RES may freely act as a moneylender on the side as long as commission income is declared

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(easy)_
>
> The single-agency rule means an RES can be registered with only one licensed EA at a time, and RESs are prohibited from moneylending and from being connected to a licensed moneylender. C is correct. B violates the single-agency rule. A is wrong: an RES must be attached to a licensed EA to practise. D is wrong: moneylending involvement is prohibited regardless of declaration. 中文一句话: 单一公司原则：经纪同一时间只能挂靠一家持牌公司，且禁止放贷及违规兼职。
>
> 📎 Source: Estate Agents Act 2010; CEA RES registration rules

---


## P1.2 Code of Ethics & Professional Client Care (CEPCC) + Code of Practice

**Q1.** Under what instrument is the Code of Ethics & Professional Client Care (CEPCC) prescribed, and to whom does it primarily apply?

- A. Prescribed under the Estate Agents (Dispute Resolution Schemes) Regulations 2011; it applies only when a dispute has been filed
- B. Prescribed directly in the Estate Agents Act 2010 main body; it applies only to Key Executive Officers (KEOs)
- C. Prescribed under the Land Titles Act 1993; it applies to conveyancing lawyers
- D. Prescribed under the Estate Agents (Estate Agency Work) Regulations 2010; it sets the standard of conduct for individual salespersons (RES) and EAs toward clients and the public

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(easy)_
>
> The CEPCC is prescribed under the Estate Agents (Estate Agency Work) Regulations 2010 and sets the conduct standard owed by EAs and RESs to clients and the public; breach leads to disciplinary action. B is wrong because the CEPCC sits in subsidiary regulations, not the Act's main body, and binds all RES/EAs, not only KEOs. C is wrong - that is land law, unrelated. A confuses CEPCC with the Dispute Resolution Schemes Regulations. 中文：CEPCC 由《地产代理(地产代理工作)条例 2010》规定，约束 EA 与 RES 对客户及公众的行为。
>
> 📎 Source: EA (Estate Agency Work) Regulations 2010 (CEPCC); CEA

---

**Q2.** The Code of Practice for Estate Agents (COPEA) is a firm-level code. Which of the following is NOT one of the matters it governs?

- A. Setting the maximum commission rate that an EA may charge a client
- B. Management and supervision of salespersons by the EA
- C. Procedures for handling claims and complaints
- D. Retention of documents and records

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> COPEA (Second Schedule, EAW Regulations 2010) covers firm-level areas such as management & supervision, the Estate Agent Card, claims/complaints procedures, and document/record retention. It does NOT fix commission - commission is fully negotiable and not regulated by CEA, so A is the correct 'NOT' answer. B, C and D are genuine COPEA areas. 中文：COPEA 管的是管理监督、代理卡、投诉处理、文件保存；佣金不受规定，故 A 不属于。
>
> 📎 Source: COPEA, Second Schedule, EAW Regulations 2010; CEA

---

**Q3.** Under COPEA Para 7(1), for how long must an EA retain transaction documents and records, and why was the period set at that figure?

- A. 3 years, the original period that remains unchanged
- B. 5 years, to align with AML/CFT customer due diligence record-keeping requirements
- C. 7 years, to match the Companies Act audit retention rule
- D. 2 years, matching the validity of an RES exam pass

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> COPEA Para 7(1) requires retention of transaction documents and records for at least 5 years, aligning with AML/CFT (CDD) record-keeping obligations, and electronic records are acceptable. A is the outdated 3-year figure (a classic trap). C (7 years) and D (2 years - exam-pass/Cert validity) are unrelated. 中文：COPEA 第7(1)条要求文件保存至少 5 年，与反洗钱记录要求一致。
>
> 📎 Source: COPEA Para 7(1); AML/CFT record-retention 5 years; CEA

---

**Q4.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: RES Alvin is appointed by a seller to market a condominium. A buyer, who has no agent, approaches Alvin directly and asks Alvin to also act for him and collect a fee from him for the same unit. Alvin agrees and collects commission from both the seller and the buyer. Which statement BEST describes Alvin's position?

- A. This is permitted as long as Alvin verbally tells both parties he is acting for both
- B. This is permitted because the buyer is unrepresented, so Alvin is simply filling a gap and providing a service
- C. Alvin has committed dual representation, which is an offence - he cannot collect a fee from both parties to the same transaction
- D. It is only a problem if the two fees together exceed the prescribed commission cap

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> Dual representation - one RES collecting or sharing fees from BOTH sides of the same transaction - is prohibited and is a criminal offence (a former salesperson drew a $9,000 fine in a CEA case; the statutory maximum is a fine up to $25,000 and/or imprisonment up to 12 months). So C is correct. B is wrong: the prohibition applies regardless of whether the other side is unrepresented. A is wrong because verbal disclosure does not cure an outright prohibited act. D is wrong - there is no commission cap; commission is negotiable. 中文：双重代理属违法，Alvin 不能同时向买卖双方收费，无论买方是否有代理。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA dual representation prohibition; max penalty $25,000/12 months; $9,000 case

---

**Q5.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Two salespersons, Beng and Cara, both registered with the SAME estate agency, end up on opposite sides of one resale transaction - Beng represents the seller and Cara the buyer. Each collects a fee only from their own client. What must they do for this to be compliant, and is it dual representation?

- A. It is permitted only if the KEO collects the commission centrally and both salespersons forgo their share
- B. It is automatically dual representation because they share the same EA, so the transaction must be aborted
- C. Nothing is required - being from the same EA carries no conflict-of-interest obligation
- D. It is NOT dual representation; but each must declare in writing that they are from the same EA and obtain the written consent of their respective clients

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> Two RES from the same EA on opposite sides is NOT dual representation, provided neither collects/shares a fee from both sides; however, each must declare in writing that they are from the same EA and obtain written client consent (managing the conflict of interest). D is correct. B is wrong - same-EA opposite-side dealing is allowed with safeguards. C is wrong because written disclosure and consent ARE required. D invents a requirement that does not exist. 中文：同一 EA 两名 RES 各代表一方且各自收费，不算双重代理，但须书面披露并取得客户书面同意。
>
> 📎 Source: CEPCC conflict-of-interest / same-EA disclosure rules; CEA

---

**Q6.** From 1 January 2026, what are the Continuing Professional Development (CPD) requirements for an RES under Project ADEPT?

- A. 16 training hours/year = 12h Structured Learning (incl. at least 4h Prescribed Essentials) + 4h Self-Directed Learning, on a Jan-Dec cycle
- B. 6 CPD credits/year on an Oct-Sep cycle, unchanged from 2025
- C. 10 training hours/year, all of which must be Prescribed Essentials
- D. 16 training hours/year, all of which must be Structured Learning, with no Self-Directed component

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> From 1 Jan 2026 (Project ADEPT) the requirement is 16 hours/year = 12h Structured Learning (with at least 4h Prescribed Essentials) + 4h Self-Directed Learning, on a calendar-year (Jan-Dec) cycle. A is correct. B describes the outgoing framework (6 credits, Oct-Sep). C and D misstate the split - there IS a 4h SDL component and Prescribed Essentials is only part of Structured Learning. 中文：2026 起 CPD 为每年 16 小时＝12 结构化学习（含至少4 必修）＋4 自主学习，按日历年计。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA CPD 2026 (Project ADEPT) - cea.gov.sg CPD framework

---

**Q7.** For the 2026 CPD cycle, which topic is the specified Prescribed Essential (PE), and what is the consequence of failing to meet CPD requirements?

- A. Conveyancing procedure; failure results in an automatic $5,000 fine
- B. PMLPFTF (prevention of money laundering, proliferation financing and terrorism financing); failing CPD jeopardises the RES's annual registration renewal
- C. Ethnic Integration Policy; failure results in immediate revocation of the EA licence
- D. Property tax computation; failure has no consequence as CPD is voluntary

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> The 2026 specific Prescribed Essential topic is PMLPFTF (Prevention of Money Laundering, Proliferation Financing and Terrorism Financing), and CPD compliance is a condition of the RES's annual registration renewal. B is correct. A and C invent penalties/topics - non-compliance affects renewal, not an automatic fine or revocation, and the PE topic is AML-related, not conveyancing/EIP. D is wrong because CPD is mandatory. 中文：2026 必修主题为反洗钱(PMLPFTF)；未达 CPD 影响年度注册续期。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA CPD 2026 - PE topic PMLPFTF; renewal condition

---

**Q8.** A complainant lost $8,000 because of an RES's misconduct and wants both the RES disciplined AND his money recovered. What is the correct understanding of CEA's role?

- A. CEA cannot act at all because the loss is under $20,000
- B. CEA will both discipline the RES and order the RES to refund the $8,000 directly to the complainant
- C. CEA handles discipline and conduct but does NOT recover money for consumers; the complainant must pursue recovery via mediation/adjudication or the Small Claims Tribunals
- D. Only the Disciplinary Committee can order a refund, after which CEA disburses the money

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> CEA regulates conduct and imposes disciplinary penalties (paid to the State, not the consumer); it does NOT recover money for consumers. To recover his loss the consumer uses the CEA Dispute Resolution Scheme (mediation/adjudication) or the Small Claims Tribunals (claims up to $20,000, or up to $30,000 by mutual consent via a Memorandum of Consent). C is correct. B and D wrongly assume CEA/DC refunds money. A is wrong - CEA can still discipline regardless of amount. 中文：CEA 负责纪律处分但不替消费者追讨金钱；追款须经调解/仲裁或小额索偿庭（上限 $20,000，双方同意可至 $30,000）。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA dispute resolution; Small Claims Tribunals $20,000/$30,000 (judiciary.gov.sg)

---

**Q9.** Following a disciplinary inquiry, what is the maximum financial penalty a Disciplinary Committee (DC) may impose on an individual RES for a (non-AML) breach, and what is the appeal route?

- A. Up to $25,000 per case; appeal to the Strata Titles Board within 21 days
- B. Up to $200,000 per case; appeal to the High Court within 30 days
- C. Up to $5,000 per case; appeal to CEA's CEO within 7 days
- D. Up to $100,000 per case; appeal to the MND Appeals Board within 14 days

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> A DC may impose a financial penalty up to $100,000 on an RES for non-AML breaches (and up to $200,000 on an EA), and the appeal lies to the Ministry of National Development (MND) Appeals Board within 14 days of being notified of the decision. D is correct. B swaps in the EA cap ($200,000) and a wrong appeal route. C describes the Letter of Censure ceiling ($5,000), not a DC penalty. D borrows the criminal dual-rep figure ($25,000) and the wrong tribunal. 中文：DC 对 RES 最高罚 $100,000，可于 14 天内向 MND 上诉委员会上诉。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA disciplinary proceedings; DC RES $100,000 / EA $200,000; MND Appeals Board 14 days

---

**Q10.** The Letter of Censure (LOC) framework is used for less serious, non-criminal breaches. What is its maximum quantum, and where does it sit in the enforcement ladder?

- A. Max $5,000 (per case generally; per breach for AML matters on/after 1 Jul 2025); the ladder runs Letter of Warning then Letter of Censure then Disciplinary Committee
- B. Max $100,000 per case; it is the most severe sanction available, above the Disciplinary Committee
- C. Max $5,000 but only for KEOs; salespersons cannot receive an LOC
- D. Max $25,000; it is issued only by the courts after criminal conviction

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> The LOC carries a maximum of $5,000 - per case generally, but assessable per breach for AML matters on/after 1 Jul 2025 - and sits between a Letter of Warning and a Disciplinary Committee referral. A is correct. B overstates the LOC as the top sanction (the DC is more severe, up to $100k/$200k). C wrongly limits LOCs to KEOs (they apply to both RES and EAs). D confuses it with criminal court penalties. 中文：LOC 上限 $5,000（一般按案，反洗钱按违规计），在执法阶梯中位于警告信与纪律委员会之间。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA Letter of Censure framework; LOC $5,000; cea.gov.sg

---

**Q11.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: RES Dawn is told by her seller-client that the unit has serious water-seepage problems. A prospective buyer asks Dawn directly whether there are any known defects. Dawn says 'No, none that I'm aware of' to help close the sale. The seller had also asked Dawn to keep the seepage 'confidential'. Under the CEPCC, what is the BEST description of Dawn's conduct?

- A. Dawn acted correctly because her overriding duty of confidentiality to her client requires her to conceal the defect
- B. Dawn has breached her duties - confidentiality does not extend to making false or misleading statements; she must not actively misrepresent material facts to the public
- C. Dawn acted correctly because the buyer should have engaged his own agent and inspected (caveat emptor absolves her)
- D. Dawn's only error was failing to put the denial in writing; a written denial would have been acceptable

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> Under the CEPCC, an RES must not make false or misleading statements and must deal fairly with the public; client confidentiality cannot be used as a shield to actively misrepresent a material fact she actually knows. B is correct. B misuses confidentiality - it never licenses misrepresentation. C misapplies caveat emptor - it does not permit the agent to lie. D is wrong - the medium (oral vs written) does not cure a false statement. 中文：保密义务不能用来作虚假陈述；Dawn 明知漏水却否认，违反 CEPCC 对公众诚信义务。
>
> 📎 Source: CEPCC duties to public / no false or misleading statements; CEA

---

**Q12.** An RES is asked to explain a tenancy agreement to a tenant whose first language is not English, and the tenant clearly does not understand the English document. Under the CEPCC, what is the RES's obligation?

- A. Refuse to deal with any client who cannot read English
- B. Proceed to obtain the signature quickly, since the signed document is binding regardless of comprehension
- C. Ensure the contents are accurately explained/translated so the client understands before signing; the RES must not procure a signature on a document the client does not understand
- D. Tell the tenant to sign first and seek a translation afterward at the tenant's own cost

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> The CEPCC requires that documents be accurately explained/translated so the client understands, and an RES must not procure execution of a document the client does not comprehend. C is correct. B ignores the comprehension duty. A is discriminatory and unnecessary - the duty is to explain/translate, not refuse service. D reverses the proper sequence (understanding must precede signature). 中文：CEPCC 要求确保客户在签字前理解文件内容（必要时翻译），不得让客户签署其不理解的文件。
>
> 📎 Source: CEPCC translation / document execution duties; CEA

---

**Q13.** An RES will receive an 'overriding' commission (an extra cut routed through a sub-arrangement) on a deal in addition to her normal commission. Under the CEPCC's conflict-of-interest provisions, what must she do?

- A. Decline the overriding fee, because accepting any second fee is automatically dual representation
- B. Nothing - overriding commissions are an internal matter between agents and need not be disclosed
- C. Obtain CEA's prior written approval before accepting any overriding fee
- D. Disclose the overriding fee in writing as a potential conflict of interest to the affected client

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> Under the CEPCC, overriding/additional fees that could create a conflict of interest must be disclosed in writing to the affected client. D is correct. B is wrong - non-disclosure of a conflicting interest breaches the Code. C invents a CEA pre-approval step that does not exist. A wrongly equates an overriding fee with dual representation (dual rep is collecting/sharing a fee from both sides of one transaction). 中文：取得额外/超额佣金须主动书面向相关客户披露为潜在利益冲突。
>
> 📎 Source: CEPCC conflict-of-interest disclosure; CEA

---

**Q14.** Which statement correctly distinguishes the CEPCC from the COPEA?

- A. CEPCC sets the standard of conduct (ethics/client care) chiefly at the individual salesperson and EA level; COPEA is the firm-level code on management, supervision, records and complaints
- B. CEPCC is firm-level only; COPEA governs individual salesperson ethics
- C. Both apply only to KEOs and not to ordinary salespersons
- D. CEPCC governs commission rates; COPEA governs advertising content

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> The CEPCC is the conduct/ethics and client-care code applying to RES and EAs; the COPEA is the firm-level Code of Practice addressing management & supervision, the EA Card, complaints procedures and record retention. A is correct. B reverses the two. C is wrong - both bind salespersons. D mis-assigns content (neither sets commission rates). 中文：CEPCC 为个人/EA 的行为操守守则；COPEA 为公司层面的执业守则。
>
> 📎 Source: CEPCC & COPEA, EAW Regulations 2010; CEA

---

**Q15.** Several penalty figures appear in CEA's framework. Which pairing of breach type to its correct maximum is accurate?

- A. Letter of Censure (general): up to $100,000 per case
- B. Dual representation (criminal prosecution): fine up to $25,000 and/or imprisonment up to 12 months
- C. Disciplinary Committee penalty on an EA: up to $5,000 per case
- D. Disciplinary Committee penalty on an EA: up to $25,000 per case

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> Dual representation is a criminal offence carrying a fine of up to $25,000 and/or imprisonment up to 12 months, so B is correct. A is wrong - the Letter of Censure ceiling is $5,000, not $100,000. C and D are wrong - a Disciplinary Committee may fine an EA up to $200,000 (and an RES up to $100,000), not $5,000 or $25,000. 中文：双重代理为刑事罪，可罚款至 $25,000 及/或监禁 12 个月；LOC 上限 $5,000，DC 对 EA 最高 $200,000。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA penalties - dual rep $25,000/12mo; LOC $5,000; DC EA $200,000 / RES $100,000

---


## P1.3 Licensing, Registration, CPD, Disciplinary Action & Dispute Resolution

**Q1.** Mei Ling has just passed her RES examination and wants to start practising. Which statement BEST describes the correct licensing/registration structure she must operate under?

- A. She applies directly to CEA for her own personal RES licence and may then work independently for any agency
- B. She must first obtain an EA licence before she can be registered as an RES
- C. She must be registered as an RES through a single licensed estate agent (EA), as the EA is licensed while the salesperson is registered
- D. She may register with up to two licensed EAs at the same time to maximise her listings

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(easy)_
>
> Under the Estate Agents Act 2010, the firm (EA) is LICENSED while the individual salesperson (RES) is REGISTERED, and the RES must be registered through a licensed EA. The single-agency rule limits an RES to exactly one EA at any time. A is wrong: an RES is registered (not 'licensed') and cannot work independently outside an EA. B is wrong: an RES does not need an EA licence (that is the firm-level licence). D is wrong: the single-agency rule prohibits registering with two EAs concurrently. 中文一句：行号(EA)是被'发牌'，经纪(RES)是通过一家持牌行号'注册'，且只能挂靠一家(single-agency rule)。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – Estate Agents Act 2010; single-agency rule

---

**Q2.** Under the CPD framework taking effect 1 January 2026 (Project ADEPT), what is the correct annual training requirement for a practising RES?

- A. 6 CPD credits over an October–September cycle, all from professional competency courses
- B. 10 training hours = 6h Structured Learning + 4h Self-Directed Learning, over a January–December cycle
- C. 16 training hours all of which must be Structured Learning, with no Self-Directed component permitted
- D. 16 training hours = 12h Structured Learning (including at least 4h Prescribed Essentials) + 4h Self-Directed Learning, over a January–December cycle

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> From 1 Jan 2026 the requirement is 16 training hours per year: 12h Structured Learning (with ≥4h Prescribed Essentials forming part of the SL component) + 4h Self-Directed Learning, on a Jan–Dec cycle. A describes the OUTGOING regime (6 credits, Oct–Sep). C is wrong because 4h must be Self-Directed Learning. D understates the totals (16h total, 12h SL). 中文一句：2026年起每年16小时 = 12小时结构化学习(含≥4小时必修Prescribed Essentials) + 4小时自主学习，周期改为1–12月。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – Transforming Your CPD Journey: Key Changes from 2026

---

**Q3.** Kumar, a registered RES, is found by a CEA Disciplinary Committee (DC) to have committed a serious (non-AML) breach of the CEPCC. What is the MAXIMUM financial penalty the DC may impose on him for this case?

- A. $100,000
- B. $50,000
- C. $5,000
- D. $200,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> A Disciplinary Committee may impose a financial penalty of up to $100,000 on an individual RES (and up to $200,000 on an EA firm). A ($5,000) is the cap under the Letter of Censure framework for LESS serious breaches, not the DC. B ($50,000) is a distractor with no statutory basis. D ($200,000) is the maximum for an EA firm, not an individual RES. 中文一句：纪律委员会(DC)对个人经纪RES最高罚款$100,000；行号EA最高$200,000；而$5,000是较轻违规的Letter of Censure上限。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – Disciplinary proceedings (serious breaches)

---

**Q4.** A consumer is unhappy that an RES allegedly overcharged commission and wants the money returned. He calls CEA expecting CEA to order a refund. Which statement is CORRECT about CEA's role?

- A. CEA will adjudicate the dispute and directly order the RES to refund the consumer's money
- B. CEA handles disciplinary action against the RES but does NOT recover or refund money for consumers; monetary recovery is via mediation/adjudication or the courts
- C. CEA has no role at all and the consumer must go straight to the Small Claims Tribunals
- D. CEA will deduct the disputed sum from the RES's commission and pay it to the consumer

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> CEA regulates conduct and takes disciplinary action, but it does NOT recover or refund money to consumers. Monetary recovery is pursued through the CEA Dispute Resolution Scheme (mediation/adjudication) or through the courts/Small Claims Tribunals. A and D are wrong: CEA cannot order or arrange a refund/garnish commission. C is wrong: CEA does have a regulatory/disciplinary role and offers a dispute resolution scheme, so the consumer is not limited to SCT only. 中文一句：CEA只负责纪律处分，不替消费者追讨/退款；金钱争议须经调解/仲裁或小额索偿庭(SCT)解决。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – Complaints & Dispute Resolution Scheme (Regs 2011)

---

**Q5.** A buyer and seller agree to bring a $9,000 commission dispute to the Small Claims Tribunals (SCT). The claim amount is below the standard SCT limit. Up to what amount can the SCT hear a claim WITHOUT both parties' consent, and what is the raised limit WITH written consent of both parties?

- A. Standard limit $5,000; with consent up to $10,000
- B. Standard limit $10,000; with written consent of both parties up to $20,000
- C. Standard limit $20,000; with written consent of both parties up to $30,000
- D. Standard limit $30,000; with consent up to $60,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> The Small Claims Tribunals hear claims up to $20,000 as standard, raised to up to $30,000 if both parties file a Memorandum of Consent (written consent). The $9,000 dispute is well within the standard limit. A and B understate the limits (the standard is $20,000, not $5,000 or $10,000; the raised ceiling is $30,000, not $20,000). D overstates both figures. 中文一句：小额索偿庭标准上限$20,000；双方书面同意(Memorandum of Consent)可提高至$30,000。
>
> 📎 Source: State Courts of Singapore – Small Claims Tribunals jurisdictional limits ($20,000 / $30,000 with consent)

---

**Q6.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: RES Daniel represents the SELLER of a condo. RES Priya, from the SAME estate agency as Daniel, represents the BUYER. Each collects commission only from his/her own client. Separately, RES Wei (from a different agency) personally collects commission from BOTH the seller and the buyer in another transaction. Which statement BEST describes the regulatory position?

- A. Both situations are dual representation offences because two opposing parties are involved in each
- B. Daniel and Priya have committed dual representation, but Wei has not because he is a single agent handling one deal
- C. Neither situation is a problem because commission arrangements are entirely up to the agents
- D. Daniel and Priya are NOT dual representation provided each collects only from their own side and both make written disclosure of being from the same EA with written consent; Wei has committed the offence of dual representation

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> Two RES from the SAME EA acting on opposite sides is NOT dual representation, provided neither collects from both sides and both declare in writing they are from the same EA and obtain written consent. Dual representation (an offence) is ONE RES collecting/sharing fees from BOTH sides of the same transaction — exactly what Wei did. A wrongly treats Daniel/Priya as an offence. C ignores that dual representation is a prohibited offence. B inverts the rule: Wei is the offender, not Daniel/Priya. 中文一句：同一行号两名经纪各收各方佣金并书面披露+取得同意，不算双重代理；同一经纪向买卖双方收佣(Wei)才是违法的双重代理。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – Conflict of Interest & Dual Representation rules

---

**Q7.** Following the operationalisation of the AML and Other Matters (Estate Agents and Developers) Act 2025 on 1 July 2025, how are the maximum penalties for AML-related disciplinary breaches now calculated, compared with other (non-AML) breaches?

- A. For AML breaches the maximum penalties (e.g. $5,000 under LOC; $100,000 RES / $200,000 EA at DC) are imposed PER BREACH, whereas for other breaches the equivalent caps generally apply per case
- B. AML penalties are capped per case, identical to non-AML breaches
- C. AML breaches can only ever be dealt with by the Disciplinary Committee, never by Letter of Censure
- D. The Act lowered all AML penalty caps to encourage voluntary disclosure

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> The 2025 Act strengthened AML/CFT enforcement: for AML-related breaches committed on or after 1 July 2025 the caps apply PER BREACH (LOC up to $5,000 per breach; DC up to $100,000 for an RES and $200,000 for an EA per breach), while for other breaches the equivalent caps generally apply per case. B is wrong: AML is per breach, not per case. C is wrong: AML breaches can still be handled under the LOC framework (per-breach $5,000). D is the opposite of the truth — the Act raised maximum penalties. 中文一句：2025年AML法案使反洗钱违规按'每项违规'计罚(LOC每项$5,000；DC经纪$100,000、行号$200,000)，其他违规一般按'每宗案件'计。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – AML and Other Matters Act 2025 (operative 1 Jul 2025)

---

**Q8.** Which body administers the RES examination and handles registration logistics, and which statutory board regulates the industry under the Estate Agents Act?

- A. CEA administers the exam directly; HDB regulates the industry
- B. NTUC LearningHub administers the exam; CEA, a statutory board under MND, regulates the industry
- C. MAS administers the exam; CEA regulates the industry under MAS
- D. SLA administers the exam; URA regulates the industry

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> NTUC LearningHub administers the RES examination, while CEA — a statutory board under the Ministry of National Development (MND) — regulates the estate agency industry under the Estate Agents Act 2010. A is wrong: HDB does not regulate the industry. C is wrong: CEA sits under MND, not MAS, and MAS does not run the RES exam. D is wrong: SLA/URA are land/planning authorities, not the exam administrator/industry regulator. 中文一句：RES考试由NTUC LearningHub承办；CEA(隶属国家发展部MND)依据《地产代理法》监管行业。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – Prepare for the RES Examination; NTUC LearningHub

---

**Q9.** Aspiring agent Farah passed the RES exam on 1 March 2025 but has not yet registered with any EA. She finally decides to register in May 2026. What is the position regarding the validity of her exam pass?

- A. There is no time limit; she can register at any time using her March 2025 pass
- B. Her pass expired after 6 months and she must immediately re-sit the exam only
- C. She must register as an RES through a licensed EA within 2 years of passing, otherwise she must retake both the course and the exam
- D. Her pass is valid for 5 years from the date of passing

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> An exam pass is valid for RES registration for 2 years; the candidate must register as an RES via a licensed EA within 2 years of passing, failing which they must retake BOTH the course and the exam. Farah passed in March 2025, so registering in May 2026 is still within the 2-year window — valid. A is wrong because there IS a 2-year limit. B is wrong (no 6-month rule; lapsing requires retaking course + exam, not exam only). D wrongly cites 5 years. 中文一句：考试通过后须在2年内透过持牌行号注册，否则要重考课程+考试；不是无限期，也不是5年。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – Real estate salesperson examination results and appeals (register within 2 years)

---

**Q10.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: An RES, Jason, is served with a Statement of Case by CEA alleging a serious breach. He wants to know the procedural timeline. Which sequence and timeframe is CORRECT?

- A. Statement of Case → Admission/Defence within 7 days → straight to hearing; appeal to the High Court within 7 days
- B. Statement of Case → immediate revocation with no right of reply; appeal to the Minister within 60 days
- C. Statement of Case → respondent has 30 days to reply → hearing; appeal to CEA itself within 30 days
- D. Statement of Case → Admission/Defence within 14 days → Reply (14d) → Rejoinder (14d) → hearing → sentencing; appeal to the MND Appeals Board within 14 days

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> The DC process runs: Statement of Case → respondent's Admission/Defence within 14 days → Reply (14 days) → Rejoinder (14 days) → hearing → sentencing, with appeal to the MND Appeals Board within 14 days. A is wrong on every timeframe (14 days, not 7) and on the appeal venue (Appeals Board, not High Court directly). C is wrong: pleadings are 14 days each and appeal is to the MND Appeals Board, not to CEA. B is wrong: there is a full right of reply, not immediate revocation. 中文一句：纪律程序各阶段抗辩/答复/再答复均为14天，听证后判罚，再于14天内向MND上诉委员会上诉。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – Disciplinary process and appeal to MND Appeals Board

---

**Q11.** What is the pass mark for each paper of the RES examination, and what does the commonly-cited '75%' figure actually refer to?

- A. Pass mark is 60% (60/100) per paper, subject to review by CEA; the 75% figure refers to the RES course attendance requirement
- B. Pass mark is 75% per paper; 60% refers to course attendance
- C. Pass mark is 50% per paper; 75% is the overall combined-paper requirement
- D. Pass mark is 60% averaged across both papers combined; 75% is the minimum for one paper

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> Each paper is passed independently at 60/100 (60%), subject to review by CEA. The 75% figure is a classic exam trap — it refers to the minimum RES COURSE ATTENDANCE rate required to obtain the Certificate of RES Course Completion, not the exam pass mark. A swaps the two figures. C is wrong (pass mark is 60%, not 50%; there is no 75% combined requirement). D is wrong: each paper is passed independently, not averaged. 中文一句：每份考卷独立及格线为60%(60/100)；75%是RES课程出席率要求，不是考试及格分数。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – Prepare for the RES Examination (pass mark 60; 75% attendance)

---

**Q12.** A candidate sat both papers but failed Paper 2 while passing Paper 1. He wants to re-sit only Paper 2. Which statement BEST reflects the RES exam structure relevant to his situation?

- A. A fail in either paper voids both passes, so he must re-sit both Paper 1 and Paper 2
- B. Each paper must be passed independently, so he may do a modular re-sit of only Paper 2 while retaining his Paper 1 pass
- C. He cannot re-sit; he must retake the entire RES course before any re-sit
- D. He must wait two full years before any re-sit is permitted

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> Each paper is passed independently, so a candidate who passes Paper 1 but fails Paper 2 may do a modular re-sit of only Paper 2 (a modular sitting fee applies) while keeping the Paper 1 pass, provided he passes the remaining paper within 2 years of his course completion. A is wrong: passing one paper is not voided by failing the other. C is wrong: re-sitting a single paper does not require retaking the whole course. D is wrong: there is no mandatory 2-year wait to re-sit. 中文一句：两份考卷各自独立及格，可只补考(modular re-sit)未过的Paper 2，保留已过的Paper 1。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – RES exam format (modular sitting; each paper passed independently)

---

**Q13.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Senior agent Lim wants to be appointed as a Key Executive Officer (KEO) of a new estate agency. Which set of requirements must he satisfy?

- A. ≥21 years old; at least 1 year as a salesperson; 10 transactions in the past year; he may remain a registered RES of another EA concurrently
- B. Any age; 5 years experience; no transaction record needed; may concurrently run his own separate agency
- C. ≥21 years old; at least 3 years as a salesperson; at least 30 transactions in the past 3 years (with ≥10 private and ≥10 HDB); valid REA exam pass; fit-and-proper; and he cannot concurrently be an RES, sole proprietor or director of another EA
- D. ≥35 years old; 3 years experience; 50 transactions in the past year; no exam required

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> KEO eligibility: ≥21 years; ≥3 years estate agency experience (e.g. as a registered salesperson); ≥30 transactions in the past 3 years (≥10 private and ≥10 HDB); a valid REA exam pass obtained within the preceding 2 years; fit-and-proper; and the KEO cannot concurrently be an RES, sole proprietor or director of another EA. A understates experience/transactions and wrongly permits concurrent RES status. B is wrong on every count (age/experience/transactions/exam and the concurrency bar). D invents an age-35 rule and a 50-transaction figure, and wrongly drops the exam requirement. 中文一句：KEO须≥21岁、≥3年资历、近3年≥30宗(私宅≥10、组屋≥10)、通过REA考试、品行端正，且不得同时是另一行号的RES/独资人/董事。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – KEO eligibility criteria

---

**Q14.** Which dispute resolution mechanisms are offered under the CEA Dispute Resolution Scheme (Estate Agents (Dispute Resolution Schemes) Regulations 2011)?

- A. Only litigation in the State Courts
- B. A CEA-run tribunal that issues criminal convictions
- C. Only binding arbitration with no mediation option
- D. Mediation (e.g. via the Singapore Mediation Centre) and adjudication/arbitration

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(easy)_
>
> The CEA Dispute Resolution Scheme provides mediation (e.g. via the Singapore Mediation Centre) and adjudication/arbitration. A is wrong: the scheme is precisely an alternative to court litigation. C is wrong: mediation is offered, not just arbitration. B is wrong: the scheme resolves civil disputes; it does not issue criminal convictions (disciplinary/criminal matters are handled separately). 中文一句：CEA争议解决机制提供调解(经新加坡调解中心)与裁定/仲裁，并非只有诉讼或刑事定罪。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – Estate Agents (Dispute Resolution Schemes) Regulations 2011

---

**Q15.** An RES is found to have committed a LESS serious, non-criminal breach that CEA decides to handle without a full Disciplinary Committee hearing. Under the Letter of Censure (LOC) framework, what is the maximum financial penalty, and where does the LOC sit in the enforcement ladder?

- A. Maximum $5,000 (per case for general breaches, or per breach for AML matters on/after 1 Jul 2025); the LOC sits between a Letter of Warning (LOW) and the Disciplinary Committee (DC)
- B. Maximum $100,000; the LOC sits above the Disciplinary Committee in severity
- C. Maximum $20,000; the LOC replaces the DC entirely for all breaches
- D. Maximum $50,000; the LOC is issued only by the MND Appeals Board

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> The LOC framework caps the financial penalty at $5,000 (per case for general breaches; per breach for AML matters on/after 1 Jul 2025) and sits in the ladder LOW → LOC → DC, used for less serious non-criminal breaches without a full DC hearing. B confuses the LOC cap with the DC's $100,000 individual cap and misorders the ladder. C overstates the cap and wrongly says LOC replaces the DC for all breaches (serious matters still go to the DC). D invents a $50,000 cap and wrongly attributes issuance to the Appeals Board. 中文一句：Letter of Censure(较轻违规)最高罚$5,000(一般按案件、AML按每项违规)，位于LOW→LOC→DC处分阶梯之中。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – Letter of Censure framework

---

**Q16.** A newly registered RES, Aisha, joins her EA in February 2026. She is anxious about meeting the full 16-hour CPD requirement in her first year. Which statement is CORRECT?

- A. A new RES must complete double the CPD (32 hours) in their first year as a probation measure
- B. A new RES is exempt from CPD in their first registration cycle, but CPD compliance becomes a condition of annual registration renewal thereafter
- C. CPD is voluntary for all RES and never affects registration renewal
- D. A new RES must complete only the 4h Self-Directed Learning in their first year and nothing else

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> Under the 2026 framework a new RES is exempt from CPD in their first registration cycle; thereafter CPD completion is a condition of annual registration renewal. A is wrong: there is no 32-hour probation requirement. C is wrong: CPD is mandatory (a renewal condition), not voluntary. D is wrong: the first-cycle position is full exemption, not a partial 4-hour requirement. 中文一句：新RES首个注册周期豁免CPD；之后完成CPD是每年注册续期的必要条件。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – CPD 2026 framework (new RES first-cycle exemption)

---


## P1.4 Basic Land Law: Estates & Interests in Land, Ownership & Co-ownership

**Q1.** Mr Tan owns a piece of land in fee simple. Which statement BEST describes the nature of his ownership?

- A. It is the largest leasehold estate, lasting 999 years
- B. It is a freehold estate but conditional, held subject to the State Lands Act
- C. It is a freehold estate of indefinite duration, unconditional and capable of being inherited
- D. It lasts only for his lifetime and reverts to the State on his death

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(easy)_
>
> Fee simple is the highest and most complete form of freehold ownership: indefinite in duration, unconditional, and inheritable. B describes an Estate in Perpetuity, which is freehold but conditional under the State Lands Act. A is wrong because 999-year is a leasehold (approximating freehold) but is still a fixed term, not fee simple. D describes a life estate, which ends on the holder's death. 中文: 永久产权（fee simple）是最高、无条件、可继承且无限期的产权；B是有条件的永久地契，C是租赁地契，D是终身产权。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK P1.10 Estates & Interests in Land

---

**Q2.** Ahmad and Siti hold their condominium as joint tenants. Ahmad dies, leaving a will that gives 'all my property' to his son. What happens to Ahmad's interest in the condominium?

- A. It passes to the State because joint tenancy interests cannot be inherited
- B. It passes to Ahmad's son under the will
- C. It is divided equally between Siti and Ahmad's son
- D. It passes automatically to Siti by the right of survivorship, regardless of the will

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(easy)_
>
> In a joint tenancy the right of survivorship (jus accrescendi) operates: on the death of one joint tenant, their interest passes automatically to the surviving joint tenant(s) and CANNOT be disposed of by will or intestacy. So Siti takes the whole. B is the trap that confuses joint tenancy with tenancy-in-common (where a share IS willable). C invents a split that has no legal basis. A is wrong because the interest does pass, just to the survivor not the State. 中文: 联权（JT）有生存者取得权，亡者份额自动归生存者，遗嘱无效；B误把JT当作分权共有（TIC）。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK P1.12 Co-ownership; Common Trap #4

---

**Q3.** Two business partners want to co-own a shophouse so that each can leave his distinct 60% and 40% share to his own family by will. Which form of co-ownership and which feature is correct?

- A. Tenancy-in-common, which allows unequal distinct shares with no right of survivorship
- B. Joint tenancy, because only joint tenancy permits unequal shares
- C. Tenancy-in-common, which requires all four unities (PITT)
- D. Joint tenancy, because the right of survivorship lets each leave his share by will

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> Tenancy-in-common (TIC) allows distinct, possibly unequal undivided shares (e.g. 60/40), has only the unity of possession, and has NO survivorship, so each share passes by will or intestacy - exactly what the partners want. B is wrong: joint tenancy requires equal undivided ownership (no distinct shares). C is wrong: the four unities (PITT) are required for joint tenancy, not TIC (TIC needs only unity of possession). D is self-contradictory: survivorship means a share canNOT be left by will. 中文: 想按不等份额且可遗赠，应选分权共有（TIC，仅需占有统一、无生存权）；JT需四统一且有生存权，无法遗赠。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK P1.12 Co-ownership

---

**Q4.** A buyer exercises an Option to Purchase on a private condominium and pays the deposit, but the seller has not yet executed the transfer for registration. What interest does the buyer hold at this point, and what may the buyer do to protect it?

- A. A legal interest, which is already enforceable against the whole world
- B. An equitable interest, which the buyer may protect by lodging a caveat
- C. No interest until completion, so a caveat cannot be lodged
- D. A statutory easement, registrable on the folio

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> On exercising the OTP / signing the S&P, the buyer acquires an EQUITABLE interest in the land (legal title vests only on registration of the transfer). This equitable interest is a caveatable interest, so the buyer lodges a caveat with SLA to warn third parties. A is wrong because legal title for Torrens land vests only on registration, not before. C is wrong because the equitable interest arises on exercise, which is precisely the basis for a caveat. D wrongly characterises a buyer's contractual interest as an easement. 中文: 行使OTP后买方取得衡平法权益，可登记契约（caveat）保护；法定产权须登记后才生效。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK P1.11 Legal vs Equitable Interest; P1.15 Caveats

---

**Q5.** A holds an unregistered equitable interest in a property. B, who knows nothing of A's interest, buys the same property for full market value and becomes the registered proprietor. Separately, C holds a registered legal interest in another plot. Which statement is correct?

- A. A's equitable interest survives against B because all interests bind a purchaser once value is paid
- B. Both A's equitable interest and C's legal interest are defeated by a bona fide purchaser
- C. A's equitable interest is defeated by B, a bona fide purchaser for value without notice, but a legal interest like C's is enforceable against the whole world
- D. C's legal interest can be defeated by a later purchaser without notice, but A's equitable interest cannot

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> An equitable interest is enforceable against everyone EXCEPT a bona fide purchaser for value without notice (the classic 'equity's darling'), so A loses to B. A legal interest is enforceable in rem - against the whole world - so C's interest survives. B is wrong because legal interests are not defeated this way. A inverts the rule (equitable interests are vulnerable, not bulletproof). D reverses the correct positions of legal vs equitable. 中文: 衡平法权益败给善意有偿无通知的买方，但法定权益对世人皆有效；B、A、D颠倒了两者的保护力。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK P1.11 Legal vs Equitable Interest; Common Trap #6

---

**Q6.** Under the Torrens system administered by SLA, which of the following BEST states the effect of section 46 LTA (indefeasibility) on a registered proprietor's title?

- A. It guarantees the title only after a 5-year period has elapsed from registration
- B. It is absolute and cannot be challenged on any ground whatsoever
- C. It only protects the proprietor against unregistered equitable interests, not against fraud
- D. It is generally conclusive but NOT absolute - fraud or forgery by the proprietor and certain statutory/overriding interests are exceptions

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> Indefeasibility under s46 LTA makes the register conclusive evidence of title, but it is NOT absolute: the key exceptions are fraud or forgery by the registered proprietor or their agent, plus statutory/overriding interests. B overstates it as absolute. C is wrong - fraud is precisely the main exception, and indefeasibility does protect against most unregistered claims. D invents a non-existent 5-year waiting period (the 5 years relates to caveat validity, a distractor trap). 中文: s46赋予登记产权'不可推翻'但非绝对，欺诈/伪造及法定优先权益为例外；并无5年等待期。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK P1.13 Land Titles Act / Torrens; verified via SSO LTA

---

**Q7.** A buyer lodged a caveat over a property. The seller later attempts a dealing inconsistent with the caveat, and SLA serves the caveator a notice under s127 LTA. To keep the caveat alive, what must the caveator do, and what is the correct timeframe?

- A. Obtain a court order supporting the caveat within 30 days, or the caveat lapses
- B. Renew the caveat within 5 years, after which it lapses automatically
- C. Do nothing, because the Registrar cannot act against a lodged caveat
- D. Pay compensation to the seller within 14 days under s128

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(hard)_
>
> When an inconsistent dealing is presented, SLA serves the caveator a notice; under s127 the caveator must obtain a court order to maintain the caveat within 30 days of service, failing which the caveat lapses. B confuses the s127 lapsing notice with the general 5-year validity period (extendable) - that is separate. C is wrong: although the Registrar cannot remove a caveat purely on its own motion, the lapsing-on-notice mechanism still defeats an inactive caveator. D misapplies s128, which concerns compensation payable BY a person who wrongfully lodges a caveat, not a payment to keep it alive. 中文: 收到s127通知后须在30天内取得法院命令，否则失效；5年是一般有效期，s128是错误登记的赔偿。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK P1.15 Caveats (s127, s128); verified via SSO LTA

---

**Q8.** A foreign person (not an SC or SPR with special approval) wishes to acquire residential property in Singapore. WITHOUT any LDAU approval, which of the following may the foreigner legally purchase?

- A. A semi-detached landed house on freehold land
- B. A condominium unit (strata) in a private development
- C. A bungalow in Sentosa Cove
- D. Vacant residential land for self-build

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> Under the Residential Property Act, a strata condominium unit is NON-restricted property that a foreigner may buy without LDAU approval. B (semi-detached/landed), C (Sentosa Cove landed) and D (vacant residential land) are all RESTRICTED property requiring LDAU approval. (Note: Sentosa Cove landed has a faster-track LDAU scheme but still requires approval, so it remains restricted.) 中文: 外国人无须批准可购买公寓单位（非限制类）；半独立式洋房、圣淘沙湾洋房、空置住宅地皆为限制类需LDAU批准。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK P1.19 Residential Property Act; Common Trap #7; verified via SLA Foreign Ownership of Property

---

**Q9.** A foreign investor wants to take a lease of a landed bungalow (a restricted property). For how long may he lease it WITHOUT needing LDAU approval?

- A. Any term, because leasing never requires approval - only purchase does
- B. A term not exceeding 30 years
- C. A term not exceeding 7 years, including any option for renewal
- D. A term not exceeding 99 years

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> Under the Residential Property Act, a foreign person may take a leasehold interest in restricted (landed) residential property for a term NOT exceeding 7 years (including any further term grantable by way of an option for renewal) without LDAU approval; a longer term requires approval. B (30 years) and D (99 years) exceed the threshold and would need approval. A is wrong: long leases of restricted property DO require approval. 中文: 外国人租赁限制类住宅，期限不超过7年（含续约选项）无须LDAU批准；超过则需批准。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK P1.19; verified via SLA Foreign Ownership of Property

---

**Q10.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Parkview Mansions is a private condominium that obtained its TOP exactly 9 years ago. A group of subsidiary proprietors wants to launch a collective (en bloc) sale. The Collective Sale Committee is formed and the Collective Sale Agreement (CSA) begins circulating for signature. What is the minimum consent threshold required for the en bloc to proceed?

- A. 80% of share value OR 80% of strata floor area, whichever is reached first
- B. 80% of both share value and strata floor area, because age is measured from the date of the first sale
- C. 90% of share value only, with no requirement as to strata floor area
- D. 90% of both share value AND total strata floor area, because the development is less than 10 years old

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> Under s84A of the Land Titles (Strata) Act, age is measured from the date of issue of the latest TOP (or CSC if no TOP). At 9 years the development is LESS than 10 years old, so the higher 90% threshold applies, and it must be met for BOTH share value AND total strata floor area. B uses the wrong age basis (first sale) and the wrong 80% figure. C drops the floor-area requirement (both metrics are needed). A wrongly uses 'OR' - both thresholds must be satisfied simultaneously, and at the wrong 80% level. 中文: 楼龄不足10年（按最新TOP计）须90%份值'与'楼面面积双双达标；本例9年用90%且需同时满足两项。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK P1.18 En Bloc / Collective Sale; verified via SSO LTSA s84A

---

**Q11.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY (cont. - Parkview Mansions): The CSA is now circulating. One owner, Mdm Lim, signs the agreement on Day 1. The committee struggles to gather the rest of the signatures. By when must the requisite majority consent be obtained from the date Mdm Lim (the first signatory) signed, and what cooling-off right does she have?

- A. Consent must be obtained within 12 months of the first signature; she has a 5-day cooling-off period to rescind her signature
- B. Consent must be obtained within 5 days; she has a 12-month cooling-off period
- C. Consent must be obtained within 24 months; she has a 14-day cooling-off period
- D. There is no time limit on consent collection, and there is no cooling-off right once signed

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(hard)_
>
> The requisite majority consent must be obtained within 12 months of the first signature on the CSA. Each signing owner also has a 5-day cooling-off period during which they may rescind their signature. B swaps the two periods. C uses the wrong figures (24 months / 14 days are distractors). D is wrong on both counts - there is both a 12-month window and a 5-day cooling-off right. 中文: 同意须在首签起12个月内取得；签署人有5天冷静期可撤销。B/C/D数字颠倒或错误。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK P1.18 En Bloc / Collective Sale; verified via LTSA

---

**Q12.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY (cont. - Parkview Mansions): The sale is not unanimous and an objecting owner challenges it at the Strata Titles Board (STB). On what basis must the STB be satisfied before approving the collective sale?

- A. That at least 50% of objectors withdraw their objections
- B. That the sale is in good faith and that no objector will suffer a financial loss
- C. That the sale price exceeds the URA Master Plan valuation by 20%
- D. That the Registrar has confirmed indefeasibility of all the strata titles

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> The STB must be satisfied that the transaction is in GOOD FAITH (assessed by the sale price, the method of distributing the proceeds, and the relationship between the purchaser and any subsidiary proprietor) and that no objecting owner will suffer a FINANCIAL LOSS. B invents a 50% withdrawal rule. C invents a Master Plan valuation benchmark. D confuses STB's en bloc function with the Torrens indefeasibility concept (s46 LTA), which is irrelevant here. 中文: STB须确信交易出于善意且反对者无财务损失；其余选项均为虚构标准。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK P1.18 En Bloc / Collective Sale (STB)

---

**Q13.** A developer takes out a mortgage over a Torrens-system property to finance construction. Which statement BEST describes the legal effect of a registered mortgage under the Land Titles Act?

- A. It is valid and binding even before registration, by virtue of the loan agreement
- B. It transfers legal ownership of the land to the mortgagee until the loan is repaid
- C. It operates as a registered charge - the mortgagor retains title - and is effective only on registration
- D. It automatically gives the mortgagee an easement over the land

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> Under the Torrens system a mortgage does NOT transfer ownership; it operates as a registered CHARGE, the mortgagor retains title, and it takes effect only on registration (the folio then shows the encumbrance, and on default the mortgagee has a statutory power of sale). B describes the old common-law mortgage (title transfer), which Torrens abolished. A is wrong because a Torrens mortgage takes effect only on registration. D confuses a mortgage with an easement - different interests entirely. 中文: Torrens按揭为登记的押记，业主保留产权，须登记才生效，不转移所有权，亦非地役权。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK P1.17 Encumbrances / Mortgages / Charges

---

**Q14.** A homeowner grants his neighbour a registered right of way across his garden so the neighbour can reach the main road. In this easement, the neighbour's land that benefits is the ______ and the homeowner's land that is burdened is the ______.

- A. caveatable interest; overriding interest
- B. servient tenement; dominant tenement
- C. freehold estate; leasehold estate
- D. dominant tenement; servient tenement

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(easy)_
>
> An easement requires a dominant tenement (the land that benefits - here the neighbour's land) and a servient tenement (the land that is burdened - the homeowner's garden). B reverses the two terms. C describes types of estate, not easement parties. A confuses easement terminology with unrelated land-law concepts. 中文: 地役权中受益地为'需役地'(dominant)，负担地为'供役地'(servient)；B颠倒，C/D概念错误。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK P1.16 Easements

---

**Q15.** Which statement about the lodging and removal of a caveat under the Land Titles Act is the common exam trap most candidates get WRONG?

- A. A caveat is precautionary, NOT mandatory, and the Registrar cannot remove it on his own motion
- B. A caveat is legally mandatory for every buyer and must be lodged before the OTP is signed
- C. The Registrar may remove any caveat at his own discretion at any time
- D. A wrongful caveat carries no consequences for the person who lodged it

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> A caveat is a PRECAUTIONARY (protective) measure - it is not mandatory, and the Registrar cannot remove it purely on his own motion (removal follows the statutory lapsing/withdrawal/court-order processes). B is wrong: a caveat is optional and is lodged only once a caveatable interest arises (e.g. after exercising the OTP), not before. C is wrong because the Registrar has no such unilateral power. D is wrong because a wrongful caveat exposes the caveator to liability in damages under s128. 中文: 契约登记是预防性、非强制，登记官不能自行删除；错误登记须依s128赔偿。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK P1.15 Caveats; Common Trap #8

---


## P1.5 Land Titles & Registration, Caveats, Easements, Encumbrances

**Q1.** Singapore's land registration system under the Land Titles Act 1993 is based on the Torrens system, which rests on three foundational principles. Which of the following correctly states the 'Curtain' principle?

- A. The register is guaranteed by the State, which compensates anyone who suffers loss from a registration error
- B. A purchaser need not look behind the register to investigate the history of prior dealings in the title
- C. The register accurately reflects all the material facts about the current state of the title
- D. Registration of an instrument vests legal title in the registered proprietor

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> The Curtain principle means a prospective buyer can rely on the register as it stands and does not need to investigate the chain of past dealings hidden 'behind the curtain'. Option A describes the Insurance principle (State guarantee/compensation). Option C describes the Mirror principle (register reflects the title accurately). Option D is a general effect of registration vesting legal title, not one of the three named principles. 中文: 'Curtain'(帷幕)原则指买方无需查看登记簿背后的历史交易;A是保险原则,C是镜子原则,D只是登记的法律效果。
>
> 📎 Source: Land Titles Act 1993 (Torrens principles: Mirror, Curtain, Insurance)

---

**Q2.** Mr Tan is the registered proprietor of a freehold property under the Land Titles Act. Section 46 grants him an indefeasible title. Which ONE of the following situations would NOT be protected by indefeasibility and could allow his registered title to be set aside?

- A. A prior unregistered equitable interest that he had no notice of when he registered
- B. An old unregistered restrictive covenant that was never noted on the folio
- C. Where Mr Tan himself procured registration through fraud or forgery
- D. A neighbour's claim based on an informal verbal agreement made years before registration

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> Indefeasibility under s46 LTA is not absolute. Section 46(2) provides that title may be defeated by fraud or forgery to which the registered proprietor (or his agent) was a party or in which he colluded. Where Mr Tan himself procured registration by fraud, his title can be set aside. Options A, B and D describe unregistered interests that are generally defeated by a registered proprietor taking in good faith precisely because of indefeasibility and the curtain principle. 中文: s46(2)赋予的不可推翻性最重要的例外是注册人本人(或代理人)欺诈或伪造(C);A、B、D是未注册权益,通常被善意注册人击败。
>
> 📎 Source: Land Titles Act 1993 s46(2) (indefeasibility; fraud/forgery exception)

---

**Q3.** A buyer exercises the Option to Purchase on a private condominium unit and instructs her lawyer to lodge a caveat with SLA. What is the PRIMARY purpose of lodging this caveat?

- A. It is a legal requirement that must be done before the buyer can lawfully complete the purchase
- B. It transfers legal ownership of the unit to the buyer immediately upon lodgement
- C. It automatically extinguishes any existing mortgage registered against the property
- D. It gives notice of the buyer's interest and acts as a precautionary 'freeze' so SLA notifies her of inconsistent dealings

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> A caveat is a precautionary statutory notice that protects the caveator's interest by alerting SLA, so the caveator is notified of any inconsistent dealing and can act. It is NOT mandatory (A is the common trap). It does not transfer legal title (B) - legal title passes only on registration of the transfer. It does not extinguish a mortgage (C) - the mortgage remains a registered encumbrance. 中文: 警告通知(caveat)是预防性的、非强制的,用于告知并冻结;它不转移产权(B),非必须(A),也不消灭抵押(C)。
>
> 📎 Source: Land Titles Act 1993 (caveats)

---

**Q4.** Once successfully lodged with SLA, for how long does a caveat under the Land Titles Act remain valid before it must be extended?

- A. 5 years, extendable for a further 5 years
- B. 3 years, extendable for a further 3 years
- C. Indefinitely, until the caveator withdraws it
- D. 1 year, renewable annually

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> A caveat accepted by SLA is valid for 5 years from the date of lodgement and may be extended for a further 5 years before it expires. Option B confuses it with other timeframes; option C is wrong because a caveat is time-limited and will lapse if not extended; option D is incorrect. 中文: caveat有效期5年,可再延长5年;并非3年(B)、无限期(C)或1年(D)。
>
> 📎 Source: Land Titles Act 1993; SLA (caveat valid 5 years, extendable 5 more)

---

**Q5.** A caveator has lodged a caveat. The registered proprietor applies to register an inconsistent dealing (e.g. a transfer), and SLA serves a lapsing notice on the caveator. To keep the caveat alive, what must the caveator do, and within what period?

- A. Lodge a fresh caveat within 14 days of the notice
- B. Obtain a court order extending the operation of the caveat within 30 days of the notice
- C. Apply to SLA in writing to extend the caveat within 21 days of the notice
- D. Do nothing - SLA cannot register the inconsistent dealing while any caveat exists

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> Under s127 LTA, when the Registrar serves a lapsing notice, the caveator has 30 days to serve on the Registrar a court order extending the caveat's operation; otherwise the caveat lapses and the dealing is registered. A fresh caveat (A) or a mere written SLA application (C) does not satisfy the requirement - a court order is needed. Option D is wrong because the notice mechanism exists precisely to allow the dealing to proceed if no court order is obtained. 中文: 依s127,收到失效通知后须在30天内取得并送达法院命令延续caveat,否则失效;非14天(A)、非书面申请(C),也不能永久阻止登记(D)。
>
> 📎 Source: Land Titles Act 1993 s127 (lapsing of caveat on notice; 30 days for court order)

---

**Q6.** A property developer believes a rival has wrongfully lodged a caveat against its land without any genuine caveatable interest, delaying its sale. Which statement correctly describes the legal position?

- A. SLA's Registrar may remove the caveat on its own initiative once it doubts the interest, and the developer has no remedy
- B. A caveat can only ever be lodged by the registered proprietor, so the rival's caveat is automatically void
- C. The Registrar cannot remove the caveat on its own motion, but a person who lodges a caveat wrongfully, vexatiously or without reasonable cause may be liable in damages
- D. The developer must wait the full 5 years for the caveat to lapse and has no earlier recourse

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> The Registrar does not remove a caveat on its own motion; removal occurs through withdrawal, lapsing (e.g. via the s127 notice procedure), or court order. A caveator who lodges wrongfully, vexatiously or without reasonable cause may be liable in damages under s128 to any person who suffers pecuniary loss. Option A is wrong on both counts. Option B is wrong - any person with a caveatable interest (buyer, mortgagee, CPF Board, etc.) may lodge, not only the proprietor.
