Option D is wrong because the developer can use the lapsing-notice procedure rather than wait 5 years. 中文: Registrar不能自行移除caveat,但无合理理由错误lodge者依s128须赔偿;A、B、D均错。
>
> 📎 Source: Land Titles Act 1993 s127 (notice procedure); s128 (compensation for wrongful caveat)

---

**Q7.** Mdm Lim's bungalow has no direct access to the public road and she relies on a registered right of way over her neighbour Mr Goh's land. In easement terminology, which statement is correct?

- A. Mdm Lim's land is the servient tenement and Mr Goh's land is the dominant tenement
- B. A registered easement does not bind Mr Goh's successors when he sells the land
- C. An easement does not require both a benefited and a burdened parcel of land
- D. Mdm Lim's land is the dominant tenement (benefited) and Mr Goh's land is the servient tenement (burdened)

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> An easement needs a dominant tenement (the land that benefits) and a servient tenement (the land that is burdened). Mdm Lim benefits, so her land is dominant; Mr Goh's land bears the burden, so it is servient. Option A reverses these. Option C is wrong - an easement requires both tenements. Option B is wrong - a registered easement is noted on the folio and binds successors in title. 中文: 受益地为需役地(dominant),负担地为供役地(servient);A颠倒,C漏了两块地的要求,D错(已登记地役权约束继受人)。
>
> 📎 Source: Land Titles Act 1993 (easements: dominant and servient tenements)

---

**Q8.** Which of the following is NOT an encumbrance on land?

- A. The fee simple estate held by the registered proprietor
- B. A registered easement
- C. A registered mortgage
- D. A restrictive covenant

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> An encumbrance is a third-party right that burdens the land. A mortgage, easement and restrictive covenant all burden the land for the benefit of someone other than the owner. The fee simple estate is the owner's own ownership interest - it is the estate being encumbered, not an encumbrance itself. 中文: 抵押、地役权、限制性约定都是负担(encumbrance);fee simple是所有权本身,不是负担,故选A。
>
> 📎 Source: Estates and interests in land (encumbrances)

---

**Q9.** Under the Land Titles Act, when a borrower mortgages a Torrens-registered property to a bank, what is the legal effect of the mortgage?

- A. Legal ownership of the property is transferred to the bank until the loan is repaid
- B. The mortgage operates as a registered charge; the mortgagor retains title and the bank obtains a statutory power of sale on default
- C. The mortgage takes effect immediately upon signing, even before registration
- D. The bank automatically becomes a joint tenant with the borrower

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> A Torrens mortgage does NOT transfer ownership; it operates as a registered charge. The mortgagor keeps title, and on default the mortgagee has a statutory power of sale. Option A reflects the old common-law mortgage, not the Torrens system. Option C is wrong - the mortgage takes effect only on registration. Option D is wrong - a mortgagee is not a co-owner. 中文: Torrens抵押不转移所有权,仅为登记的charge,违约时银行有法定出售权;A是旧普通法概念,C错(须登记生效),D错。
>
> 📎 Source: Land Titles Act 1993 (Torrens mortgage as registered charge)

---

**Q10.** Two siblings, Aaron and Brenda, hold a property as joint tenants. Aaron dies leaving a will giving 'all my property to my friend Carl'. What happens to Aaron's interest in the property?

- A. Aaron's half share passes to Carl under the will
- B. The property is sold and proceeds split between Brenda and Carl
- C. Aaron's interest passes automatically to Brenda by right of survivorship; the will does not apply to the joint tenancy
- D. Carl becomes a tenant-in-common with Brenda

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> In a joint tenancy the right of survivorship (jus accrescendi) means a deceased joint tenant's interest passes automatically to the surviving joint tenant(s), overriding the will. So Aaron's interest goes to Brenda, not Carl. Options A, B and D wrongly treat the interest as willable - that is the rule for tenancy-in-common, where a share passes by will or intestacy. 中文: 联权(joint tenancy)有生存者取得权,亡者份额自动归生存者Brenda,遗嘱无效;A、B、D是分权(TIC)的规则。
>
> 📎 Source: Co-ownership: joint tenancy and right of survivorship

---

**Q11.** Which of the following best distinguishes a joint tenancy from a tenancy-in-common?

- A. A joint tenancy requires only unity of possession, while a tenancy-in-common requires all four unities (PITT)
- B. A tenancy-in-common cannot be created with unequal shares
- C. Both forms carry the right of survivorship, but only a tenancy-in-common allows unequal shares
- D. A joint tenancy requires the four unities (Possession, Interest, Title, Time) and carries survivorship, while a tenancy-in-common requires only unity of possession and has no survivorship

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> A joint tenancy requires all four unities (Possession, Interest, Title, Time - PITT) and has the right of survivorship. A tenancy-in-common requires only unity of possession, allows distinct (possibly unequal) undivided shares, and has no survivorship. Option A reverses the unities requirement. Option C is wrong - a tenancy-in-common does NOT carry survivorship. Option B is wrong - a tenancy-in-common can have unequal shares. 中文: 联权需四统一(PITT)+生存者权;分权只需占有统一、份额可不等且无生存者权;A颠倒,C、D错。
>
> 📎 Source: Co-ownership: joint tenancy vs tenancy-in-common (four unities, survivorship)

---

**Q12.** A buyer exercised an Option to Purchase but failed to lodge a caveat. Before completion, the seller fraudulently sold and transferred the same property to a second buyer who paid full value, had no notice of the first sale, and became the registered proprietor. As between the equitable interest of the first buyer and the second buyer's registered title, what is the most likely outcome?

- A. The second buyer, as a bona fide purchaser for value without notice who is now registered, generally takes free of the first buyer's equitable interest
- B. The first buyer's equitable interest defeats the second buyer because it arose earlier in time
- C. Neither buyer obtains the property; it reverts to the State
- D. The first buyer can compel the Registrar to cancel the second buyer's registration without any court process

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> An equitable interest is enforceable against everyone EXCEPT a bona fide purchaser for value without notice. The second buyer paid value, had no notice, and is now registered, so he generally takes free of the earlier equitable interest - which is exactly why a caveat would have protected the first buyer. Option B wrongly assumes 'first in time' always wins. Option C is incorrect. Option D is wrong - the Registrar does not unilaterally cancel a registered title; the first buyer's remedy is against the fraudulent seller. 中文: 衡平权益对所有人有效,但不能对抗善意有偿且无通知的买方;第二买方已注册即取得无负担产权,这正是首买方应lodge caveat的原因。
>
> 📎 Source: Legal vs equitable interest; bona fide purchaser for value without notice

---

**Q13.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Mr and Mrs Rajan bought a 99-year leasehold condominium as JOINT TENANTS in 2015 and registered the title under the Land Titles Act. In 2024 their relationship broke down. Without telling his wife, Mr Rajan signed a deed/instrument unilaterally declaring that he holds his interest as a tenant-in-common, and registered it. He then granted an Option to Purchase over 'his share' to an investor, Mr Wee, who lodged a caveat. Based on these facts, which statement is most accurate?

- A. Mr Rajan cannot sever the joint tenancy without his wife's consent, so the deed has no effect
- B. A unilateral instrument of declaration is a recognised mode of severance under the LTA; it converts the joint tenancy into a tenancy-in-common, after which there is no right of survivorship over his share
- C. Severance is impossible once a property is registered under the Land Titles Act
- D. Severing the joint tenancy automatically gives Mr Rajan ownership of the whole property

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> A joint tenancy may be severed unilaterally - including, for registered land, by an instrument of declaration served on the other joint tenant (and through alienation, mutual agreement, mutual conduct, or court order). Mr Rajan's registered instrument of declaration is a valid mode of severance, converting his interest into a tenancy-in-common share with no survivorship. Option A is wrong - the wife's consent is not required for unilateral severance. Option C is wrong - severance is available for registered land. Option D is wrong - severance gives him a distinct share, not the whole property. 中文: 联权可单方面解除(对已登记土地可用声明书并送达对方),无需配偶同意,解除后变为分权且无生存者权;A、C、D均错。
>
> 📎 Source: Land Titles Act 1993 (severance of joint tenancy by instrument of declaration; modes of severance)

---

**Q14.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY (continued): SLA's records still show Mr and Mrs Rajan together with a notation reflecting Mr Rajan's severance, and Mr Wee's caveat is on the folio. Mrs Rajan now wishes to sell the WHOLE property to a third party but the buyer's lawyer flags Mr Wee's caveat during legal requisitions. Which of the following is the most appropriate and accurate advice?

- A. The caveat is irrelevant because Mrs Rajan owns the property and a buyer's caveat never binds a co-owner
- B. As registered proprietor Mrs Rajan can instruct SLA's Registrar to delete Mr Wee's caveat on its own motion
- C. Mr Wee's caveat protects his interest in Mr Rajan's share; the dealing cannot simply ignore it - it must be addressed by withdrawal, lapsing via the s127 notice procedure, or court order
- D. Mr Wee's caveat automatically lapses the moment any sale of the whole property is signed

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> Mr Wee has a caveatable interest (he holds an exercised OTP over Mr Rajan's share) and his caveat protects it. The transaction cannot ignore the caveat - it must be removed by withdrawal, by lapsing through the s127 notice procedure (caveator then has 30 days to obtain a court order), or by court order. Option A is wrong - the caveat affects the co-owner's share and clouds the title. Option B is wrong - the Registrar does not remove a caveat on its own motion. Option D is wrong - signing a sale does not auto-lapse the caveat. 中文: Mr Wee持有caveatable interest,caveat须经撤回、s127通知失效程序或法院命令处理,不能忽视;Registrar不能自行删除(B),也不会因签约自动失效(D)。
>
> 📎 Source: Land Titles Act 1993 (caveats; s127 lapsing procedure)

---

**Q15.** A small residue of private land in Singapore remains under the old deeds-based system (Registration of Deeds Act) rather than the Torrens / Land Titles Act system. Which statement correctly contrasts the two systems?

- A. Under the deeds system the State guarantees title, whereas Torrens title carries no State guarantee
- B. The deeds system gives stronger protection to purchasers than the Torrens system
- C. Both systems vest indefeasible title on registration in exactly the same way
- D. Under the Torrens system the register is conclusive and title is indefeasible on registration, whereas the deeds system relies on a chain of title deeds with no State guarantee

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(easy)_
>
> Under Torrens (Land Titles Act), the register is conclusive and title becomes indefeasible upon registration. The deeds system (Registration of Deeds Act) merely registers documents in a chain of historical title deeds, with priority by order of registration and NO State guarantee of title. Option A reverses the guarantee - it is the Torrens system that carries the State guarantee. Option C is wrong - only Torrens vests indefeasible title. Option B is wrong - Torrens generally gives purchasers stronger, cleaner protection. 中文: Torrens登记簿具确定性、注册即不可推翻且有国家担保;契据系统靠产权契据链、无国家担保;A颠倒,C、D错。
>
> 📎 Source: Land Titles Act 1993 (Torrens) vs Registration of Deeds Act (deeds system)

---


## P1.6 HDB: Eligibility Schemes, Grants & CPF Usage

**Q1.** A married Singapore Citizen couple, both aged 30, want to buy a 4-room HDB resale flat. Their combined average gross monthly household income is $11,500. Which CPF Housing Grant scheme has an income ceiling that they could potentially qualify for?

- A. The Family Grant ($14,000 income ceiling)
- B. The Single Singapore Citizen Scheme grant
- C. No grant, because resale flat buyers have no income ceiling
- D. The Enhanced CPF Housing Grant only, since its ceiling is $14,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> The Family Grant (CPF Housing Grant for resale flats, Families) has an income ceiling of $14,000. At $11,500 the couple is within that ceiling and can potentially qualify. B is wrong because they are a married couple, not single applicants. C confuses the rule that buying a resale flat WITHOUT any grant has no income ceiling — the moment you want a grant, the relevant ceiling applies. D states the wrong EHG ceiling: the EHG (Families) ceiling is $9,000, not $14,000, so at $11,500 they would exceed the EHG ceiling. 中文：购买二手组屋本身无收入顶限，但要拿家庭津贴顶限为$14,000，而EHG(家庭)顶限是$9,000，此夫妇$11,500只能符合家庭津贴。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB Family Grant / EHG income ceilings 2026

---

**Q2.** What is the maximum Enhanced CPF Housing Grant (EHG) that a first-timer FAMILY can receive when buying an HDB flat in 2026?

- A. $80,000
- B. $120,000
- C. $60,000
- D. $230,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> The EHG (Families) is up to $120,000 (a tiered grant that scales down as income rises, subject to the $9,000 income ceiling). A ($80,000) is the maximum Family Grant for a 2-4 room resale flat, not the EHG. C ($60,000) is the maximum EHG for SINGLES, not families. D ($230,000) is the approximate MAXIMUM COMBINED resale grants a family can stack ($80k Family Grant + $120k EHG + $30k PHG live-with), not the EHG alone. 中文：家庭EHG最高$120,000；$80,000是家庭津贴，$60,000是单身EHG，$230,000是叠加后的总额。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB Enhanced CPF Housing Grant (Families) 2026

---

**Q3.** A buyer purchases a resale HDB flat near (within 4km of) his parents' owner-occupied flat, and stacks the maximum eligible grants. He receives an $80,000 Family Grant, $120,000 EHG and the Proximity Housing Grant. What is the PHG amount and the approximate maximum combined resale grant total?

- A. PHG $30,000; total ~$230,000
- B. PHG $20,000; total ~$230,000
- C. PHG $20,000; total ~$220,000
- D. PHG $30,000; total ~$200,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> For families, living NEAR parents (within 4km) gives a PHG of $20,000, while living WITH them gives $30,000. $80,000 + $120,000 + $20,000 = $220,000. A and D wrongly use $30,000 (that is the 'live with' amount, not 'near'). C uses the correct $20,000 PHG but the widely-quoted ~$230,000 maximum reflects the 'live WITH' stack ($80k+$120k+$30k); for living NEAR the total is ~$220,000. 中文：家庭住在父母附近(4km内)PHG为$20,000，合计约$220,000；$30,000是与父母同住的金额。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB Proximity Housing Grant (Families) 2026

---

**Q4.** Two unmarried Singapore Citizen friends, aged 36 and 38, wish to jointly buy a flat directly from HDB. Under which scheme can they apply, and what is the key age condition?

- A. Public Scheme; both must be at least 21
- B. Single Singapore Citizen Scheme; one applicant must be at least 35
- C. Fiancé/Fiancée Scheme; they must marry within 3 months
- D. Joint Singles Scheme; all applicants must be at least 35

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> The Joint Singles Scheme allows 2 to 4 single Singapore Citizens to jointly buy, and all applicants must be at least 35 years old — both friends (36 and 38) qualify. A (Public Scheme) requires a family nucleus with at least one SC, which two unrelated friends do not form. C (Fiancé/Fiancée) is only for couples intending to marry. D (Single SC Scheme) is for ONE single person buying alone, not two friends jointly. 中文：两位单身朋友合买须用联合单身计划，所有人须满35岁；公共计划需家庭核心，单身计划仅限一人。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB Eligibility Schemes (Joint Singles Scheme) 2026

---

**Q5.** A 40-year-old single Singapore Citizen wants to use CPF to help buy a resale HDB flat with a remaining lease of 18 years. How much CPF Ordinary Account savings can she use towards the purchase?

- A. Nothing — no CPF may be used because the remaining lease is under 20 years
- B. A pro-rated amount based on the lease shortfall to age 95
- C. Up to 100% of the Valuation Limit
- D. Up to 120% of the Valuation Limit (the Withdrawal Limit)

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> The rule: no CPF may be used if the remaining lease is LESS THAN 20 years. At 18 years she cannot use any CPF OA savings. C is wrong — full CPF (up to the VL) only applies when the remaining lease is at least 20 years AND covers the youngest buyer to age 95. B (pro-rating) applies only when the lease is at least 20 years but does not cover the buyer to age 95 — it does not apply below the 20-year floor. D wrongly applies the private-property Withdrawal Limit; HDB flats bought with an HDB loan have no WL, and in any case the sub-20-year lease bars CPF use entirely here. 中文：剩余地契不足20年完全不能动用公积金；20年以上但不足以覆盖至95岁才按比例。
>
> 📎 Source: CPFB CPF usage lease rules 2026

---

**Q6.** A buyer buys a PRIVATE condominium for $1,000,000 (also its market value at purchase). What is the maximum amount of CPF he can use towards the property over the life of the loan, and what condition applies near that cap?

- A. $1,000,000 (the Valuation Limit), with no further condition
- B. $1,200,000 (the Withdrawal Limit), and to use CPF beyond 100% VL he must set aside the BRS if aged 55+
- C. $1,200,000, with no Basic Retirement Sum condition
- D. Unlimited — private property has no Withdrawal Limit

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> For private property, CPF use is capped at the Withdrawal Limit = 120% of VL = $1,200,000. To use CPF BEYOND 100% of VL (i.e. above $1,000,000) up to the WL, a member aged 55 and above must have set aside the Basic Retirement Sum (BRS). A stops at the VL but ignores that CPF can go up to 120% VL. C is wrong because the BRS set-aside condition does apply for those 55+. D is the reverse trap — it is HDB flats (with an HDB loan) that have NO Withdrawal Limit; PRIVATE property is exactly where the 120% WL applies. 中文：私宅公积金上限为120%估值($1,200,000)，超过100%者须(55岁以上)留存BRS；无上限的是组屋(用HDB贷款)而非私宅。
>
> 📎 Source: CPF Withdrawal Limit / BRS rules 2026

---

**Q7.** Which statement about CPF Valuation Limit (VL) and Withdrawal Limit (WL) is CORRECT for an HDB flat bought with an HDB concessionary loan?

- A. Both the VL and the 120% WL apply as for private property
- B. Only the 120% Withdrawal Limit applies
- C. Neither the VL nor the WL applies to such a purchase
- D. The VL applies but is fixed at the market value, not the purchase price

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> For an HDB flat financed with an HDB concessionary loan, NEITHER the VL nor the WL applies — CPF can be used to pay the purchase and servicing without a 100%/120% cap (subject to BRS/lease conditions where relevant). A is wrong — that describes private property. B is wrong — such HDB flats have no 120% WL at all. D mis-states the VL definition (the VL is the LOWER of purchase price or market value at purchase) and wrongly says it applies here. 中文：用HDB优惠贷款买组屋时VL和WL都不适用；私宅才有120%上限。
>
> 📎 Source: CPFB CPF VL/WL rules — HDB flats 2026

---

**Q8.** A couple buys a flat directly from HDB under the Fiancé/Fiancée Scheme. What is the key condition they must satisfy?

- A. They must already be legally married before applying
- B. They must have a combined income below $7,000
- C. They must be at least 35 years old
- D. They must register their marriage within 3 months of collecting the keys

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(easy)_
>
> Under the Fiancé/Fiancée Scheme, the couple must register their marriage within 3 months of key collection. A is wrong — the whole point of the scheme is that they are NOT yet married at application (married couples use the Public Scheme). C confuses the singles age-35 rule, which does not apply to an engaged couple. D ($7,000) is the singles 2-room Flexi BTO income ceiling, not a Fiancé/Fiancée condition (the family BTO ceiling is $14,000). 中文：未婚夫妇计划须在领钥匙后3个月内注册结婚；35岁是单身计划，$7,000是单身2房BTO顶限。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB Fiancé/Fiancée Scheme 2026

---

**Q9.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Daniel (SC, 33) and Mei (SC, 31), a married couple, are first-timers. Their combined average gross monthly household income is $8,500. They buy a 4-room resale flat for $560,000 located 3km from Mei's parents' owner-occupied HDB flat, and one of them has worked continuously for the past 14 months. Q: For which of the following are they BOTH within the income ceiling AND otherwise eligible?

- A. Family Grant, EHG and Proximity Housing Grant
- B. Family Grant and Proximity Housing Grant only — they exceed the EHG ceiling
- C. EHG only — resale flats are not eligible for the Family Grant
- D. Proximity Housing Grant only — the others have no income ceiling

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(hard)_
>
> Income $8,500 is within the Family Grant ceiling ($14,000) AND within the EHG (Families) ceiling ($9,000). The EHG also requires at least 12 continuous months of employment — satisfied (14 months). Living within 4km of parents qualifies for the PHG ($20,000 'near', no income ceiling). So all three apply. B is wrong because $8,500 is BELOW the $9,000 EHG ceiling, so they do NOT exceed it. C is wrong — the Family Grant is specifically for resale flats. D wrongly claims the Family Grant and EHG have no income ceiling. 中文：收入$8,500同时低于家庭津贴($14,000)和EHG($9,000)顶限，且满足12个月就业及4km邻近条件，故三项津贴皆可。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB Family Grant / EHG / PHG eligibility 2026

---

**Q10.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY (continued): Daniel and Mei finance the $560,000 resale flat (market value also $560,000) with an HDB concessionary loan at 75% LTV. The LTV for the HDB concessionary loan was cut from 80% to 75% on 20 August 2024. Q: What is the minimum down payment and how may it be paid?

- A. $140,000 (25%), payable fully in cash
- B. $140,000 (25%), which may be paid using CPF Ordinary Account savings
- C. $28,000 (5%), of which 5% must be cash
- D. $84,000 (15%), payable in cash or CPF

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> At 75% LTV on $560,000 the loan is $420,000, so the down payment is 25% = $140,000. For an HDB concessionary loan there is NO mandatory cash component — the down payment may be paid fully using CPF OA savings. A is wrong because no cash is mandatory for the HDB concessionary loan. C uses a 5% figure that does not apply (the bank-loan minimum cash is 5%, and 5% is not the down payment here). D uses 15%, which corresponds to neither the post-Aug-2024 25% down payment. 中文：75%贷款后首付25%=$140,000，HDB优惠贷款无强制现金，可全用公积金支付。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB concessionary loan LTV 75% (eff. 20 Aug 2024)

---

**Q11.** A first-timer single Singapore Citizen, aged 36, buys a resale flat. Which combination of grants is she eligible for, and at what amounts (assume she lives WITH her parents and meets income limits)?

- A. Family Grant $80,000 and PHG $30,000
- B. EHG $120,000 and PHG $30,000
- C. Singles Grant $40,000 (2-4rm) and PHG $15,000 (live with)
- D. Singles Grant $25,000 and PHG $10,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> For singles, the resale CPF Housing Grant (Singles) is $40,000 for a 2-4 room flat (and $25,000 for 5-room or larger). The PHG for a single living WITH parents is $15,000 (living near is $10,000). A applies the FAMILY amounts ($80,000 / $30,000), not the singles amounts. C uses the family EHG cap ($120,000) — singles EHG is only up to $60,000 — and the family 'live with' PHG. D mixes the 5-room+ Singles Grant ($25,000) with the 'live near' single PHG ($10,000), which does not match a 'live with' a 2-4 room scenario. 中文：单身二手津贴2-4房$40,000，与父母同住单身PHG为$15,000；$80,000/$30,000是家庭金额。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB Singles Grant / PHG (Singles) 2026

---

**Q12.** Which of the following correctly states an HDB Minimum Occupation Period (MOP) rule for flats with key collection in 2026?

- A. All HDB flats have a 5-year MOP regardless of category
- B. A Prime flat has a 5-year MOP, the same as a standard flat
- C. A resale flat bought without any grant has no MOP, while subsidised flats have a 5-year MOP
- D. A Plus or Prime flat has a 10-year MOP, while a standard flat has a 5-year MOP

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> Under the Standard/Plus/Prime classification, Plus and Prime flats carry a 10-year MOP, while Standard flats keep the 5-year MOP. A is wrong because Plus/Prime are 10 years, not 5. B understates the Prime MOP (it is 10, not 5). C is wrong — a resale flat bought without any grant (with the purchase application received on or after 30 Aug 2010) still carries a 5-year MOP; it does NOT have 'no MOP' under current rules. 中文：Plus和Prime组屋MOP为10年，普通(Standard)为5年；2010年8月30日起买的无津贴二手组屋仍有5年MOP，并非无MOP。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB Standard/Plus/Prime MOP framework 2026

---

**Q13.** What is the income ceiling to qualify for the Enhanced CPF Housing Grant (EHG) as a SINGLE applicant in 2026?

- A. $4,500
- B. $7,000
- C. $9,000
- D. $14,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> The EHG income ceiling for singles is $4,500 (the EHG (Families) ceiling is $9,000). B ($7,000) is the income ceiling for singles buying a 2-room Flexi BTO, not the EHG-singles ceiling. C ($9,000) is the EHG ceiling for FAMILIES, not singles. D ($14,000) is the family BTO/Family Grant ceiling. 中文：单身EHG收入顶限为$4,500；家庭EHG为$9,000，单身2房BTO为$7,000，家庭津贴/BTO为$14,000。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB EHG (Singles) income ceiling 2026

---

**Q14.** Which statement about buying an HDB resale flat outright (without any CPF Housing Grant) is correct regarding the income ceiling?

- A. The $14,000 family income ceiling always applies to any HDB purchase
- B. There is NO income ceiling to buy a resale flat without a grant
- C. The $16,000 Executive Condominium ceiling applies
- D. The $7,000 ceiling applies to all resale flats

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> There is NO income ceiling to buy a resale HDB flat outright without any grant — the ceiling only bites once you apply for a grant or buy a new/BTO flat. A is a classic trap: the $14,000 ceiling applies to BTO/new flats and the Family Grant, not to a no-grant resale purchase. C ($16,000) is the EC ceiling, irrelevant to a resale HDB purchase. D ($7,000) is the singles 2-room Flexi BTO ceiling, not a resale rule. 中文：不拿津贴买二手组屋无收入顶限；$14,000适用于BTO/家庭津贴，$16,000是EC，$7,000是单身2房BTO。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB resale eligibility / income ceiling rules 2026

---


## P1.7 HDB: Resale Procedure, MOP, Ethnic Integration Policy / SPR Quota, Renting Out

**Q1.** Mdm Tan collected the keys to her standard BTO 4-room flat on 1 March 2021. She wants to know the earliest date she can sell the flat on the open market. When is the earliest she may sell?

- A. 1 March 2024 (3-year MOP)
- B. 1 March 2031 (10-year MOP)
- C. 1 March 2026 (5-year MOP)
- D. Immediately, because resale flats have no MOP

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(easy)_
>
> The Minimum Occupation Period for a standard HDB flat is 5 years computed from the date of key collection, so 1 March 2021 + 5 years = 1 March 2026. A) 3 years is not an HDB MOP figure. B) 10 years applies only to Plus and Prime flats, not standard flats. D) No-MOP applies only to a resale flat bought without any grant, not to a BTO flat. 中文：标准组屋的最低居住期(MOP)为5年，自领钥匙日起算，故最早可售日为2026年3月1日。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB MOP rules (verified hdb.gov.sg June 2026: Standard = 5 years from key collection)

---

**Q2.** A salesperson is explaining the Ethnic Integration Policy (EIP) to a prospective buyer. Which statement is CORRECT?

- A. The EIP applies to both HDB resale flats and private condominiums
- B. Malaysian SPRs are exempt from the EIP ethnic quota
- C. The EIP block limit for the Malay group is 84%
- D. The EIP quota is only checked when the buyer's ethnic group differs from the seller's ethnic group

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(easy)_
>
> The EIP quota check is triggered only when the buyer and seller belong to different ethnic groups; a same-group transaction does not change the block's ethnic proportions, so no check applies. A) EIP applies only to HDB flats, never to private property. C) 84% (block) / 78% (neighbourhood) is the Chinese limit; the Malay limit is 22% (block) / 16% (neighbourhood). B) Malaysians are exempt from the separate SPR quota, but NOT from the EIP ethnic quota — a Malaysian SPR is still counted under his registered race for EIP. That is a common trap. 中文：EIP仅在买卖双方种族不同时触发检查；它只适用于组屋，不适用于私宅；84%/78%是华族上限(马来族为22%/16%)；马来西亚人只豁免SPR配额，不豁免EIP种族配额。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB EIP/SPR Quota (verified hdb.gov.sg June 2026: Chinese 84% block/78% nbhd, Malay 22% block/16% nbhd, Indian/Others 12% block/10% nbhd)

---

**Q3.** Mr Lim, a Singapore Citizen, owns a 5-room standard HDB flat that has completed its MOP. He wants to rent out the entire flat to a foreign tenant. Which condition is NOT a valid requirement he must satisfy?

- A. He must continue to physically reside in the flat throughout the tenancy
- B. The minimum tenancy period must be at least 6 months
- C. He must obtain HDB's approval to rent out the whole flat
- D. The flat must comply with the Non-Citizen Quota if the tenant is a non-Malaysian non-citizen

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> Renting out the WHOLE flat means the owner does not live there, so continued physical residence is NOT a requirement (that requirement applies to renting out bedrooms only). C) HDB approval is required to rent out a whole flat. B) The minimum tenancy is 6 months. D) The Non-Citizen Quota (8% neighbourhood / 11% block) applies when the whole-flat tenant is a non-Malaysian non-citizen. 中文：整套出租意味着屋主不住，因此无须本人居住；需HDB批准、最短6个月租期、并符合非公民配额(8%邻里/11%楼)。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB Renting Out rules (verified hdb.gov.sg June 2026: whole-flat rental, 6-month min, NCQ 8% nbhd/11% block)

---

**Q4.** An SPR couple (both non-Malaysian) owns an HDB resale flat that has completed its 5-year MOP. They approach a salesperson wanting to rent out the entire flat while they relocate overseas for work. What is the correct advice?

- A. They may rent out the whole flat, subject to HDB approval and the Non-Citizen Quota
- B. They cannot rent out the whole flat because SPR owners are not allowed to sublet the entire flat
- C. They may rent out the whole flat only if at least one of them is a Malaysian SPR
- D. They may rent out the whole flat for a maximum tenancy of 2 years

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> Only Singapore Citizen owners may rent out the whole flat after MOP. SPR owners are NOT permitted to sublet the entire flat regardless of MOP completion (they may only rent out spare bedrooms while residing in the flat). A) and D) presuppose eligibility that SPRs do not have. C) Being a Malaysian SPR affects the tenant-side Non-Citizen Quota, not the owner's eligibility to rent out the whole flat. 中文：只有公民屋主在满足MOP后才能整套出租；SPR屋主无论是否满MOP都不能整套出租，只能在自住下出租卧室。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB Renting Out eligibility (verified hdb.gov.sg June 2026: SPR owners may only rent out bedrooms, not whole flat)

---

**Q5.** A Chinese seller wants to sell his HDB resale flat. A salesperson checks the EIP/SPR portal and finds that the Chinese block limit has been reached, but the neighbourhood limit has not. Which buyer can the seller definitely sell to without any further EIP check?

- A. An Indian Singapore Citizen buyer, with no EIP restriction whatsoever
- B. Only a Malay Singapore Citizen, because Malays are never quota-restricted
- C. A Chinese buyer, because a same-group sale is exempt from the EIP quota check
- D. No buyer at all, because the block limit is full

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> When the Chinese block limit is full, the seller may still sell to a Chinese buyer because a same-group transaction is exempt from the EIP check — it does not change the block's Chinese proportion (one out, one in). A) is wrong as stated: selling to an Indian buyer is NOT free of any EIP restriction — the Indian buyer must still pass the Indian block AND neighbourhood limits, so the sale is conditional, not unrestricted. B) Malays are subject to their own EIP limits (22% block / 16% neighbourhood), so they are not 'never restricted'. D) A same-group sale is always still possible, so 'no buyer at all' is wrong. 中文：华族楼层配额满时，华族卖家仍可卖给华族买家(同族交易豁免检查)；卖给印度族买家仍须通过印度族配额，并非毫无限制。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB EIP/SPR Quota mechanics (verified hdb.gov.sg June 2026: same-ethnic-group sales exempt from quota check)

---

**Q6.** In an HDB resale transaction, the Option Fee and the Exercise Fee are governed by HDB caps. Which combination is within the permitted limits?

- A. Option Fee $1,500; Exercise Fee $4,000 (total $5,500)
- B. Option Fee $1,000; Exercise Fee $5,000 (total $6,000)
- C. Option Fee $2,000; Exercise Fee $3,500 (total $5,500)
- D. Option Fee $1,000; Exercise Fee $4,000 (total $5,000)

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> For an HDB resale OTP, the Option Fee must be between $1 and $1,000, and the Option Fee plus Exercise Fee combined must not exceed $5,000. Only B satisfies both: Option Fee $1,000 (within $1–$1,000) and total $5,000 (within cap). A) and C) have Option Fees exceeding $1,000. B) total of $6,000 exceeds the $5,000 combined cap. 中文：组屋转售期权费上限$1,000，期权费+行使费合计不超过$5,000，只有B符合。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB resale OTP (verified hdb.gov.sg June 2026: Option Fee $1–$1,000; Option+Exercise ≤ $5,000)

---

**Q7.** After a seller grants an HDB resale Option to Purchase (OTP), within what period must the buyer exercise the option, and at what time does it expire on the final day?

- A. 21 calendar days, expiring at 4pm
- B. 14 calendar days, expiring at 5pm
- C. 21 working days, expiring at 4pm
- D. 7 calendar days, expiring at 4pm

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> An HDB resale OTP has a fixed option period of 21 calendar days and expires at 4pm on the last day. B) 14 days at 5pm describes a private OTP convention, not HDB. C) The period is calendar days, not working days. D) 7 days is the HDB seller's cooling-off period after registering Intent to Sell (before granting the OTP), not the option exercise period. 中文：组屋转售期权期限为21个日历日，最后一天下午4点截止。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB OTP (verified hdb.gov.sg June 2026: option period 21 calendar days, expires 4pm)

---

**Q8.** A buyer of an HDB resale flat submits a Request for Value to HDB. Which statement about the valuation is CORRECT?

- A. The Request for Value must be submitted before the OTP is granted
- B. The valuation, once obtained, is valid for 3 months
- C. The seller, not the buyer, must request and pay for the valuation
- D. The valuation determines the maximum Option Fee that can be charged

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> An HDB Request for Value (cost $120) produces a valuation that is valid for 3 months from when it is made available. A) The Request for Value is submitted by the buyer AFTER the OTP has been granted (the buyer must hold a valid OTP, and submit by the next working day after receiving the OTP). C) The buyer requests and pays for the valuation, not the seller. D) The valuation governs CPF/loan amounts and any Cash-Over-Valuation, not the Option Fee cap (which is fixed at $1–$1,000). 中文：组屋估值由买家在取得期权后申请，费用$120，有效期3个月。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB resale procedure (verified hdb.gov.sg June 2026: Request for Value — buyer; $120; valid 3 months; submit by next working day after OTP)

---

**Q9.** Mr and Mrs Kumar own an HDB 4-room flat. Under the temporarily relaxed occupancy cap currently in force (22 Jan 2024 to 31 Dec 2028), what is the maximum number of occupants permitted in the flat, and what is the maximum number of bedrooms they may rent out while continuing to live there?

- A. 6 occupants; may rent out 1 bedroom
- B. 8 occupants; may rent out 3 bedrooms
- C. 8 occupants; may rent out 2 bedrooms
- D. 6 occupants; may rent out 2 bedrooms

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> Under the relaxed occupancy cap (extended on 22 Jan 2024 and now running to 31 Dec 2028), a 4-room and larger flat may have up to 8 occupants. For bedroom rental, a 4-room or larger flat may rent out a maximum of 2 bedrooms (a 3-room flat may rent out only 1). A) 6 is the cap for 3-room flats and understates bedrooms. B) A 4-room flat has only 3 bedrooms but the rental cap is 2 rooms, not 3. D) 6 occupants is the 3-room cap. 中文：宽限期(已延长至2028年12月31日)内4房及以上户型占用上限8人，最多可出租2间卧室。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB/URA occupancy cap (verified hdb.gov.sg June 2026: relaxation extended to 31 Dec 2028; 8 for 4rm+; bedroom rental 4rm+ max 2 rooms, 3rm max 1)

---

**Q10.** A salesperson is advising on a Prime-category HDB flat that has just completed its 10-year MOP. The owner, a Singapore Citizen, asks whether he can now rent out the entire flat. What is the correct advice?

- A. Yes, because the 10-year MOP has been completed and he is a Singapore Citizen
- B. Yes, but only to Singapore Citizen or Malaysian tenants
- C. No, because Prime flats can never be rented out under any circumstances
- D. No, because whole-flat rental is not permitted for Prime flats even after MOP

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> Prime-category flats are subject to stricter conditions: whole-flat rental is NOT allowed even after the 10-year MOP is completed. A) and B) wrongly assume that completing MOP unlocks whole-flat rental, which is true for standard flats but not Prime/Plus. C) is too absolute — bedroom rental (with the owner residing in the flat, 3-room or larger) is generally still permitted, so Prime flats are not barred from ALL rental. 中文：Prime类组屋即使满10年MOP也不能整套出租，故C正确；但仍可在屋主居住下出租卧室。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB Renting Out (verified hdb.gov.sg June 2026: Plus/Prime — no whole-flat rental even after MOP)

---

**Q11.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Mr Goh (Chinese SC) is selling his 4-room HDB resale flat through salesperson Aileen. A prospective buyer, Mr Ravi, is an Indian Singapore Citizen. Aileen checks the EIP/SPR portal at the start of the month and confirms both the Indian block and neighbourhood limits have ample headroom. Mr Ravi is buying with his wife, who is a non-Malaysian Indian SPR. The block's SPR proportion currently stands at 8%. What should Aileen advise about the eligibility of this transaction?

- A. The sale cannot proceed because the SPR quota (8% per block) has already been reached
- B. The sale can proceed because the Indian ethnic quota has headroom
- C. The sale can proceed because at least one buyer is a Singapore Citizen, which exempts the household from the SPR quota
- D. The sale cannot proceed because a Chinese seller can never sell to an Indian buyer

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(hard)_
>
> Even when the ethnic (EIP) quota has headroom, a separate SPR quota of 8% per block (and 5% per neighbourhood) must also be satisfied where any buyer is a non-Malaysian SPR. Mrs Ravi is a non-Malaysian Indian SPR, and the block's SPR proportion is already at the 8% cap, so the transaction is blocked. B) Passing the EIP check is necessary but not sufficient; the SPR cap is an independent gate. C) Having an SC co-buyer does NOT exempt the household; the SPR quota bites if any buyer is a non-Malaysian SPR. D) Cross-group sales are allowed when quota permits; there is no blanket Chinese-to-Indian ban. 中文：即使EIP种族配额有空位，只要有非马来西亚SPR买家，仍须满足每楼8%(每邻里5%)的SPR配额；此处已达8%故交易不可进行。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB EIP/SPR Quota (verified hdb.gov.sg June 2026: SPR cap 8% per block / 5% per neighbourhood, independent of EIP)

---

**Q12.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Madam Siti (Malay SC) collected keys to her standard 4-room BTO flat on 15 June 2020. In 2026 she is divorced and wants to: (i) sell the flat, and (ii) before selling, rent out one bedroom to a foreign student to ease cash flow while she still lives there. Salesperson Hadi assesses her plans. Which statement is the BEST advice?

- A. She cannot sell yet because her MOP only ends on 15 June 2030, and she cannot rent out any bedroom before MOP
- B. Her MOP ended on 15 June 2025, so she may sell; and bedroom rental was permitted earlier because owners may rent out bedrooms before MOP if they still reside in the flat
- C. She may sell only after a 10-year MOP because she received a CPF grant
- D. She may rent out the whole flat now because her 5-year MOP is complete

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> A standard flat's MOP is 5 years from key collection: 15 June 2020 + 5 years = 15 June 2025, so by 2026 she may sell. Bedroom rental (as opposed to whole-flat rental) is permitted even BEFORE MOP, provided the owner continues to reside in the flat — so renting a room out in earlier years was allowed. A) Wrongly states MOP is 10 years and that no bedroom rental is allowed before MOP. C) A standard flat keeps a 5-year MOP even with a grant; 10 years applies only to Plus/Prime flats. D) Although she may now rent the whole flat as an SC after MOP, the scenario describes renting a single bedroom while residing — D mischaracterises her stated plan. 中文：标准组屋5年MOP(2025年6月满)，可售；卧室出租在屋主自住情况下即使未满MOP也可进行。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB MOP & Renting Out (verified hdb.gov.sg June 2026: Standard MOP 5 years; bedrooms may be rented before MOP if owner still resides)

---

**Q13.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: A landlord (SC) has completed MOP and wants to rent out his whole 5-room flat. The neighbourhood Non-Citizen Quota has been reached. Three prospective tenant households apply: (1) a Malaysian work-pass family; (2) a Filipino professional family; (3) a Singapore Citizen family. Which tenants can the landlord legally rent the whole flat to?

- A. Only the Singapore Citizen family (3)
- B. All three households
- C. The Malaysian family (1) and the Singapore Citizen family (3)
- D. Only the Filipino family (2), because foreigners are exempt from the quota

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> When the Non-Citizen Quota is reached, only Singapore Citizens and Malaysians may rent a whole flat in that neighbourhood/block, because Malaysians are exempt from the quota. So both the Malaysian family (1) and the SC family (3) qualify. A) Excludes the Malaysian family, who are exempt and therefore eligible. B) The Filipino family (2) is a non-Malaysian non-citizen and is barred once the quota is full. D) Foreigners are NOT exempt — Malaysians are; this reverses the rule. 中文：非公民配额满时，只有公民与马来西亚人可整套租住(马来西亚人豁免)，故1和3可，菲律宾家庭不可。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB Non-Citizen Quota (verified hdb.gov.sg June 2026: Malaysians exempt; quota 8% nbhd / 11% block)

---

**Q14.** Which of the following resale buyers would be subject to NO income ceiling at all?

- A. A family buying a resale flat and applying for the CPF Family Grant
- B. A family buying a new BTO flat
- C. A single buying a 2-room Flexi BTO flat
- D. A family buying a resale flat with no housing grant

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> There is no income ceiling to buy a resale flat outright (without any grant or HDB loan) — a classic exam trap. A) Applying for the CPF Family Grant imposes the $14,000 household income ceiling. C) The 2-room Flexi for singles has a $7,000 ceiling. B) A new BTO family flat has a $14,000 ceiling. 中文：不申请任何津贴(及不用HDB贷款)的转售购买无收入顶限；申请津贴或买新组屋则有顶限。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB Income Ceilings (verified hdb.gov.sg June 2026: resale without grant = no ceiling; Family Grant $14,000; 2-room Flexi single $7,000)

---

**Q15.** A salesperson is outlining the correct sequence of an HDB resale transaction to a first-time seller. Which ordering of key steps is CORRECT?

- A. Register Intent to Sell (7-day cooling-off) → Grant OTP → Buyer exercises OTP → Submit resale application
- B. Grant OTP → Register Intent to Sell → Buyer exercises OTP → Submit resale application
- C. Submit resale application → Register Intent to Sell → Grant OTP → Buyer exercises OTP
- D. Register Intent to Sell → Submit resale application → Grant OTP → Buyer exercises OTP

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> The correct flow is: register Intent to Sell on My Flat Dashboard (which triggers a 7-day seller cooling-off period before an OTP may be granted) → grant the OTP (buyer must hold a valid HFE letter) → buyer exercises the OTP within the 21-day option period → both parties submit the resale application. B) Granting the OTP before registering Intent to Sell is wrong — Intent to Sell and the 7-day cooling-off come first. C) and D) place the resale application before the OTP is granted/exercised, which is out of sequence (the application follows a validly exercised OTP). 中文：正确顺序为登记销售意向(7天冷静期)→批出期权→买家行使期权→提交转售申请。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB resale procedure (verified hdb.gov.sg June 2026: Register Intent → 7-day cooling-off → OTP → exercise within 21 days → resale application)

---


## P1.8 Private Residential Property & Residential Property Act (Foreign Ownership)

**Q1.** Under the Residential Property Act 1976, which of the following is considered a 'foreign person' who is subject to restrictions on the purchase of restricted residential property?

- A. A Singapore Citizen buying his second landed home
- B. A Singapore Permanent Resident (SPR)
- C. A Singapore-registered company wholly owned by Singapore Citizens
- D. A Singapore Citizen acting as trustee for his SC children

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> The RPA's definition of 'foreign person' expressly includes Singapore Permanent Residents (as well as foreigners and foreign-controlled entities), so an SPR must obtain LDAU approval to buy restricted property. (A) and (D) involve Singapore Citizens, who are not foreign persons. (C) A Singapore company wholly owned by SCs is not foreign-controlled and is not a foreign person. The key trap is that SPRs are NOT treated as locals under the RPA. 中文:外国人定义涵盖永久居民(PR),买受限制性住宅需LDAU批准。
>
> 📎 Source: Residential Property Act 1976; SLA Foreign Ownership (https://www.sla.gov.sg/regulatory/foreign-ownership-of-property/)

---

**Q2.** Mr Tan, a foreigner, wishes to buy a residential property in Singapore WITHOUT needing approval from the Land Dealings Approval Unit (LDAU). Which property can he buy freely?

- A. A vacant plot of residential land in Bukit Timah
- B. A terrace house in a landed housing estate
- C. A condominium unit in a development approved under the Planning Act
- D. A strata landed bungalow located outside an approved condominium

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(easy)_
>
> A condominium unit is a non-restricted property; foreigners may buy it freely without LDAU approval. (A) vacant residential land is restricted. (B) a terrace (landed) house is restricted. (D) strata landed property OUTSIDE an approved condominium is restricted; only strata landed WITHIN an approved condo is non-restricted. The trap is the 'outside an approved condo' qualifier in (D). 中文:外国人可自由购买公寓单位;空地、有地住宅、未在公寓内的有地分层产权均受限。
>
> 📎 Source: SLA Foreign Ownership of Property

---

**Q3.** A foreigner applies to the LDAU for approval to purchase a semi-detached house on mainland Singapore. Which combination BEST reflects the principal criteria the LDAU considers?

- A. Singapore PR for at least 10 years OR ownership of a local business
- B. Singapore PR for at least 3 years AND minimum annual income of $300,000
- C. Any foreigner with at least $5 million in local bank deposits
- D. Singapore PR for at least 5 years AND exceptional economic contribution to Singapore

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> Per the SLA LDAU criteria, the applicant should be a Singapore PR for at least 5 years AND must make an exceptional economic contribution to Singapore (assessed e.g. by employment income assessable for tax in Singapore). Both conditions apply. (B) uses the wrong PR duration (3 years) and an invented income threshold. (C) bank deposits alone are not the test, and a non-PR foreigner generally cannot get mainland approval. (A) overstates the PR period to 10 years and the 'OR' is wrong; both conditions are needed. 中文:LDAU主要标准是PR满5年 + 对新加坡有显著经济贡献,两者并需。
>
> 📎 Source: SLA LDAU approval criteria (https://app.sla.gov.sg/ldau/faq)

---

**Q4.** A non-resident foreigner (not a Singapore PR) wants to buy a landed property. Where is he most likely to obtain LDAU approval, and under what key restriction?

- A. Sentosa Cove, provided the land area does not exceed 1,800 sq metres
- B. Any landed estate on the mainland, provided the land area does not exceed 15,000 sq ft
- C. Sentosa Cove, provided the land area does not exceed 15,000 sq ft
- D. Any strata landed property outside a condo, provided he occupies it himself

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> Sentosa Cove is the enclave open even to non-PR foreigners (with LDAU approval), subject to a land-area cap of 1,800 sq metres. (B) Mainland landed approval generally requires 5-year PR status (and the mainland cap is 15,000 sq ft, not applicable to a non-PR here). (C) mixes up the unit: Sentosa's cap is 1,800 sqm, not 15,000 sq ft (that is the mainland figure). (D) strata landed outside a condo is restricted and not the route for a non-PR foreigner. 中文:非PR外国人最可能在圣淘沙湾获批,土地面积上限1,800平方米(本岛上限为15,000平方英尺)。
>
> 📎 Source: SLA Sentosa Cove conditions (https://ask.gov.sg/sla); RPA

---

**Q5.** After obtaining LDAU approval to buy a restricted bungalow on the mainland, an approved foreign owner is bound by which of the following conditions?

- A. He may rent out the property as long as he pays the rental income tax
- B. He must use the property for owner-occupation only and cannot dispose of it within 5 years
- C. He may sell the property at any time without restriction
- D. He may subdivide the land into two plots if each remains below 15,000 sq ft

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> Approved restricted purchases carry conditions: owner-occupation only (no renting), no disposal within the holding period (a minimum 5-year retention applies to approved purchases), no subdivision, and the mainland land area must not exceed 15,000 sq ft. (A) renting is prohibited. (C) there is a 5-year disposal restriction, so 'sell at any time' is wrong. (D) subdivision is not allowed. 中文:获批的受限制有地产业:仅自住、不得出租、5年内不得转让、不得分割。
>
> 📎 Source: SLA LDAU; RPA conditions on approved restricted purchases

---

**Q6.** A United States citizen (not a Singapore PR) buys his FIRST residential property in Singapore — a condominium unit. Which statement is correct regarding the RPA and ABSD position?

- A. He needs LDAU approval and pays 60% ABSD
- B. He needs no LDAU approval and pays 60% ABSD
- C. He needs no LDAU approval and, under the FTA, pays the same ABSD as a Singapore Citizen (0% on first property)
- D. He needs LDAU approval and pays 0% ABSD as a first-time buyer

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> A condo unit is non-restricted, so no LDAU approval is needed. Under the US-Singapore FTA, US citizens are accorded the same ABSD treatment as Singapore Citizens, so a first property attracts 0% ABSD (not the 60% foreigner rate that has applied since 27 April 2023). (A) and (D) wrongly require LDAU approval for a condo. (B) ignores the FTA exemption and applies 60%. This tests both the non-restricted nature of condos and the FTA carve-out. 中文:公寓非受限制无需LDAU批准;美国公民依FTA享公民待遇,首套ABSD为0%。
>
> 📎 Source: ABSD FTA exemption, IRAS; RPA distinction (figures vs approval)

---

**Q7.** Which of the following CANNOT be purchased freely by a foreigner without LDAU approval?

- A. A leasehold landed property with a remaining term of 6 years
- B. A commercial shophouse used for retail business
- C. A unit in a fully privatised Executive Condominium that obtained TOP 11 years ago
- D. A residential-use shophouse in a conservation area

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> A residential-use shophouse is a restricted property and requires LDAU approval. (A) a leasehold landed property for a term not exceeding 7 years (including renewal options) is non-restricted, so a 6-year term qualifies. (B) a commercial (non-residential) shophouse is freely purchasable. (C) a fully privatised EC (10+ years past TOP) is non-restricted and open to anyone. The trap is the commercial vs residential use of a shophouse. 中文:住宅用途店屋受限制;商业店屋、≤7年租约有地、私有化满10年EC均不受限。
>
> 📎 Source: SLA Foreign Ownership; RPA non-restricted list

---

**Q8.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: An EC at 'Parc Vista' obtained its TOP in 2014. In 2026 a foreigner (non-PR) approaches RES Jenny wanting to buy a resale unit there. What should Jenny advise?

- A. The foreigner can buy now, because by 2026 the EC is more than 10 years past TOP and has been fully privatised
- B. The foreigner cannot buy because ECs are always restricted to Singapore Citizens
- C. The foreigner can buy now only if he first obtains LDAU approval
- D. The foreigner can buy only after the 5-year MOP, which has not yet lapsed

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(hard)_
>
> ECs become fully privatised 10 years after TOP and are then open to all buyers including foreigners, with no LDAU approval needed. TOP 2014 plus 10 years means privatisation from 2024, so a 2026 purchase is allowed. (B) is wrong because ECs open up over time. (C) privatised ECs are non-restricted; no LDAU approval is required. (D) the 5-year MOP applies in years 0-5; by 2026 that lapsed long ago. 中文:EC在TOP满10年后私有化,任何人(含外国人)可买,无需LDAU批准。
>
> 📎 Source: EC foreigner eligibility timeline; HDB/SLA

---

**Q9.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY (same estate, different timing): Suppose instead 'Parc Vista' obtained TOP in 2019. In 2026 the same non-PR foreigner asks to buy a resale unit. What is the correct advice?

- A. He may buy now from the open market including foreigners
- B. He cannot buy now; only Singapore Citizens and SPRs may buy this EC on resale until it is fully privatised
- C. He may buy now provided he obtains LDAU approval first
- D. He cannot buy because the 5-year MOP has not yet lapsed

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> TOP 2019 means 2026 is in the 5-10 year window (years 5 to 10 after TOP): MOP has lapsed (so resale is allowed), but resale is restricted to Singapore Citizens and SPRs only; foreigners can buy only after the 10-year full privatisation (2029). (A) is premature. (C) ECs are not in the RPA restricted-approval regime; LDAU approval is not the mechanism. (D) MOP (5 years) lapsed in 2024, so this is wrong. 中文:TOP2019的EC在2026处于5-10年期,转售仅限公民和PR,外国人须等满10年私有化。
>
> 📎 Source: EC foreigner eligibility timeline (Yr 0-5 / 5-10 / 10+)

---

**Q10.** A foreigner submits an LDAU application to buy a restricted property. Which statement about the fee and timeline is correct?

- A. Application fee of $5,000 per property; processing about 14 working days
- B. Application fee of $1,220 per property; processing about 30 calendar days
- C. Application fee of $1,220 per property; processing about 30 working days
- D. No fee is payable; processing about 30 working days

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> The LDAU charges $1,220 per property and assessment typically takes about 30 WORKING days after all required documents and information are received. (B) uses calendar days instead of working days. (A) invents a $5,000 fee and wrong timeline. (D) wrongly says no fee. 中文:LDAU每宗产业收费$1,220,处理约30个工作日。
>
> 📎 Source: SLA LDAU fee and processing time

---

**Q11.** Which of the following is a RESTRICTED property requiring LDAU approval for a foreign buyer?

- A. A strata landed house within an approved condominium development
- B. A registered hotel
- C. An apartment in a high-rise private condominium
- D. A detached bungalow on a private plot of land

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(easy)_
>
> A detached bungalow (landed property) is restricted and needs LDAU approval. (A) strata landed WITHIN an approved condo is non-restricted. (B) registered hotels are non-restricted. (C) an apartment/condo unit is non-restricted. The recurring trap distinguishes strata landed inside vs outside a condo. 中文:独立洋房(有地)受限制;公寓单位、酒店、公寓内的分层有地住宅不受限制。
>
> 📎 Source: RPA / SLA restricted vs non-restricted

---

**Q12.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Mr Kim is a Singapore PR of 3 years. He is buying his FIRST Singapore property — a private condominium unit — for $1,500,000. His RES asks you to confirm the position. Which is correct?

- A. He needs no LDAU approval (a condo is non-restricted) and pays 5% ABSD as an SPR first property
- B. He needs LDAU approval (PR under 5 years) and pays 5% ABSD
- C. He needs no LDAU approval and pays 0% ABSD as a first-time buyer
- D. He needs LDAU approval and pays 60% ABSD as a foreigner

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(hard)_
>
> A condo unit is non-restricted, so the 5-year PR rule (which only governs LDAU approval for RESTRICTED landed property) is irrelevant here — no approval is needed. As an SPR buying his first residential property, ABSD is 5%. (B) and (D) wrongly impose LDAU approval on a condo. (C) confuses SC first-property (0%) with SPR first-property (5%). 中文:公寓非受限制无需批准;PR购首套住宅ABSD为5%。
>
> 📎 Source: RPA non-restricted list; ABSD for SPR; SLA

---

**Q13.** Which of these would a foreigner NEED LDAU approval to acquire?

- A. A purely industrial factory unit
- B. A serviced apartment building for residential use
- C. A commercial office unit
- D. A strata-titled retail shop

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> Serviced apartments/dormitories for residential use are restricted property requiring LDAU approval. (A) industrial property, (C) commercial office, and (D) retail shops are non-residential and freely purchasable by foreigners. The trap is recognising a serviced apartment as residential-use property. 中文:住宅用途的服务式公寓受限制需批准;工业、商业办公、零售店铺不受限制。
>
> 📎 Source: RPA restricted list; SLA

---

**Q14.** An approved foreign owner of a Sentosa Cove landed property asks his RES whether he can rent out the property while he works overseas for a year. What is the correct advice?

- A. Yes, rental is permitted at Sentosa Cove as there is no MOP there
- B. Yes, but only with fresh LDAU approval for each tenancy
- C. No, the property must be used for owner-occupation by him and his family only; it cannot be rented out
- D. No, but only because the 5-year mainland MOP applies to Sentosa Cove

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> All restricted properties bought with LDAU approval, including at Sentosa Cove, must be used solely for owner-occupation by the owner and family — rental is not allowed. (A) confuses the absence of a 5-year MOP at Sentosa with permission to rent; the no-rental condition still applies. (B) there is no per-tenancy approval because rental is simply not allowed. (D) the 5-year MOP is a mainland condition, not the reason here. 中文:圣淘沙湾受限制产业须自住,不得出租(尽管那里无5年MOP)。
>
> 📎 Source: RPA conditions; SLA Sentosa Cove (no rental, no MOP at Sentosa)

---

**Q15.** A foreigner is considering four shophouse-type or mixed properties. Which one can he buy WITHOUT LDAU approval?

- A. A shophouse approved for residential use upstairs and a shop below
- B. A mixed commercial-and-residential development unit
- C. A residential-use shophouse in a conservation district
- D. A commercial shophouse used entirely for office and retail use

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> A wholly commercial shophouse (non-residential) is non-restricted and freely purchasable. (A) and (C) involve residential use and are restricted. (B) mixed commercial-residential property is restricted because it includes a residential component. The exam trap is that any residential-use component triggers the restriction. 中文:纯商业用途店屋不受限制;含住宅用途的店屋或商住混合产业均受限制。
>
> 📎 Source: RPA non-restricted list; mixed-use distinction

---


## P1.9 Commercial & Industrial Property, URA Zoning, GST on Property

**Q1.** A buyer is comparing two purchases: a residential condominium unit and a commercial retail shop. Which statement correctly describes the GST treatment of these two transactions in 2026?

- A. The condominium sale is an exempt supply; the commercial shop sale is standard-rated at 9%
- B. Both are standard-rated at 9% because all property is taxable
- C. The condominium sale is standard-rated at 9%; the commercial shop is exempt
- D. Both are exempt supplies because they are sales of immovable property

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> Under the GST Act, the sale and lease of residential property is an EXEMPT supply, while commercial and industrial property is standard-rated at 9% (GST rate since 1 Jan 2024, unchanged in 2026). Option B is wrong because not all property is taxable - residential is exempt. Option C reverses the correct treatment. Option D is wrong because commercial property is taxable, not exempt. 中文:住宅买卖免征GST,商业/工业物业则标准税率9%征收。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS Real Estate GST guide; FACT PACK GST section (current as of June 2026)

---

**Q2.** An investor wants to buy a property in a B2-zoned industrial estate and use part of it as a corporate office and showroom for the manufacturing business operated there. Which constraint must he satisfy?

- A. At least 40% must be core industrial, with up to 60% for ancillary office use
- B. At least 60% of the Gross Floor Area must be core industrial activity, with no more than 40% for ancillary uses such as office and showroom
- C. The entire GFA may be used as office because B2 zoning permits commercial use
- D. He may convert up to 50% of GFA to residential staff quarters

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> The URA 60:40 rule requires a minimum 60% of GFA for core industrial activity and a maximum 40% for ancillary uses (office, showroom, canteen) supporting the industrial operation. Option A reverses the ratio. Option C is wrong - B2 is industrial zoning, not commercial; office is only allowed as ancillary use. Option D is wrong because no residential use is permitted in industrial zones. 中文:工业用地60:40规则—至少60%核心工业用途,最多40%辅助办公/展厅,且不得作住宅。
>
> 📎 Source: URA industrial zoning guidelines; FACT PACK Commercial & Industrial section

---

**Q3.** A light-industry tenant requiring a clean, low-nuisance environment is choosing between a B1 and a B2 industrial unit. Which is the BEST description of the difference relevant to nuisance buffering?

- A. B1 is for heavy industry with a 50m buffer; B2 is for light industry with a 100m buffer
- B. Both B1 and B2 require the same 100m buffer regardless of activity intensity
- C. B1 is for light/clean industry with up to a 50m nuisance buffer; B2 is for heavier industry with up to a 100m buffer
- D. B1 requires no buffer; B2 requires a 60m buffer

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> B1 is for light, clean industry requiring a nuisance buffer of up to 50m; B2 is for heavier industry (greater noise/emissions) requiring up to a 100m buffer. Option A reverses light/heavy. Option B wrongly equalises the buffers. Option D states incorrect buffer figures. 中文:B1轻工业50米缓冲,B2重工业100米缓冲。
>
> 📎 Source: URA/NEA industrial buffer guidelines; FACT PACK

---

**Q4.** A developer is assessing a commercial site of 2,000 sqm with a Gross Plot Ratio (GPR) of 3.5 in the Master Plan. What is the maximum Gross Floor Area (GFA) permitted, ignoring height limits?

- A. 571 sqm
- B. 5,000 sqm
- C. 2,000 sqm
- D. 7,000 sqm

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(easy)_
>
> GPR = GFA / Site Area, so maximum GFA = GPR x Site Area = 3.5 x 2,000 = 7,000 sqm. Option A wrongly divides site area by GPR (2,000/3.5). Option B is an arbitrary figure. Option D ignores the GPR entirely. 中文:GFA = 容积率 x 地块面积 = 3.5 x 2,000 = 7,000平方米。
>
> 📎 Source: URA Master Plan / GPR guidelines; FACT PACK URA Zoning section

---

**Q5.** A GST-registered landlord leases out a furnished residential apartment, including a built-in kitchen cabinet (a fixture) and a free-standing sofa and refrigerator (movable furniture). How is GST applied?

- A. GST at 9% on the portion attributable to the movable furniture/fittings; the residential property and its fixtures remain exempt
- B. No GST at all because it is residential property
- C. GST at 9% on the entire rental because the unit is furnished
- D. GST at 9% only on the built-in kitchen cabinet

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> Residential property and its fixtures (e.g., built-in cabinets) are exempt, but GST applies to the portion attributable to movable furniture/fittings (sofa, fridge). Option C wrongly taxes the whole rent. Option B ignores the taxable movable items. Option D taxes the fixture (cabinet), which actually remains exempt with the property, and ignores the movables. 中文:住宅物业及固定装置免GST,但可移动家具/设备部分须征9% GST。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS GST on residential furniture/fixtures; FACT PACK GST section

---

**Q6.** A foreign individual (non-PR) wishes to buy each of the following without any LDAU approval. Which acquisition is NOT permitted without approval?

- A. A strata-titled office unit in a commercial building
- B. A bungalow (landed residential) on mainland Singapore
- C. A commercial shophouse used wholly for retail
- D. An industrial factory unit in a B2 estate

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> Under the Residential Property Act, landed residential property such as a mainland bungalow is restricted - a foreigner needs LDAU approval (typically requiring PR status of at least 5 years and exceptional economic contribution). Commercial office units, industrial units, and commercial-use shophouses are non-restricted, so foreigners may buy freely. 中文:外国人可自由购买商业/工业物业,但购买有地住宅(如洋房)需LDAU批准。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK Foreign Ownership / Commercial property; Residential Property Act 1976

---

**Q7.** A company buys a commercial (non-residential) office unit at a market value of $2,000,000. Using the non-residential BSD schedule, what is the Buyer's Stamp Duty payable (ignore GST and ABSD)?

- A. $64,600
- B. $74,600
- C. $69,600
- D. $60,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> Non-residential BSD on $2,000,000: 1% x 180,000 = 1,800; 2% x 180,000 = 3,600; 3% x 640,000 = 19,200; 4% x 500,000 = 20,000 (bringing the total to the $1.5m mark); then 5% x 500,000 = 25,000 on the portion from $1.5m to $2m. Total = 1,800 + 3,600 + 19,200 + 20,000 + 25,000 = $69,600. Non-residential has no 6% tier (that applies only to residential above $3m); its top marginal rate is 5% above $1.5m. Option A under-states the duty. Option C over-applies higher rates. Option D is a flat 3% estimate. 中文:非住宅BSD分级计算至$2m = $69,600(非住宅最高5%,无6%档)。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS BSD non-residential schedule (eff. 15 Feb 2023); FACT PACK BSD table

---

**Q8.** A tenant signs a 3-year commercial lease at $5,000 per month (signed in Singapore). What is the lease stamp duty payable?

- A. $240
- B. $144
- C. $180,000
- D. $720

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> For a lease of 4 years or less, stamp duty = 0.4% of total rent. Total rent = $5,000 x 12 x 3 = $180,000; 0.4% x 180,000 = $720. Option A applies only one year's rent. Option C is the total rent, not the duty. Option D ($144) corresponds to a smaller example ($36,000 rent). The Average Annual Rent ($60,000) exceeds $1,000, so the lease is not exempt. 中文:≤4年租约,印花税=0.4% x 总租金=0.4% x $180,000=$720。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS lease stamp duty formula; FACT PACK Lease Stamp Duty section

---

**Q9.** An SME leases a JTC industrial unit and wants to sublet part of the floor space to an affiliated company. What must it do first?

- A. Obtain prior written approval from JTC before subletting
- B. Nothing - subletting of JTC units is automatically allowed
- C. Apply to URA for change of use
- D. Register the sublease as a fresh 30+30 year lease with SLA

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> JTC industrial leases (typically 30+30 years) require prior written JTC approval before subletting; subletting without JTC's consent is a breach that can lead to higher sublet fees or termination of the lease. Option B is wrong - subletting is not automatic. Option C confuses subletting with change of use (a URA matter, not triggered by subletting within the same industrial use). Option D invents a registration requirement. 中文:转租JTC工业单位须事先取得JTC书面批准。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK JTC leasehold / industrial section

---

**Q10.** Which statement BEST describes the URA Master Plan?

- A. A non-statutory aspirational plan reviewed every 30 years covering a 50-year horizon
- B. A statutory land-use plan reviewed roughly every 5 years that sets zoning and intensity (GPR and height) for a 10-15 year horizon
- C. A plan that only governs residential land and excludes commercial/industrial zoning
- D. A plan administered by JTC that allocates only industrial land

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> The Master Plan is a statutory land-use plan reviewed about every 5 years, guiding development over a 10-15 year horizon and setting zoning plus intensity (GPR and height). Option A describes something closer to the broader Concept Plan and is otherwise inaccurate. Option C wrongly restricts it to residential. Option D wrongly attributes it to JTC - URA administers the Master Plan. 中文:总蓝图是法定土地用途规划,约每5年检讨,设定分区与发展强度(容积率/高度)。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK URA Master Plan section

---

**Q11.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Meridian Pte Ltd, a GST-registered company, agrees to buy a commercial retail unit from a GST-registered seller. The price is $1,500,000 (exclusive of GST) and equals market value. Question 1: What is the total GST chargeable on this sale?

- A. $0 because the buyer is GST-registered
- B. $120,000
- C. $135,000
- D. $45,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> Commercial property is a standard-rated supply, so GST at 9% applies: 9% x $1,500,000 = $135,000 (the buyer may later claim input tax if conditions are met, but GST is still charged). Option A is wrong - registration does not make the supply zero-rated; GST is still charged. Option C uses 8% (the old rate). Option D uses 3%. 中文:商业物业标准税率,GST = 9% x $1,500,000 = $135,000(买方GST注册不改变须先征收)。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS GST; FACT PACK GST section (2026)

---

**Q12.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY (continued): For the same $1,500,000 commercial retail unit (price equals market value), Question 2: What is the Buyer's Stamp Duty payable by Meridian Pte Ltd?

- A. $65,000
- B. $32,600
- C. $49,600
- D. $44,600

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> Non-residential BSD on $1,500,000: 1% x 180,000 = 1,800; 2% x 180,000 = 3,600; 3% x 640,000 = 19,200; 4% x 500,000 = 20,000. Total = $44,600. The 5% tier begins only ABOVE $1.5m for non-residential, so at exactly $1.5m it does not apply. Option B ($32,600) is the BSD on $1.2m. Option C wrongly applies a 5% tier. Option A applies ABSD-style rates - ABSD does NOT apply to commercial property. 中文:非住宅BSD($1.5m)= $44,600;商业物业不征ABSD。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS BSD non-residential schedule; FACT PACK BSD section

---

**Q13.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY (continued): Meridian Pte Ltd's sole director is a foreign national (non-PR). Question 3: Which statement is correct about this commercial purchase?

- A. No LDAU approval is needed because commercial property is non-restricted under the Residential Property Act
- B. The purchase requires LDAU approval because a foreigner controls the company
- C. ABSD at 65% applies because the buyer is an entity
- D. The purchase is prohibited unless the director becomes a PR for 5 years

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> Commercial property is non-restricted under the Residential Property Act, so neither foreign individuals nor foreign-controlled entities need LDAU approval to buy it. Option B wrongly imports residential restrictions. Option C is wrong - ABSD applies to RESIDENTIAL property only, not commercial (and even the entity ABSD rate of 65% would not apply here). Option D applies the LDAU criteria (PR 5 years) that govern restricted residential property, not commercial. 中文:商业物业不受限,外资公司无需LDAU批准;ABSD仅适用住宅,不适用商业。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK Foreign Ownership + Commercial/GST sections

---

**Q14.** A salesperson tells a client that a high plot ratio guarantees the client can build a taller building than a neighbouring plot. What is the BEST correction?

- A. The statement is correct - plot ratio and building height are the same control
- B. Plot ratio governs floor area intensity, while building height is a separate control; a high GPR does not by itself guarantee greater height
- C. Plot ratio applies only to residential land, so it is irrelevant for commercial plots
- D. Building height is set solely by the developer, not by URA

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> GPR (floor area intensity) and building height are distinct planning controls; a high GPR does not automatically permit greater height, which is governed by a separate height limit (e.g., storey-height controls or aviation/technical height constraints). Option A conflates two separate controls (a classic exam trap). Option C wrongly limits GPR to residential land. Option D is wrong - URA sets height controls, not the developer. 中文:容积率(楼面强度)与建筑高度是两个独立管制;高容积率不等于可建更高建筑。
>
> 📎 Source: FACT PACK URA Zoning - Master Plan controls (common exam trap)

---

**Q15.** An investor sells an industrial factory unit 18 months after acquiring it (acquired in 2024). What Seller's Stamp Duty applies, and on what base?

- A. 8% of the higher of price or market value, under the residential SSD schedule
- B. 15% of the higher of price or market value, under the industrial SSD schedule
- C. 10% of the higher of price or market value, under the industrial SSD schedule
- D. 0% because SSD does not apply to industrial property

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> Industrial property (acquired on/after 12 Jan 2013) has its own SSD schedule: 15% (holding up to 1 year), 10% (more than 1 up to 2 years), 5% (more than 2 up to 3 years), 0% (more than 3 years), charged on the HIGHER of price or market value. An 18-month holding falls in the >1-2 year band = 10%. Option A applies the residential schedule (wrong asset type). Option B applies the up-to-1-year rate (15%), but 18 months is past 1 year. Option D is wrong - SSD does apply to industrial property. 中文:工业物业SSD按持有期15/10/5/0%计;持有18个月属>1-2年档,税率10%(取价格或市值较高者)。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS SSD industrial schedule (acquired on/after 12 Jan 2013); FACT PACK SSD section

---


## P1.10 Financing: LTV, TDSR, MSR, Loan Types & Cooling Measures

**Q1.** Mr Tan is taking out his FIRST housing loan from a bank to buy a private condominium. The loan tenure is 25 years and will be fully repaid before he turns 65. What is the maximum Loan-to-Value (LTV) ratio he can obtain?

- A. 55%
- B. 65%
- C. 80%
- D. 75%

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(easy)_
>
> For a first housing loan from a financial institution, the maximum LTV is 75% PROVIDED the tenure is ≤30 years AND the loan does not extend beyond the borrower's age 65 — both conditions are met here. 55% applies only when those conditions are NOT met (tenure >30yr or extends beyond age 65). 65% is not an LTV tier (a distractor). 80% was the old HDB concessionary loan limit, cut to 75% on 20 Aug 2024, and never applied to bank loans. 中文：首贷且年限≤30年、不超65岁，最高LTV为75%。
>
> 📎 Source: MAS Rules for New Housing Loans (LTV limits)

---

**Q2.** Mdm Lim already has ONE outstanding housing loan. She now wants a SECOND bank housing loan with a 35-year tenure that will extend beyond her age 65. What is the maximum LTV she can obtain, and what is the minimum cash downpayment?

- A. 25% LTV; 25% cash
- B. 45% LTV; 25% cash
- C. 45% LTV; 5% cash
- D. 35% LTV; 10% cash

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> A second housing loan normally has an LTV cap of 45%, but because the tenure exceeds 30 years AND extends beyond age 65, the LTV drops to 25%. The minimum cash downpayment for a 2nd (or 3rd+) loan is 25%. So 25% LTV with 25% cash. '45% LTV; 5% cash' confuses the first-loan cash rule. '45% LTV; 25% cash' ignores the tenure/age penalty. '35% LTV; 10% cash' mixes the 3rd-loan tier with the wrong cash figure. 中文：第二贷且超条件，LTV降至25%，现金首付最低25%。
>
> 📎 Source: MAS LTV limits for second housing loans

---

**Q3.** Which financing rule applies ONLY to HDB flats and Executive Condominiums bought directly from a developer — and NOT to private resale property?

- A. TDSR of 55%
- B. MSR of 30%
- C. LTV of 75%
- D. Stress-test floor of 4.0%

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> The Mortgage Servicing Ratio (MSR) of 30% of gross monthly income applies ONLY to HDB flats and ECs purchased from a developer. TDSR (55%), the 75% first-loan LTV cap, and the 4.0% residential stress-test floor all apply to ALL residential property loans including private resale. A common trap is to think MSR applies broadly — it does not. 中文：MSR 30%仅适用于HDB及发展商EC，不适用于私宅转售。
>
> 📎 Source: MAS MSR and TDSR Rules

---

**Q4.** Mr and Mrs Ng have a combined gross monthly income of $10,000. They have a car loan of $800/month and a personal loan of $400/month. They are buying a private condo. Using the TDSR limit of 55%, what is the MAXIMUM monthly amount available for their new property loan repayment?

- A. $3,300
- B. $5,500
- C. $4,300
- D. $6,700

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> TDSR caps TOTAL monthly debt at 55% of gross income: 55% × $10,000 = $5,500. Existing debts ($800 + $400 = $1,200) are deducted: $5,500 − $1,200 = $4,300 available for the new property loan. $3,300 wrongly uses 30% (MSR, which doesn't apply to private property). $5,500 forgets to subtract existing debts. $6,700 adds rather than subtracts the debts. 中文：55%×10000=5500，减去现有债务1200，余下4300。
>
> 📎 Source: MAS TDSR computation (55% limit)

---

**Q5.** Since 30 September 2022, when computing TDSR and MSR for a RESIDENTIAL property loan, banks must apply a stress-test (medium-term) interest rate floor of:

- A. 3.5% p.a. or actual, whichever is higher
- B. The prevailing board rate only
- C. 5.0% p.a. or actual, whichever is higher
- D. 4.0% p.a. or actual, whichever is higher

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> For residential property the stress-test floor is 4.0% p.a. (or the actual rate, whichever is higher). 3.5% was the earlier floor before it was raised. 5.0% is the floor for NON-residential property, not residential — a classic trap. Using only the prevailing rate ignores the regulatory floor entirely. 中文：住宅贷款压力测试下限为4.0%（或实际利率较高者）。
>
> 📎 Source: MAS stress-test floor (4.0% residential, since 30 Sep 2022)

---

**Q6.** With effect from 20 August 2024, the maximum LTV ratio for an HDB concessionary (HDB-granted) housing loan is:

- A. 75%
- B. 85%
- C. 80%
- D. 90%

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> On 20 Aug 2024 the HDB concessionary loan LTV was cut from 80% to 75%, aligning it with the bank-loan first-loan cap. 90% and 85% have never been current HDB-loan LTV limits. 80% is the OLD figure before the August 2024 cooling measure — the most tempting distractor for candidates not tracking the change. 中文：2024年8月20日起，HDB优惠贷款LTV从80%降至75%。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB / MND cooling measures, 20 Aug 2024

---

**Q7.** A buyer takes an HDB CONCESSIONARY loan at the maximum 75% LTV. Regarding the 25% downpayment, which statement is correct?

- A. The full 25% must be paid in cash
- B. No mandatory cash component — CPF Ordinary Account savings may be used
- C. A minimum 5% must be in cash; the rest may be CPF
- D. At least 10% must be in cash because the LTV is below 80%

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> For an HDB concessionary loan there is NO mandatory cash downpayment — the 25% may be paid fully from CPF Ordinary Account savings (subject to availability). This differs from bank loans, which require minimum cash (5% at 75% LTV). 'Full 25% cash' and the '5%/10% cash' options describe bank-loan rules, not HDB-loan rules. 中文：HDB优惠贷款无强制现金首付，25%可全部用CPF。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB concessionary loan downpayment rules

---

**Q8.** Which of the following is the correct maximum loan TENURE in each case?

- A. Private bank loan 30 years; HDB bank loan 35 years
- B. Private bank loan 25 years; HDB concessionary loan 30 years
- C. Private bank loan 35 years; HDB concessionary loan 25 years
- D. All housing loans capped at 35 years regardless of property type

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> Maximum tenures: private property bank loan = 35 years; HDB flat bank loan = 30 years; HDB concessionary loan = 25 years. Option A swaps the private and HDB figures. Option C understates the private cap and overstates the HDB concessionary cap. Option D wrongly applies one cap to all. Note that exceeding the relevant tenure threshold (30yr private / 25yr HDB) also triggers the lower LTV. 中文：私宅银行贷35年，HDB银行贷30年，HDB优惠贷25年。
>
> 📎 Source: MAS / HDB loan tenure caps

---
