**Q9.** A buyer purchasing an HDB flat with a bank loan has gross monthly income of $6,000 and an existing car loan of $500/month. The loan must satisfy BOTH MSR (30%) and TDSR (55%). What is the maximum monthly amount available for the new HDB mortgage?

- A. $1,300
- B. $2,800
- C. $3,300
- D. $1,800

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> For an HDB flat both limits apply, and the loan must satisfy the MORE restrictive one. MSR: 30% × $6,000 = $1,800 (MSR counts only the property loan, not other debts). TDSR: 55% × $6,000 = $3,300, minus the $500 car loan = $2,800 available. The binding (lower) figure is $1,800. $2,800 is the TDSR-only result (ignores MSR). $3,300 is gross TDSR before deducting debt. $1,300 wrongly subtracts the car loan from the MSR figure (MSR excludes non-property debt). 中文：HDB同时受MSR与TDSR限制，取较低者：MSR 1800 < TDSR 2800，故为1800。
>
> 📎 Source: MAS MSR (30%) and TDSR (55%) — lower of the two binds

---

**Q10.** Regarding CPF usage for housing, which statement about the Withdrawal Limit (WL) is CORRECT?

- A. The WL is 120% of the Valuation Limit and applies to PRIVATE property only
- B. The WL is 100% of the purchase price and applies to all property
- C. The WL is 120% of the Valuation Limit and applies equally to HDB flats
- D. HDB flats have a WL of 150% of the Valuation Limit

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> The Withdrawal Limit is 120% of the Valuation Limit (VL) and is an absolute CPF cap that applies to PRIVATE property only. HDB flats have NO Withdrawal Limit — a common trap. The WL is not based on purchase price (that's part of the VL definition), and there is no 150% WL for HDB. To use CPF beyond 100% VL up to the WL, members aged 55+ must set aside the Basic Retirement Sum. 中文：WL=120%×VL，仅适用于私宅；HDB无WL。
>
> 📎 Source: CPF Withdrawal Limit / Valuation Limit rules

---

**Q11.** A 56-year-old SC buys a private resale condo. The CPF Valuation Limit is $1,000,000 and he wishes to use CPF up to the Withdrawal Limit. Which statement is correct about using CPF beyond 100% of the VL?

- A. He can use unlimited CPF because he is over 55
- B. He can use CPF up to $1,200,000 only if he has set aside the Basic Retirement Sum
- C. He cannot use any CPF beyond $1,000,000 under any circumstances
- D. The Withdrawal Limit for him is $1,500,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> The Withdrawal Limit is 120% of VL = $1,200,000 for this private property. Because he is 55+, to use CPF beyond 100% of VL ($1,000,000) up to the WL ($1,200,000) he must FIRST set aside the Basic Retirement Sum in his CPF. So B is correct. He cannot use 'unlimited' CPF (the 120% cap is absolute for private property). It is not true that no CPF can be used beyond VL — it can, up to the WL with the BRS condition. $1,500,000 is 150%, not the correct 120% WL. 中文：私宅WL=120%×VL=120万；55岁以上超100%VL需先留下BRS。
>
> 📎 Source: CPF WL (120% VL) + BRS set-aside for members 55+; 2026 BRS $110,200

---

**Q12.** When using CPF to buy a property, full CPF can be used (no pro-ration) only if the remaining lease meets which condition?

- A. Remaining lease ≥30 years regardless of buyer's age
- B. Remaining lease ≥60 years for any buyer
- C. Remaining lease ≥20 years AND it covers the youngest buyer until age 95
- D. Any remaining lease above 0 years, with no age condition

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> Full CPF (no pro-ration) is allowed only if the remaining lease is at least 20 years AND covers the youngest buyer to age 95; otherwise CPF is pro-rated, and there is NO CPF at all if the remaining lease is 20 years or less. The 30-year and 60-year options use incorrect thresholds. The 'any lease, no age condition' option ignores both the 20-year floor and the age-95 coverage rule. 中文：剩余地契≥20年且覆盖最年轻买家至95岁，才可全额CPF。
>
> 📎 Source: CPF housing lease-coverage rules

---

**Q13.** A Singapore Citizen who currently owns ONE residential property buys a SECOND residential property. What ABSD rate applies (2026 rates)?

- A. 0%
- B. 12%
- C. 17%
- D. 20%

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> Under the rates effective 27 Apr 2023 (unchanged in 2026), a Singapore Citizen pays 0% on the 1st residential property, 20% on the 2nd, and 30% on the 3rd and subsequent. So the 2nd property attracts 20%. 0% is the 1st-property rate. 12% and 17% are OUTDATED SC second-property rates from earlier ABSD revisions — strong traps for candidates relying on older material. 中文：SC第二套住宅ABSD为20%（现行）。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS ABSD rates (effective 27 Apr 2023, current 2026)

---

**Q14.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY — The Wong family: Mr Wong (Singapore Citizen) and his wife (Singapore PR) jointly buy a $2,000,000 condominium as their first property together. Both are co-owners; this is Mr Wong's first property and his wife's first property. Under the joint-ownership ABSD rule (the HIGHER applicable profile applies), what ABSD rate is charged on the full purchase price?

- A. 5% (the SPR first-property rate)
- B. 0% (because at least one owner is an SC buying his first property)
- C. 2.5% (averaged between SC and SPR)
- D. 20% (the SC second-property rate)

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(hard)_
>
> When buyers of different profiles purchase jointly, ABSD is charged at the HIGHEST applicable rate among the owners. Here the SPR wife's first-property rate is 5%, which is higher than the SC's 0% — so 5% applies to the entire price. ABSD is NOT averaged (so 2.5% is wrong), and it is not reduced to 0% just because one owner is SC. 20% is the SC second-property rate, irrelevant here as both are first-time buyers. (A married SC+SPR couple may later claim ABSD refund only on a SECOND property if conditions are met — not applicable to a single first purchase.) 中文：联名购买取最高适用ABSD，SPR首套为5%，故全额按5%。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS ABSD — joint purchase highest-profile rule (SPR 1st = 5%)

---

**Q15.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY — Investor scenario: Mr Rajan, a Singapore Citizen, buys a residential property as an investment for $1,200,000 (market value $1,200,000). It is his SECOND residential property. He must pay both Buyer's Stamp Duty (BSD) and ABSD. What is his TOTAL stamp duty payable?

- A. $32,600
- B. $272,600
- C. $240,000
- D. $259,200

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> BSD on $1.2m residential (rates from 15 Feb 2023, current 2026): 1%×180k + 2%×180k + 3%×640k + 4%×200k = $1,800 + $3,600 + $19,200 + $8,000 = $32,600. ABSD for an SC's 2nd property = 20% × $1,200,000 = $240,000. Total = $32,600 + $240,000 = $272,600. $32,600 is BSD only (forgets ABSD). $240,000 is ABSD only (forgets BSD). $259,200 wrongly applies a flat ~3% BSD plus a miscalculated ABSD. 中文：BSD 32,600 + ABSD(20%)240,000 = 272,600。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS BSD schedule + ABSD (SC 2nd = 20%), 2026

---


## P1.11 Stamp Duties: BSD, ABSD, SSD (current rates + calculation)

**Q1.** A Singapore Citizen buying his very first residential property, a Singapore Permanent Resident buying her first residential property, and a foreigner buying his first residential property each purchase an identical $1,200,000 condominium unit. How does the Buyer's Stamp Duty (BSD) payable by the three buyers compare?

- A. The foreigner pays the most because BSD increases with foreign status
- B. The SC pays the least, the PR pays more, and the foreigner pays the most
- C. All three pay exactly the same BSD amount
- D. The SC pays nothing because it is his first property

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(easy)_
>
> BSD is buyer-profile-independent: it is computed solely on the price or market value (whichever higher) and does not vary by citizenship or number of properties owned. All three pay the same BSD of $32,600 on $1.2m. It is ABSD, not BSD, that depends on citizenship and property count. B and A wrongly attribute citizenship-based scaling to BSD (that is ABSD). D confuses the first-property ABSD position for SCs (ABSD 0%) with BSD, which is always payable. 中文: BSD 只看价格不看买家身份，三人相同；按身份递增的是 ABSD。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS Buyer's Stamp Duty (BSD): https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/buying-or-acquiring-property/buyer's-stamp-duty-(bsd)

---

**Q2.** A buyer purchases a residential property for $1,200,000, which is also its market value. Using the BSD rates effective 15 Feb 2023, what is the Buyer's Stamp Duty payable?

- A. $30,000
- B. $36,000
- C. $33,600
- D. $32,600

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> Tiered: 1% x $180,000 = $1,800; 2% x $180,000 = $3,600; 3% x $640,000 = $19,200 (brings cumulative to $1m); 4% x $200,000 = $8,000 (the portion from $1m to $1.2m). Total = $1,800 + $3,600 + $19,200 + $8,000 = $32,600. A ($30,000) wrongly applies a flat 2.5%. C ($33,600) double-counts a tier. D ($36,000) wrongly applies a flat 3% to the whole price. 中文: 分级计算得 $32,600；其他选项误用统一税率或算错分层。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS BSD rate table (eff. 15 Feb 2023): https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/buying-or-acquiring-property/buyer's-stamp-duty-(bsd)

---

**Q3.** A Singapore Citizen who already owns one residential property signs an Option to Purchase for a second residential condominium at a price of $1,500,000, when the market value is $1,600,000. What ABSD rate applies, and on which amount is ABSD computed?

- A. 20% on $1,600,000
- B. 20% on $1,500,000
- C. 30% on $1,600,000
- D. 5% on $1,600,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> An SC buying a second residential property pays ABSD of 20%. Like BSD, ABSD is computed on the HIGHER of purchase price or market value, i.e. $1,600,000. A uses the correct rate but the wrong (lower) base. C uses the SC third-property rate of 30%. D uses the SPR first-property rate of 5%. 中文: 公民第二套 ABSD 为 20%，按价格与市值较高者 $160 万计。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS ABSD rates (eff. 27 Apr 2023): https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/buying-or-acquiring-property/additional-buyer's-stamp-duty-(absd)

---

**Q4.** A foreigner who owns no property anywhere purchases his first residential apartment in Singapore. What rate of Additional Buyer's Stamp Duty (ABSD) applies (ignoring any FTA relief)?

- A. 0%
- B. 60%
- C. 30%
- D. 65%

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> A foreigner pays 60% ABSD on ANY residential purchase, including the first, since 27 Apr 2023. A (0%) is the SC first-property rate. B (30%) is the SC third+ / SPR second-property rate, not foreigner. D (65%) is the entity/trustee rate, not an individual foreigner. 中文: 外国人买任何住宅 ABSD 均为 60%，首套也不例外。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS ABSD rates: https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/buying-or-acquiring-property/additional-buyer's-stamp-duty-(absd)

---

**Q5.** An American citizen who already owns two residential properties in Singapore signs an OTP to buy a third residential property under his sole name. Considering the Free Trade Agreement (FTA) ABSD remission, what ABSD rate applies?

- A. 60%, because he is a foreigner buying his third property
- B. 35%, because the FTA caps foreigners at the SPR third-property rate
- C. 30%, because he is afforded the same treatment as a Singapore Citizen
- D. 0%, because US citizens are exempt from all ABSD

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> Under the US-Singapore FTA, US citizens are accorded the same ABSD treatment as Singapore Citizens (0%/20%/30% for 1st/2nd/3rd+). His third property therefore attracts the SC third-property rate of 30%. A ignores the FTA relief. B wrongly applies the SPR rate (35% is the SPR third+ rate); the FTA gives SC-equivalent treatment, not SPR. D wrongly assumes blanket exemption; US citizens are treated as SCs, so they still pay 20%/30% on second/third properties. 中文: 美国公民按公民待遇，第三套 ABSD 为 30%（非全免）。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS Foreigners Eligible for ABSD Remission under FTAs: https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/appeals-refunds-reliefs-and-remissions/common-stamp-duty-remissions-and-reliefs-for-property/foreigners-eligible-for-absd-remission-under-free-trade-agreements-(ftas)

---

**Q6.** Which group of foreign nationals is NOT entitled to ABSD remission (same treatment as Singapore Citizens) under Singapore's Free Trade Agreements?

- A. Citizens and permanent residents of Switzerland
- B. Citizens and permanent residents of Norway
- C. Citizens of the United States
- D. Citizens of Australia

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> FTA ABSD relief covers nationals/PRs of Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway and Switzerland, plus US citizens. Australia is NOT on the list, so Australian citizens get no relief and pay full foreigner ABSD (60%). A, B and C are all covered groups and therefore wrong answers to a 'NOT entitled' stem. 中文: 享 FTA 减免的是美、冰岛、列支敦士登、挪威、瑞士；澳大利亚不在内。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS FTA ABSD Remission: https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/appeals-refunds-reliefs-and-remissions/common-stamp-duty-remissions-and-reliefs-for-property/foreigners-eligible-for-absd-remission-under-free-trade-agreements-(ftas)

---

**Q7.** A Singapore Citizen who already owns two residential properties buys a THIRD residential property for $2,000,000 (price equals market value). What is the total BSD plus ABSD payable?

- A. $669,600
- B. $600,000
- C. $69,600
- D. $632,600

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(hard)_
>
> BSD on $2m (tiered): 1% x $180,000 = $1,800; 2% x $180,000 = $3,600; 3% x $640,000 = $19,200 (to $1m); 4% x $500,000 = $20,000 (to $1.5m); 5% x $500,000 = $25,000 (to $2m). BSD = $69,600. ABSD for an SC buying a third property = 30% x $2,000,000 = $600,000. Total = $69,600 + $600,000 = $669,600. C is BSD only (ignores ABSD). B is ABSD only (ignores BSD). D understates: it pairs the $600,000 ABSD with a too-low BSD figure ($32,600 for a $1.2m property), failing to apply the 4% and 5% tiers to a $2m price. 中文: $2m 的 BSD 为 $69,600（含4%与5%分层），公民第三套 ABSD 30% = $600,000，合计 $669,600。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS BSD and ABSD tables: https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property

---

**Q8.** On which value are BSD, ABSD and SSD all assessed?

- A. Always the purchase price stated in the contract
- B. The HIGHER of the purchase price or the market value
- C. Always the market value as assessed by IRAS
- D. The LOWER of the purchase price or the market value

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> For BSD, ABSD and SSD, duty is computed on the higher of the purchase price (consideration) or the market value. This prevents under-declaration. A and B each ignore one of the two comparators. D inverts the rule (a classic trap) - using the lower value would understate duty. 中文: 三种印花税都按价格与市值较高者计算，不是较低者。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS Stamp Duty Basics for Property: https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/basics-of-stamp-duty-for-property/learning-the-basics-for-properties

---

**Q9.** A Singapore Citizen bought a residential property on 1 September 2025 and sells it on 1 December 2026, holding it for approximately 15 months. Under the SSD rules current in 2026, what SSD rate applies?

- A. 0%, because residential SSD no longer applies after one year
- B. 16%
- C. 12%
- D. 8%

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> The property was purchased on/after 4 Jul 2025, so the current 4-year SSD schedule applies: holding more than 1 year up to 2 years = 12%. A ~15-month hold falls in the >1 to 2 year tier. A wrongly assumes SSD ends after a year (it now runs four years). B (16%) is the up-to-1-year rate. D (8%) is the >2-3 year rate. 中文: 2025年7月4日后购入，持有约15个月属>1至2年，SSD 为 12%。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS SSD for Residential Property (purchases on/after 4 Jul 2025): https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/selling-or-disposing-property/seller's-stamp-duty-(ssd)-for-residential-property

---

**Q10.** Two sellers each held a residential property for exactly 3.5 years before selling. Seller X bought on 1 June 2025; Seller Y bought on 1 August 2025. What SSD rate applies to each on disposal?

- A. Both pay 0% because they each held for more than 3 years
- B. Both pay 4%
- C. X pays 4%; Y pays 0%
- D. X pays 0%; Y pays 4%

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> The applicable SSD regime is fixed by purchase date. Seller X bought before 4 Jul 2025 (prior 3-year regime: 12/8/4/0%), so holding 3.5 years (over 3 years) = 0%. Seller Y bought on/after 4 Jul 2025 (current 4-year regime: 16/12/8/4/0%), so 3.5 years falls in the >3 to 4 year tier = 4%. A wrongly applies the old 3-year cutoff to both. B applies the new regime to both. C reverses the two sellers. 中文: 旧制（4日前购）3年后免税；新制（4日起购）>3至4年仍 4%。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS SSD for Residential Property: https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/selling-or-disposing-property/seller's-stamp-duty-(ssd)-for-residential-property

---

**Q11.** A company (a non-individual entity) acquires its first residential property in Singapore for $5,000,000 (price equals market value) for redevelopment, and it is NOT a licensed housing developer. What ABSD rate applies to the entity?

- A. 65%
- B. 60%
- C. 35%
- D. 0%, because it is the entity's first residential property

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> An entity (non-individual) pays ABSD of 65% on any residential acquisition. A (35%) corresponds to the housing-developer remittable component, which applies only to licensed developers meeting conditions, not an ordinary company. B (60%) is the individual foreigner rate. D ignores that entities have no first-property exemption. 中文: 一般公司（非持牌发展商）买住宅 ABSD 为 65%，无首套豁免。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS ABSD rates: https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/buying-or-acquiring-property/additional-buyer's-stamp-duty-(absd)

---

**Q12.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Mr and Mrs Tan are a married couple. Mr Tan is a Singapore Citizen; Mrs Tan is a Singapore PR. The couple already owns one residential flat (their matrimonial home). They jointly buy a second residential condominium for $1,800,000 (market value $1,750,000). What ABSD rate applies to this joint purchase?

- A. 20%, because married couples are charged at the Singapore Citizen rate when at least one spouse is an SC
- B. 30%, because where co-owners have different profiles the HIGHEST applicable ABSD rate (here the SPR second-property rate) applies to the entire purchase
- C. 5%, because it is treated as the SPR first-property rate
- D. 0%, because at least one buyer is a Singapore Citizen

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> For a joint purchase by buyers of different profiles, the HIGHEST applicable ABSD rate applies on the entire value. Mr Tan (SC) buying a second property would attract 20%, but Mrs Tan (SPR) buying a second property attracts 30%; the higher rate, 30%, therefore applies to the whole $1,800,000 (the higher of price/value). A is the common trap: the lowest rate does NOT govern joint purchases - the highest does. C wrongly applies the SPR first-property rate (5%), but this is their second property. D wrongly assumes the SC profile zeroes the duty; the couple already owns a property, so this is a second property and the SC component alone would still be 20%, while the joint rate is 30%. (If they sell the first home within the prescribed timeline, they may apply for the married-couple ABSD remission to refund the ABSD paid.) 中文: 不同身份联名按较高税率计，PR第二套30%高于公民20%，故全额按30%。卖掉首套后可申请退税。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS ABSD - rates and remission for joint purchase by a married couple: https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/buying-or-acquiring-property/additional-buyer's-stamp-duty-(absd)

---

**Q13.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY (continued): The Tans complete the second condo and, within the prescribed timeline, sell their original flat. Both are named on the new property and at least one is a Singapore Citizen. What ABSD relief may they apply for, and what is its effect?

- A. No relief is available once ABSD has been paid
- B. A 50% reduction in the BSD payable on the second property
- C. Married-couple ABSD remission - a REFUND of the ABSD paid on the second property, provided the first is sold within the timeline and at least one buyer is a Singapore Citizen
- D. Automatic conversion of the second property to first-property ABSD with no application needed

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> The married-couple ABSD remission allows a refund of the ABSD paid on the second residential property if the couple sells their first residential property within the prescribed timeline (within 6 months of the purchase/completion of the second property, where the second was already completed) and at least one spouse is a Singapore Citizen - they must apply for it. A is wrong: relief by way of refund is precisely the mechanism. B confuses ABSD remission with BSD (BSD is not refunded this way). D is wrong: the remission is by application/refund, not automatic. 中文: 夫妻可在期限内卖掉首套后申请退还第二套已付的 ABSD（需至少一方为公民）。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS ABSD remission for married couples: https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/appeals-refunds-reliefs-and-remissions/common-stamp-duty-remissions-and-reliefs-for-property/remission-of-absd-for-a-married-couple

---

**Q14.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Mdm Lee, a Singapore Citizen, bought a residential property on 10 July 2025 for $1,000,000. Eight months later, due to relocation, she sells it for $1,100,000 (market value $1,080,000). What is her Seller's Stamp Duty payable?

- A. $132,000
- B. $0
- C. $172,800
- D. $176,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> Purchased on/after 4 Jul 2025, held only 8 months (within the first year), so the current top SSD rate of 16% applies. SSD is on the higher of price or market value = $1,100,000. 16% x $1,100,000 = $176,000. A applies 12% (the >1-2 year rate) - wrong tier. C applies 16% to the lower market value ($1,080,000) - SSD uses the higher value. B wrongly assumes no SSD; an 8-month hold is well within the 4-year SSD window. 中文: 持有8个月按16%，且按较高的 $110万计，SSD = $176,000。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS SSD for Residential Property: https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/selling-or-disposing-property/seller's-stamp-duty-(ssd)-for-residential-property

---

**Q15.** A buyer acquires an INDUSTRIAL (B2) property for $2,000,000 (price equals market value) and later disposes of it. Which statement about the stamp duties is CORRECT?

- A. For non-residential property, the BSD portion above $1.5m is charged at 5% (there is no 6% tier), and industrial SSD runs 15/10/5/0% over a 3-year holding period
- B. SSD on industrial property follows the residential 4-year schedule of 16/12/8/4%
- C. BSD has a 6% top tier on industrial property above $3m, just like residential
- D. No SSD applies to industrial property in any circumstance

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(hard)_
>
> Non-residential (including industrial) BSD tops out at 5% on the portion above $1.5m - there is no 6% tier (the 6% tier is residential only, on the portion above $3m). Industrial SSD (for property acquired on/after 12 Jan 2013) is 15%/10%/5%/0% over a 3-year holding period - distinct from the residential schedule and unaffected by the 4 Jul 2025 residential changes. C wrongly imports the residential 6% tier into non-residential. B wrongly applies the residential 4-year SSD schedule to industrial. D is wrong: industrial property does attract SSD if sold within 3 years. 中文: 非住宅 BSD 最高 5%（无 6%）；工业 SSD 为 15/10/5/0%、3年制。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS SSD for Industrial Property: https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/selling-or-disposing-property/seller's-stamp-duty-(ssd)-for-industrial-property

---


## P1.12 Property Tax, CPF for Property, Cooling-Measure Overview

**Q1.** A foreign investor buys a strata industrial (B1) unit and an adjoining piece of vacant commercial land. What property tax rate applies to these non-residential properties?

- A. The progressive owner-occupier residential rates (0%-32%)
- B. A flat 10% of the Annual Value (AV)
- C. A flat 12% of the AV
- D. The progressive non-owner-occupier residential rates (12%-36%)

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> Non-residential property (commercial, industrial) and land are taxed at a flat 10% of AV regardless of who owns or occupies them, including when vacant. A is wrong: owner-occupier progressive rates apply only to residential homes the owner lives in. C is wrong: 12% is the first-tier non-owner-occupier RESIDENTIAL rate, not the non-residential flat rate. D is wrong: the 12%-36% progressive scale is for non-owner-occupied RESIDENTIAL property, not commercial/industrial. 中文一句话：非住宅（商业、工业、土地）一律按年值的10%征收物业税。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS Property Tax Rates (non-residential/land = 10% flat AV)

---

**Q2.** Mr Tan lives in his condo with an Annual Value (AV) of $45,000. Using the owner-occupier rates effective 2025/2026, what is his annual property tax BEFORE any rebate?

- A. $1,800
- B. $1,720
- C. $1,420
- D. $2,700

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> Owner-occupier (eff. 1 Jan 2025): first $12,000 at 0% = $0; next $28,000 (>$12k-$40k) at 4% = $1,120; next $5,000 (>$40k-$45k, within the 6% band) at 6% = $300. Total = $1,120 + $300 = $1,420. B ($1,720) mis-bands the top portion. C ($1,800) wrongly applies 4% to the whole $45,000. D ($2,700) wrongly applies 6% flat. 中文一句话：自住分级计税——首1.2万0%、1.2万至4万部分4%、4万至4.5万部分6%，共$1,420。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS owner-occupier residential rates eff. 1 Jan 2025 (verified)

---

**Q3.** Ms Lim owns a second condo that she rents out entirely. Its AV is $48,000. Using the non-owner-occupier residential rates, what is the annual property tax?

- A. $13,440
- B. $5,760
- C. $4,320
- D. $6,900

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> Non-owner-occupier residential: first $30,000 at 12% = $3,600; next $15,000 (>$30k-$45k) at 20% = $3,000; next $3,000 (>$45k-$48k, within the 28% band) at 28% = $840. Total = $3,600 + $3,000 + $840 = $6,900. B applies 12% to the whole $48,000. C wrongly uses owner-occupier bands. A applies a flat 28%. 中文一句话：出租住宅（非自住）分级——首3万12%、3万至4.5万20%、4.5万至4.8万28%，共$6,900。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS non-owner-occupier residential rates eff. 1 Jan 2024

---

**Q4.** For Year 2026, which statement about the one-off property tax rebate for owner-occupiers is correct?

- A. Private residential owner-occupiers get a 10% rebate capped at $500; HDB owner-occupiers get a 15% rebate
- B. All owner-occupiers, HDB and private, get a flat 32% rebate with no cap
- C. Only non-owner-occupiers (landlords) qualify for the rebate
- D. The rebate is 15% for private and 10% for HDB, capped at $1,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> The 2026 one-off rebate is 15% for owner-occupied HDB flats and 10% for owner-occupied private residential properties, with the private rebate capped at $500. A states this correctly. B invents a 32% no-cap rebate (32% is the top marginal owner-occupier tax rate, not a rebate). C is wrong: rebates target owner-occupiers, not landlords. D swaps the HDB/private percentages and uses the wrong cap. 中文一句话：2026年自住回扣——组屋15%、私宅10%（上限$500）。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS 2026 property tax rebate (verified: 15% HDB / 10% private capped $500)

---

**Q5.** A landed home has an AV of $150,000 and is fully owner-occupied. What is the annual property tax (before rebate)?

- A. $48,000
- B. $22,220
- C. $24,360
- D. $33,560

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> Owner-occupier bands (eff. 1 Jan 2025): $12k@0%=$0; $28k@4%=$1,120; $10k@6%=$600; $25k@10%=$2,500; $10k@14%=$1,400; $15k@20%=$3,000; $40k@26%=$10,400; remaining $10k (>$140k)@32%=$3,200. Total = $1,120+$600+$2,500+$1,400+$3,000+$10,400+$3,200 = $22,220. B is correct. B ($48,000) wrongly applies a flat 32% to the whole AV. C ($24,360) and D ($33,560) result from mis-banding. 中文一句话：自住高额年值需逐级累加，AV $15万的物业税为$22,220，远低于按顶级32%平摊。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS owner-occupier rates eff. 1 Jan 2025

---

**Q6.** What does the CPF Valuation Limit (VL) for a property purchase refer to?

- A. The higher of the purchase price or market value
- B. 120% of the purchase price
- C. The lower of the purchase price or the market value of the property at the time of purchase
- D. The total CPF an owner has in their Ordinary Account

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(easy)_
>
> The VL is the lower of the purchase price or the market value at the time of purchase; CPF can be used up to 100% of the VL. B describes the Withdrawal Limit (120% of VL), not the VL, and uses purchase price rather than VL. A inverts the rule (it is the LOWER, not higher). D confuses VL with the member's OA balance. 中文一句话：估价限额（VL）= 购买价与市价中的较低者，可动用公积金至VL的100%。
>
> 📎 Source: CPF Valuation Limit / Withdrawal Limit rules

---

**Q7.** Mrs Goh is financing a private condominium with CPF. Which statement about the CPF Withdrawal Limit (WL) is correct?

- A. The WL is 120% of the market value at the time of sale
- B. The WL is 100% of the purchase price for all property types
- C. HDB flats are subject to the WL but private condos are not
- D. The WL is 120% of the Valuation Limit and applies to private property; HDB flats have no WL

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> The WL is 120% of the VL and is the absolute CPF cap for PRIVATE property; HDB flats have no WL (CPF can fund beyond the VL). To use CPF beyond 100% VL up to the WL, members 55+ must first set aside their BRS. B confuses WL with VL (100%). C reverses the rule—it is private property that has the WL, not HDB. D uses market value at sale rather than 120% of VL. 中文一句话：提款限额=估价限额的120%，仅适用于私宅；组屋无提款限额。
>
> 📎 Source: CPF Withdrawal Limit (120% VL, private only; HDB no WL)

---

**Q8.** Mr Raju buys a private apartment. The purchase price is $1,400,000 and the market value at purchase is $1,450,000. What is the maximum amount of CPF he may use over the life of the loan (the Withdrawal Limit)?

- A. $1,680,000
- B. $1,740,000
- C. $1,400,000
- D. $1,450,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(hard)_
>
> VL = lower of price or market value = $1,400,000. WL = 120% x VL = $1,680,000. A is correct. B uses 120% of the higher market value ($1,450,000), but VL uses the LOWER figure. C ($1,400,000) is the VL (100%), not the 120% WL. D is the market value, not a limit applied to CPF. 中文一句话：VL取较低的$140万，提款限额=120%×VL=$168万。
>
> 📎 Source: CPF Withdrawal Limit calculation (120% of VL)

---

**Q9.** A 60-year-old buyer (the youngest buyer) wants to use CPF for a resale flat with a remaining lease of 55 years. Which rule determines his CPF usage?

- A. CPF can always be used in full as long as any lease remains
- B. Full CPF is allowed only if the remaining lease is at least 20 years AND covers the youngest buyer to age 95; otherwise CPF is pro-rated, and none is allowed if remaining lease is under 20 years
- C. CPF usage depends only on the buyer's CPF balance, not the lease
- D. No CPF can be used for any resale flat with a lease under 99 years

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> CPF rules: full usage if remaining lease is at least 20 years AND it covers the youngest buyer to age 95; otherwise pro-rated; no CPF at all if remaining lease is under 20 years. B states this. B ignores the age-95/20-year conditions. C ignores the lease coverage requirement entirely. D is false—CPF is widely used for 99-year leasehold flats. 中文一句话：剩余地契≥20年且能覆盖最年轻买家至95岁才可全额用公积金，否则按比例，少于20年不可用。
>
> 📎 Source: CPF lease-coverage rules for property purchase

---

**Q10.** For a CPF member turning 55 in 2026, what is the Basic Retirement Sum (BRS) and Full Retirement Sum (FRS)?

- A. BRS $220,400 and FRS $440,800
- B. BRS $106,500 and FRS $213,000
- C. BRS $110,200 and FRS $220,400
- D. BRS $96,000 and FRS $192,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(easy)_
>
> For the 2026 cohort, BRS = $110,200 and FRS = $220,400 (FRS is twice BRS); ERS = $440,800. C is correct. B is the 2025 cohort's figures. A wrongly shifts the values up one tier (those are FRS and ERS). D uses outdated figures. 中文一句话：2026年满55岁——BRS $110,200，FRS $220,400（FRS为BRS两倍）。
>
> 📎 Source: CPF Retirement Sums 2026 (verified: BRS $110,200 / FRS $220,400 / ERS $440,800)

---

**Q11.** Which statement about Singapore's property cooling measures is correct?

- A. SSD applies to a buyer at the point of purchase
- B. Both BSD and ABSD vary according to the buyer's citizenship
- C. ABSD applies to both residential and non-residential property
- D. Buyer's Stamp Duty (BSD) is the same regardless of the buyer's citizenship or how many properties they own, while ABSD depends on citizenship and property count

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> BSD is buyer-profile-independent (based only on price/value tiers), whereas ABSD depends on citizenship/residency status and the number of residential properties owned. D is correct. B is wrong—BSD does not vary by citizenship. C is wrong—ABSD applies to residential property only. A is wrong—SSD is a SELLER's stamp duty levied on disposal within the holding period, not on a buyer at purchase. 中文一句话：BSD不分买家身份，ABSD按身份与房产数量；ABSD仅住宅，SSD是卖方在持有期内出售时缴。
>
> 📎 Source: Common exam trap: BSD profile-independent vs ABSD citizenship-based; cooling measures overview

---

**Q12.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: A Singapore Citizen couple already owns one HDB flat. They jointly purchase a second private condo for $1,800,000 (market value $1,750,000), holding it as joint tenants. Before any married-couple remission, what ABSD applies to this purchase?

- A. 20% ABSD on $1,800,000 (the higher of price or market value), as it is a second residential property for SCs
- B. 5% ABSD, the SPR first-property rate
- C. 30% ABSD, the SC third-property rate
- D. No ABSD, because the first property is an HDB flat

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(hard)_
>
> For Singapore Citizens, the second residential property attracts 20% ABSD (rate unchanged since 27 Apr 2023), charged on the HIGHER of price or market value = $1,800,000. A is correct. B applies the SPR (not SC) first-property rate. C is the SC THIRD-property rate (30%), but this is only their second. D is wrong—an HDB flat still counts as a residential property owned, so the condo is a second property attracting ABSD. 中文一句话：新加坡公民第二套住宅ABSD为20%，按价与市价较高者（$180万）计算；组屋仍算一套。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS ABSD rates eff. 27 Apr 2023 (verified unchanged 2026)

---

**Q13.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY (continued): The SC couple bought the condo on 1 March 2026 for $1,800,000. Due to a job relocation, they sell it on 1 June 2027 (about 15 months after purchase). What Seller's Stamp Duty (SSD) rate applies, and on what value?

- A. 16% SSD, because they sold within the first year
- B. 12% SSD, applied to the higher of selling price or market value, because the holding period is more than 1 and up to 2 years
- C. No SSD, because residential SSD was abolished in 2025
- D. 8% SSD, applied to the original purchase price

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> For residential property purchased on/after 4 Jul 2025, SSD applies over a 4-year holding period at 16/12/8/4%. A holding period of more than 1 up to 2 years (15 months) attracts 12%, charged on the higher of selling price or market value. B is correct. B (16%) is the up-to-1-year rate, but 15 months exceeds one year. C is false—SSD was extended (holding period lengthened to 4 years, rates raised by 4 percentage points) on 4 Jul 2025, not abolished. D uses the >2-3 year rate (8%) and the wrong base (it is the higher of price or value, not original purchase price). 中文一句话：2025年7月4日后购入的住宅，持有>1至2年SSD为12%，按售价与市价较高者计。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS/MAS SSD residential eff. 4 Jul 2025 (verified: 4-yr, 16/12/8/4%)

---

**Q14.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: A young couple (both Singapore Citizens) are buying their first BTO flat directly from HDB and taking an HDB concessionary loan. Their adviser explains the financing limits. Which statement is correct?

- A. The HDB concessionary loan LTV is 80%
- B. The MSR does not apply because they are buying from HDB; only TDSR at 55% applies
- C. The Mortgage Servicing Ratio (MSR) of 30% of gross monthly income applies, and the HDB concessionary loan LTV is capped at 75%
- D. Private-property LTV rules of 75%/45%/35% by loan count apply to their HDB loan

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> MSR (30% of gross monthly income) applies to HDB flats and ECs bought from a developer; the HDB concessionary loan LTV was cut to 75% (from 80%) on 20 Aug 2024. C is correct. B is wrong—MSR specifically applies to HDB/developer-EC purchases. C uses the old pre-20-Aug-2024 80% figure. D wrongly applies the private bank-loan LTV ladder to an HDB concessionary loan. 中文一句话：购组屋适用30%偿债比率（MSR），公积金优惠贷款LTV自2024年8月20日起降至75%。
>
> 📎 Source: MAS LTV/MSR/TDSR rules; HDB LTV 75% eff. 20 Aug 2024

---

**Q15.** Which statement about using CPF to finance an HDB flat is correct?

- A. The Withdrawal Limit for HDB flats is 100% of the purchase price
- B. HDB flats are capped at the 120% Withdrawal Limit just like private property
- C. CPF cannot be used to service an HDB loan at all
- D. HDB flats have no CPF Withdrawal Limit; for an HDB flat bought with an HDB concessionary loan, neither the VL nor the WL applies

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> HDB flats have no WL (CPF can fund beyond the VL), and for an HDB flat purchased with an HDB concessionary loan, neither the VL nor the WL applies, provided the lease covers the youngest owner to age 95. D is correct. B is wrong—the 120% WL is for PRIVATE property only. C is false—CPF is routinely used to service HDB loans. D invents a 100%-of-price cap that does not apply to HDB. 中文一句话：组屋无提款限额；以公积金优惠贷款购组屋时，VL与WL均不适用。
>
> 📎 Source: Common exam trap: HDB no Withdrawal Limit; CPF for HDB with concessionary loan

---



# RES 2026 题库（含答案与解析）— Paper 2

> 共 105 题。每题附正确答案、解析与易错点。建议先盖住答案作答，再核对。
> 所有数字均按 2026 年现行规定生成并经二次核查；如遇 CEA/IRAS 政策更新，以官方为准。


## P2.1 Estate Agency Agreements (Exclusive/Open), Commission, Co-broking

**Q1.** A property agent asks a seller to sign Form 5 (Exclusive Estate Agency Agreement for the Sale of Residential Property). What is the MAXIMUM validity period that may be stated in this agreement under the prescribed form?

- A. 3 months
- B. 1 month
- C. 6 months
- D. 12 months

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> The prescribed exclusive estate agency agreement cannot have a validity exceeding 3 months, and it does not auto-renew (any renewal must be on the prescribed Renewal of Agreement form, each renewal capped at 3 months). A (1 month), C (6 months) and D (12 months) are all wrong because the cap is fixed at 3 months regardless of what the parties prefer; 6 and 12 months are common distractors based on tenancy/listing intuition but exceed the prescribed limit. 中文：独家代理协议（Form 5）的最长有效期为3个月。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA Prescribed Estate Agency Agreement Form 5 (exclusive max validity 3 months; no auto-renewal)

---

**Q2.** Under CEA rules, who sets the commission rate that a real estate salesperson may charge a client?

- A. CEA prescribes a fixed maximum rate of 2%
- B. The rate is fully negotiable between the agent and the client
- C. HDB sets the rate for HDB transactions and CEA for private
- D. The Inland Revenue Authority of Singapore (IRAS) regulates it

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> Commission is NOT fixed or regulated by CEA; it is fully negotiable and must be documented in the estate agency agreement. A is wrong because CEA does not prescribe any maximum (2% is only a market norm). C is wrong because neither HDB nor CEA sets rates. D is wrong because IRAS deals with stamp duty/tax, not agent commission. 中文：佣金不受CEA规管，完全由双方协商并写入协议。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA / Estate Agents Act – commission not regulated, negotiable

---

**Q3.** A seller signs a 3-month exclusive agreement with Agent Tan. During the validity period Agent Tan introduces Buyer Lim, but no deal is reached. Two weeks after the agreement expires, the seller sells directly to Buyer Lim without any agent. Is Agent Tan entitled to commission?

- A. No, because the exclusive agreement has already expired
- B. Yes, because the exclusive agreement automatically renewed
- C. Yes, because the buyer was introduced during the validity period and the sale occurred within the 3-month post-expiry tail
- D. No, because the seller closed the deal himself without an agent

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> The prescribed exclusive agreement includes a post-expiry commission tail: if the property is sold within 3 months after expiry to a buyer the agent INTRODUCED during the validity period, commission is still payable. A is wrong because the tail clause survives expiry for introduced buyers. B is wrong because exclusive agreements do NOT auto-renew. D is wrong because under an exclusive agreement the seller is liable even if he closes himself, and here the introduction triggers the tail. 中文：独家协议到期后3个月内卖给期内引介的买家，仍需付佣金。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA exclusive EAA – 3-month post-expiry commission tail for introduced buyers

---

**Q4.** A landlord signs a NON-exclusive (open) estate agency agreement and engages three different agencies to find a tenant. Agency C successfully secures the tenant who signs the lease. Which statement is correct regarding commission?

- A. The landlord must pay all three agencies equally
- B. The landlord may choose any one of the three to pay
- C. The first agency to advertise the unit is paid
- D. Only Agency C, which closed the deal, is paid

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> Under a non-exclusive/open arrangement the client pays only the agency that actually closes the deal. A is wrong because open agreements do not require paying every engaged agency. C is wrong because being first to advertise does not earn commission without closing. B is wrong because the client cannot arbitrarily pick a non-performing agency; commission follows the effective cause of the transaction (the closer). 中文：开放式协议下，只付给真正成交的那家代理。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA non-exclusive (open) EAA principles

---

**Q5.** Which of the following correctly describes a CO-BROKING arrangement?

- A. The seller's agent cooperates with a separate buyer's agent, each representing their own client
- B. One salesperson represents and collects commission from both the buyer and the seller in the same deal
- C. Two salespersons from the same agency split one client's commission
- D. An agent sub-contracts the entire listing to an unlicensed introducer

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> Co-broking is the cooperation between the seller's/landlord's salesperson and a separate buyer's/tenant's salesperson, each representing a different party. B describes DUAL REPRESENTATION, which is a prohibited offence — collecting/sharing fees from both sides. C describes an internal split, not co-broking. D describes illegal use of an unlicensed party. 中文：共同代理是买卖双方各有代理人互相合作，不同于违法的双重代理。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – co-broking definition; dual representation prohibition

---

**Q6.** The SEAA Best Practice Guide for Co-Broking Commission (effective 1 July 2024) encourages agents to collect commission only from the client they represent. What is the legal status of this Guide?

- A. It is a CEA regulation; breach leads to a disciplinary penalty
- B. It is a voluntary best-practice guide with no penalty for non-compliance
- C. It is part of the Estate Agents Act and is mandatory
- D. It only applies to HDB transactions

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> The SEAA Guide is a voluntary best-practice guide, NOT a regulation; there is no penalty for not following it, though EAs representing about 90% of RESs had adopted it as of February 2025. A and C are wrong because it is neither a CEA regulation nor part of the EAA. D is wrong because it is not limited to HDB transactions. 中文：SEAA共同代理佣金指南是自愿性的，不是规管，不遵守不会受罚。
>
> 📎 Source: SEAA Best Practice Guide for Co-Broking Commission (eff. 1 Jul 2024); CEA CEANERGY blog

---

**Q7.** Salesperson A represents the seller and Salesperson B represents the buyer in the same transaction. Both A and B are registered with the SAME estate agency. Which statement is correct?

- A. This is automatically dual representation and is prohibited
- B. This is allowed without any disclosure because they are colleagues
- C. This is allowed only if both declare in writing they are from the same EA and obtain the parties' written consent, with neither collecting from both sides
- D. The agency must refund all commission collected

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> Two RES from the same EA acting on opposite sides is NOT dual representation provided neither collects from both sides AND both declare in writing that they are from the same EA and obtain the parties' written consent. A is wrong because dual representation is one salesperson/EA collecting from both sides, not two colleagues each paid by their own client. B is wrong because written disclosure and consent are mandatory. D is wrong because, properly disclosed and consented, the arrangement is lawful and commission is valid. 中文：同公司两名代理分别代表买卖双方可行，但须书面披露同属一家EA并取得双方书面同意，且任一方不得双向收费。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – conflict of interest / dual representation rules; EA(EAW) Regulations 2010

---

**Q8.** In a residential sale, a salesperson arranges to collect 2% commission from the seller AND also a 1% fee from the buyer in the SAME transaction, while representing only the seller in the agency agreement. Which is correct?

- A. This is permitted because commission is negotiable
- B. It is allowed if the buyer signs a separate receipt
- C. This is acceptable if the total does not exceed 3%
- D. This is dual representation, a prohibited offence under CEA rules

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> Collecting/sharing fees from BOTH sides of the same transaction is dual representation, a prohibited offence under Reg 5 of the EA(EAW) Regulations (one prosecuted case drew a $9,000 fine; the offence carries a fine up to $25,000 and/or up to 12 months' jail). A is wrong because negotiability of the rate does not legalise collecting from both sides. C is wrong because no percentage cap turns dual collection into compliance. B is wrong because a separate receipt does not cure the prohibited dual collection. 中文：同一交易向买卖双方都收费属于双重代理，是违法行为。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – dual representation prohibited (offence); EA(EAW) Regulations 2010 Reg 5

---

**Q9.** A seller agrees to a 2% commission on a residential property that sells for $1,500,000. The co-broking buyer's agent is to receive 1% from the buyer separately. How much commission does the SELLER pay (before GST)?

- A. $30,000
- B. $22,500
- C. $15,000
- D. $45,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> The seller pays 2% of $1,500,000 = $30,000. The buyer's 1% is paid separately by the buyer and does not affect the seller's bill. A ($15,000) is 1%. B ($22,500) is 1.5%. D ($45,000) wrongly adds the buyer's 1% to the seller's 2%, but under each-side-pays-own-agent the seller only pays his own 2%. 中文：卖方付2%×$1,500,000=$30,000；买方的1%另由买方支付。
>
> 📎 Source: Market norm ~2% seller commission; arithmetic

---

**Q10.** A landlord leases out a unit for a 2-year tenancy at $4,000/month. Under the prevailing Singapore market convention for a landlord's agent (about half a month's rent per year of lease — i.e. 1 month for a 2-year lease), what commission is the landlord's agent entitled to, excluding GST?

- A. $8,000
- B. $4,000
- C. $2,000
- D. $6,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> The prevailing Singapore convention for a landlord's agent is about 0.5 month's rent per year of lease, so a 2-year lease ≈ 1 month's rent = 1 × $4,000 = $4,000. B ($8,000) is two months, reflecting the outdated 'one month per year' assumption that is not the Singapore landlord norm. C ($2,000) is half a month (the norm for a 1-year lease). D ($6,000) is 1.5 months. Note all rental commissions are negotiable, not fixed. 中文：业主代理惯例约为每年租约半个月租金，2年租约约1个月=$4,000。
>
> 📎 Source: Singapore market convention – landlord rental commission ~0.5 month per lease year (1 month for a 2-year lease); arithmetic

---

**Q11.** A seller's agent and a buyer's agent co-broke a $1,200,000 HDB resale. They agree the total commission pool is split 1% to the seller's side and 1% to the buyer's side, with the seller paying his agent and the buyer paying his agent. What does the BUYER pay his own agent (before GST)?

- A. $24,000
- B. $6,000
- C. $12,000
- D. $0 because buyers never pay commission

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> The buyer pays his own agent 1% of $1,200,000 = $12,000. A ($24,000) is 2%, which would be the combined pool, not the buyer's share. C ($6,000) is 0.5%. D is wrong because buyers can and do pay their own agent, especially under the each-side-pays-own-agent practice. 中文：买方付自己代理1%×$1,200,000=$12,000。
>
> 📎 Source: SEAA each-side-pays-own-agent practice; arithmetic

---

**Q12.** Which prescribed CEA Estate Agency Agreement form would a salesperson use when acting EXCLUSIVELY for a landlord leasing out a residential property?

- A. Form 3
- B. Form 5
- C. Form 8
- D. Form 7

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(easy)_
>
> Form 7 is the Exclusive Estate Agency Agreement for the Lease of Residential Property by a Landlord. Form 3 is the NON-exclusive landlord-leasing form. Form 5 is the exclusive SELLING form. Form 8 is the exclusive TENANT-leasing form. 中文：业主独家出租用Form 7；Form 3是非独家、Form 5是独家出售、Form 8是租客独家。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA 8 prescribed Estate Agency Agreement forms (Forms 1–8)

---

**Q13.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Mdm Goh signs a Form 5 exclusive agreement with Agent Raj (Agency X) valid 1 March to 31 May, commission 2%. On 10 May Agent Raj introduces Buyer Wong, who declines. Frustrated, Mdm Goh quietly engages Agent Siti (Agency Y) and, on 20 May, sells the unit through Siti to a different buyer, Mr Heng, for $1,000,000. Which statement about commission liability is correct?

- A. Mdm Goh is liable to pay Agency X commission because the sale occurred during the exclusive validity period
- B. Only Agency Y is paid; the exclusive agreement is void once a second agent is engaged
- C. No commission is payable to Agency X because Mr Heng was not introduced by Agent Raj
- D. Agency X and Agency Y must split the 2% equally

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(hard)_
>
> Under an exclusive agreement the client is liable to pay the exclusive agent's commission if the property is sold during the validity period — even via another agent or by the client himself. Here the sale on 20 May falls within the 1 Mar–31 May validity, so Mdm Goh owes Agency X. B is wrong because engaging a second agent does not void the exclusive agreement. C is wrong because during the validity period liability does not depend on who introduced the buyer (the introduced-buyer test applies to the post-expiry tail). D is wrong because there is no mandated equal split; Mdm Goh's exclusive liability is to Agency X (and she may separately owe Agency Y per their terms). 中文：独家有效期内成交，即使经别的代理，业主仍须付独家代理（Agency X）佣金。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA exclusive EAA – client liable during validity even if sold via another agent/self

---

**Q14.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Agent Lim lists a condo under a non-exclusive agreement. A buyer's agent, Agent Tan from another agency, contacts Lim to co-broke. They agree Tan's client (the buyer) will pay Tan's fee and Lim's client (the seller) will pay Lim's fee. During the viewing the buyer privately offers Lim an extra 'thank-you' fee if Lim persuades the seller to drop the price. What is the correct course of action for Lim under CEA conduct rules?

- A. Accept the fee since commission is negotiable
- B. Decline / not accept, as collecting from the buyer while representing the seller creates a conflict of interest and risks dual representation
- C. Accept but disclose it only after completion
- D. Accept and share half with Agent Tan

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> Lim represents the seller; accepting a fee from the buyer to act against the seller's interest (pushing the seller's price down) is a conflict of interest and amounts to collecting from both sides — dual representation, which is prohibited. A is wrong because negotiability does not permit divided loyalty/dual collection. C is wrong because after-the-fact disclosure does not cure an undisclosed conflict or acting against your own client. D is wrong because sharing the improper fee with the co-broking agent does not legitimise it. 中文：代表卖方却收买方的钱去压低卖方价格，构成利益冲突／双重代理，应拒绝。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA Code of Ethics & Professional Client Care – conflict of interest avoidance; dual representation prohibition

---

**Q15.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: A first-time HDB seller asks her agent why she should sign a prescribed Estate Agency Agreement at all, since 'we trust each other'. Which of the following is the BEST reason the agent should give that is consistent with CEA's position?

- A. It is optional but looks professional
- B. It allows the agent to charge a higher CEA-fixed commission
- C. Although not strictly mandatory, CEA strongly encourages using the prescribed agreement to document the engagement, commission terms and obligations, which protects both parties and minimises disputes
- D. It transfers all legal liability to CEA

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> CEA does not legally compel use of the prescribed forms, but strongly encourages them because they clearly document the engagement, commission and obligations, protecting both parties and minimising disputes. A is wrong because it dismisses the agreement as merely cosmetic and ignores its protective function. B is wrong because there is no CEA-fixed commission — it is negotiable. D is wrong because the agreement does not transfer liability to CEA. 中文：规定协议虽非强制，但CEA强烈建议使用，以书面记录委托、佣金与责任，保护双方、减少纠纷。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – prescribed estate agency agreements strongly encouraged (not mandatory); commission negotiable

---


## P2.2 Marketing & Advertising Rules, AML/CFT Obligations for Salespersons

**Q1.** Salesperson Faizal posts a video advertisement of a condo unit for sale on a social media platform. To comply with CEA advertising rules, what MUST the advertisement contain?

- A. Only the salesperson's name and mobile number
- B. The salesperson's name and a recent photograph of the unit
- C. Only the EA's licence number and the asking price
- D. The salesperson's name, CEA registration number, contact number, and the EA's licence number

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(easy)_
>
> For print, online and mobile/social-media advertisements, CEA requires the salesperson's name, CEA registration number and contact number, plus the estate agent's (EA) licence number. D is the only option carrying the full prescribed set. A omits the CEA registration number and EA licence number. C omits the salesperson's identifying details (name, registration number). B omits the registration number, contact number and EA licence number; a property photo is not a mandated identifier. (Note: newspaper classified and SMS/phone-text ads are a narrower exception requiring only the agent's name and phone number, but a social-media video is a full-disclosure ad.) 中文：网络/社交媒体等广告必须显示销售员姓名、CEA注册号、联系电话及经纪行执照号，故选D。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA advertising requirements (conduct & advertising rules); https://www.cea.gov.sg/

---

**Q2.** Under CEA rules, what is the maximum financial penalty CEA may impose specifically for breaches of the property advertising requirements?

- A. Up to $75,000
- B. Up to $25,000
- C. Up to $5,000
- D. Up to $500,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> CEA may impose a financial penalty of up to $75,000 for advertising breaches, in addition to suspension or revocation of registration/licence. A ($5,000) is the Letter of Censure cap for less-serious breaches, not the advertising figure. B ($25,000) is a fabricated figure. D ($500,000) is not a CEA penalty figure at all. (The Disciplinary Committee's general maximum is separately $100,000 per case for a RES and $200,000 for an EA, but $75,000 is the figure CEA publicly cites for advertising breaches.) 中文：违反广告规定最高罚款7万5千元，故选A。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA tightens up on property agents' ads; https://sg.news.yahoo.com/blogs/singaporescene/cea-tightens-property-agents-ads-090218717.html

---

**Q3.** Salesperson Mei wants to advertise a landed house for sale. The owner has verbally said 'go ahead someday' but has not given any written instruction or agreement. What is the CORRECT position before Mei publishes the advertisement?

- A. She may advertise immediately because a verbal 'go ahead' is sufficient consent
- B. She must first obtain the owner's prior consent and ensure the material information advertised is accurate and verified
- C. She may advertise without consent as long as she shows her CEA registration number
- D. She only needs consent if the property is HDB; private landed property needs none

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> Advertising rules require the owner's prior consent and that material information (e.g. floor area, tenure) be accurate and verified; an offhand verbal remark with no agreement is not reliable authorisation. A overstates the value of a vague verbal remark and ignores the verification duty. C confuses identification requirements with the consent requirement; showing a registration number does not cure lack of consent. D invents a private/HDB distinction that does not exist. 中文：刊登广告前须取得业主事先同意并核实重要资料，含糊口头话不足，故选B。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA advertising rules (material info accuracy + owner consent); https://www.cea.gov.sg/

---

**Q4.** Which of the following advertised statements would MOST likely breach CEA advertising rules?

- A. Stating the floor area exactly as shown in the verified strata title plan
- B. Including the salesperson's CEA registration number and the EA licence number
- C. Describing the unit as 'freehold' when it is actually a 99-year leasehold property
- D. Stating the asking price as negotiable with the owner's consent

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> Advertisements must not contain false or misleading material information; misstating a 99-year leasehold as 'freehold' is a clear material misrepresentation of tenure. A is correct practice (verified, accurate floor area). B is exactly what the rules require. D is permissible where the owner has consented. 中文：把99年地契误称'永久地契'属虚假误导重要资料，违规，故选C。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA advertising rules (no false/misleading material info); https://www.cea.gov.sg/

---

**Q5.** Before entering into any agreement to market a client's property, what is a salesperson's PRIMARY Customer Due Diligence (CDD) obligation under the AML/CFT framework?

- A. Run CDD only if the property value exceeds $1.5 million
- B. Ask the client to verbally confirm they are not a criminal and proceed
- C. Collect a copy of the NRIC only after the sale is completed
- D. Obtain and document the client's information, verify identity using reliable independent sources, and screen against designated lists

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> CDD must be performed before any agreement: obtain and document client info, verify identity via reliable independent sources, screen against UNSC/UN Act designated lists, check PEP status, and apply enhanced due diligence (EDD) for higher risk. A captures this. B is grossly inadequate (no verification or screening). C is wrong on timing (CDD is upfront, not post-completion). D invents a value threshold; CDD applies to clients generally, not only above a price. 中文：签约前须取得并记录客户资料、用可靠独立来源核实身份并对照制裁名单筛查，故选D。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA – Preventing money laundering, proliferation financing and terrorism financing; https://www.cea.gov.sg/regulatory-matters/preventing-money-laundering-proliferation-financing-and-terrorism-financing/

---

**Q6.** Salesperson Daniel suspects a buyer is using funds connected to money laundering. Under the AML/CFT framework, how must this suspicion be reported?

- A. File a Suspicious Transaction Report (STR) to STRO through the SONAR system, via his EA
- B. File a police report at the nearest neighbourhood police post
- C. Email CEA's complaints hotline within 30 days
- D. Notify the buyer's bank directly and request the transaction be frozen

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> Suspicions of ML/PF/TF must be reported by law to the Suspicious Transaction Reporting Office (STRO) through the STRO Online Notices And Reporting (SONAR) platform; a RES files the STR through their EA. B is the incorrect channel (STRs go to STRO/SONAR, not a generic police post report). C confuses CEA discipline channels with STR reporting. D is wrong and risks tipping-off; the RES does not direct banks to freeze funds. 中文：怀疑洗钱须依法通过SONAR向STRO提交可疑交易报告（经经纪行），故选A。
>
> 📎 Source: SPF Suspicious Transaction Reporting (STRO/SONAR); https://www.police.gov.sg/Advisories/Commercial-Crimes/Suspicious-Transaction-Reporting-Office/Suspicious-Transaction-Reporting

---

**Q7.** For how long must AML/CFT-related records (including CDD documentation) be retained?

- A. At least 3 years
- B. At least 5 years
- C. At least 7 years
- D. Indefinitely, until the client requests deletion

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> AML/CFT records, including CDD records and compliance documentation, must be kept for at least 5 years (in original or electronic form, generally from the date of the transaction). A (3 years) is incorrect, C (7 years) and D (indefinite) are incorrect. 中文：AML记录（含CDD文件）须至少保存5年，故选B。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA AML/CFT record-keeping (≥5 years); https://www.cea.gov.sg/regulatory-matters/preventing-money-laundering-proliferation-financing-and-terrorism-financing/

---

**Q8.** A new client wants to buy a $6 million bungalow and pays a large initial sum in cash. The client is reluctant to provide identity documents and the source of funds is unclear. Beyond standard CDD, what is the salesperson's MOST appropriate response?

- A. Proceed with standard CDD only, since the client has already paid
- B. Decline to verify identity because high-net-worth clients are exempt from CDD
- C. Apply Enhanced Due Diligence (EDD), and if suspicion remains, file an STR via SONAR through the EA
- D. Tell the client his profile looks suspicious and ask him to explain before reporting

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> High-value cash, reluctance to provide ID, and unclear source of funds are red flags requiring Enhanced Due Diligence; if suspicion persists an STR must be filed via SONAR through the EA. A ignores the heightened risk. B is false—there is no high-net-worth CDD exemption; high value increases scrutiny. D is dangerous 'tipping-off', which can prejudice an investigation and is prohibited. 中文：高风险情形须做加强尽职调查(EDD)，仍有怀疑则经SONAR报STR；不可向客户透露(避免泄密)，故选C。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA AML/CFT (EDD for higher risk; STR via SONAR); https://www.cea.gov.sg/regulatory-matters/preventing-money-laundering-proliferation-financing-and-terrorism-financing/

---

**Q9.** Under the AML disciplinary regime that took effect on 1 July 2025, a Disciplinary Committee may impose a financial penalty against a SALESPERSON of up to what amount per breach for an AML breach?

- A. Up to $5,000 per breach
- B. Up to $75,000 per breach
- C. Up to $200,000 per breach
- D. Up to $100,000 per breach

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> For AML/PF/TF breaches committed on or after 1 Jul 2025, the Disciplinary Committee maximum is $100,000 per breach (per contravention) for a salesperson (RES) and $200,000 per breach for an EA. A ($5,000) is the Letter of Censure cap for less-serious AML breaches, not the DC maximum. B ($75,000) is the advertising penalty figure, not the AML DC cap. D ($200,000) is the EA cap, not the RES cap. 中文：2025年7月1日起，AML违规纪律委员会对销售员每项最高罚10万元，故选C；5千是谴责信、20万是经纪行上限。
>
> 📎 Source: Anti-Money Laundering and Other Matters (Estate Agents and Developers) Act 2025; CEA disciplinary proceedings (operative 1 Jul 2025); https://www.cea.gov.sg/regulatory-matters/disciplinary-proceedings/

---

**Q10.** The 2026 Prescribed Essentials (PE) topic that all salespersons must cover within their structured CPD relates to which subject?

- A. Prevention of money laundering, proliferation financing and terrorism financing (PMLPFTF)
- B. Digital marketing and social-media advertising compliance
- C. Conflict of interest and dual representation
- D. Stamp duty computation and CPF usage limits

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> For the 2026 CPD cycle, the specified Prescribed Essentials topic is PMLPFTF (prevention of money laundering, proliferation financing and terrorism financing), introduced to support compliance with the revised PMLPFTF requirements. B, C and D are all legitimate professional topics but are not the designated 2026 PE topic. 中文：2026年CPD的规定必修(PE)主题是反洗钱、扩散融资与反恐融资(PMLPFTF)，故选A。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA CPD 2026 Changes (Project ADEPT, 2026 PE = PMLPFTF); https://www.cea.gov.sg/about-cea/newsroom-publications/ceanergy-blog/transforming-your-cpd-journey-key-changes-from-2026/

---

**Q11.** In the 2026 CPD framework, a salesperson must complete 16 training hours per year. How are these hours structured?

- A. 16 hours, all Self-Directed Learning
- B. 12 hours Structured Learning (including at least 4 hours Prescribed Essentials) + 4 hours Self-Directed Learning
- C. 8 hours Structured Learning + 8 hours Self-Directed Learning
- D. 6 hours Structured Learning + 10 hours Self-Directed Learning

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> From the 2026 cycle the requirement is 16 hours = 12h Structured Learning (with at least 4h of Prescribed Essentials) + 4h Self-Directed Learning. A, C and D all misallocate the split. 中文：2026年16小时＝12小时结构化学习(含≥4小时规定必修)＋4小时自主学习，故选B。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA CPD 2026 Changes; https://www.cea.gov.sg/about-cea/newsroom-publications/ceanergy-blog/transforming-your-cpd-journey-key-changes-from-2026/

---

**Q12.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Salespersons Ahmad and Bee are BOTH registered with the same EA, 'Skyline Realty'. Ahmad represents the seller and Bee represents the buyer in the same transaction. Each collects commission only from their own client. Which statement is CORRECT?

- A. This is prohibited dual representation and an offence, regardless of disclosure
- B. This is permitted only if Ahmad collects all commission and shares it with Bee
- C. This is permitted, provided neither collects from both sides AND both declare in writing that they are from the same EA and obtain their clients' written consent
- D. This is permitted automatically because they are different individuals

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> Two RES from the SAME EA on opposite sides is NOT prohibited dual representation, provided neither collects commission from both sides AND both declare in writing to their respective clients that they are from the same EA and obtain each client's written consent. A wrongly equates same-EA representation with the prohibited dual-rep offence (which is one agent/RES acting for and collecting from both sides). B describes commission effectively flowing from both sides via sharing and omits the written-consent safeguard. D omits the mandatory written declaration and consent. 中文：同一经纪行两名销售员各代表一方且各自只向己方收佣，非违法双重代理，但须书面声明同属一行并取得各自客户书面同意，故选C。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA dual representation rules (No dual representation guide); https://www.cea.gov.sg/docs/default-source/consumers/no-dual-representation.pdf

---

**Q13.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Salesperson Priya is marketing Mr Tan's flat. A prospective buyer, Mr Wong, offers to pay her a 'finder's bonus' on top of the seller's commission if she helps push the deal through, and asks her not to mention it to Mr Tan. What is Priya's correct course of action?

- A. Accept the bonus quietly since the seller's commission is unaffected
- B. Accept and treat it as an overriding commission with no disclosure needed
- C. Accept but only disclose it to Mr Wong, the party paying it
- D. Refuse, because collecting payment from both the seller and the buyer in the same transaction is prohibited dual representation; any potential conflict must also be disclosed in writing

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> Collecting fees from BOTH sides of the same transaction is the prohibited dual-representation offence under the Estate Agents Act; furthermore any potential conflict of interest must be disclosed in writing to the client. D is correct. A ignores the offence and the non-disclosure problem. C only discloses to the payer, not the principal client (Mr Tan) who is prejudiced. B wrongly claims extra/overriding fees need no disclosure—conflicts must be disclosed in writing. 中文：同一交易向买卖双方收费属违法双重代理，且任何利益冲突须书面披露，故选D。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA dual representation prohibition + conflict disclosure (e.g. RES fined $9,000 for dual representation); https://www.cea.gov.sg/about-cea/newsroom-publications/ceanergy-blog/former-salesperson-sentenced-to-9-000-fine-for-dual-representation/

---

**Q14.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Salesperson Lim signs an Exclusive Estate Agency Agreement (Form 5) to sell a condo, valid for the maximum allowed period. He introduces buyer 'Goh' to the property during the validity period, but Goh only signs the OTP with the seller 12 days after the agreement expires. Which statement is CORRECT?

- A. The maximum exclusive validity is 3 months, and Lim is still entitled to commission because the introduced buyer transacted within the 3-month post-expiry tail
- B. The maximum exclusive validity is 6 months, and there is no post-expiry commission protection
- C. Lim earns no commission because the exclusive agreement has expired
- D. Lim must sign a fresh agreement before any commission can be claimed for Goh

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(hard)_
>
> A prescribed exclusive EAA has a maximum validity of 3 months, and a 3-month post-expiry commission tail applies to a buyer the agent introduced to the seller during the validity period. Goh was introduced during validity and transacted only 12 days after expiry—within the tail—so commission is payable. A ignores the post-expiry tail. B states the wrong max validity (3 months, not 6) and wrongly denies the tail. D is unnecessary; the existing agreement's tail already covers the introduced buyer. 中文：独家协议最长3个月，且对协议期内引介的买家有3个月延续佣金保护期，Goh在期满后12天成交仍可收佣，故选A。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA prescribed Estate Agency Agreements (Form 5; exclusive max 3 months + 3-month tail); https://www.cea.gov.sg/

---

**Q15.** Which statement about estate agency commission and the SEAA co-broking guide is CORRECT?

- A. CEA fixes the commission rate at 2% for all residential sales
- B. Commission is fully negotiable and not fixed by CEA; the SEAA Best Practice Guide for Co-Broking Commission is a guideline, not a regulation with penalties
- C. The SEAA Co-Broking Guide is a CEA regulation; breaching it leads to a financial penalty
- D. A salesperson may collect commission from both the seller and buyer if both verbally agree

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> Commission is not fixed or regulated by CEA—it is negotiable and documented in the estate agency agreement. The SEAA Best Practice Guide for Co-Broking Commission (effective 1 Jul 2024) is industry best practice, not a CEA regulation, and carries no statutory penalty for non-compliance. A is false (no fixed rate). C wrongly elevates the SEAA guide to a penalised regulation. D describes prohibited dual representation, which is an offence regardless of verbal agreement. 中文：佣金由市场协商、非CEA规定；SEAA共同经纪佣金指南是行业最佳实践非法规，故选B。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA commission rules + SEAA Best Practice Guide for Co-Broking (eff. 1 Jul 2024); https://www.cea.gov.sg/about-cea/newsroom-publications/ceanergy-blog/key-things-to-know-about-the-seaa-best-practice-guide-for-co-broking-commission/

---


## P2.3 Sale of Completed Property: Option to Purchase (OTP) & Sale & Purchase Agreement

**Q1.** A buyer is granted an Option to Purchase (OTP) for an HDB resale flat. By when must the buyer decide whether to exercise the OTP?

- A. Within 14 calendar days, expiring at 4pm on the last day
- B. Within 21 working days, expiring at 5pm on the last day
- C. Within 21 calendar days, expiring at 4pm on the last day
- D. Within 3 months from the date the OTP is granted

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(easy)_
>
> The HDB resale OTP option period is fixed at 21 calendar days (including weekends and public holidays), expiring at 4pm on the 21st day. A: 14 days is the typical PRIVATE resale option period, not HDB. B: the period is calendar days not working days, and it expires at 4pm not 5pm. D: 3 months is the validity of the Request for Value outcome, not the option period. 中文：HDB转售OTP期限固定为21个日历日，第21天下午4点截止。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB - Option to Purchase (https://www.hdb.gov.sg/residential/buying-a-flat/buying-procedure-for-resale-flats/plan-source-and-contract/option-to-purchase)

---

**Q2.** For an HDB resale transaction, a seller wants to collect the maximum permitted Option Fee and the buyer has already paid that amount. What is the most the buyer can be asked to pay as the Option Exercise Fee, and why?

- A. $1,000, because the Exercise Fee cannot exceed the Option Fee
- B. $5,000, because each of the two fees is independently capped at $5,000
- C. $4,000, because the Exercise Fee alone is capped at $4,000 regardless of the Option Fee
- D. $4,000, because the combined Option Fee plus Exercise Fee must not exceed $5,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> The HDB rule caps the Option Fee at $1,000 and caps the COMBINED Option Fee + Exercise Fee at $5,000. If the seller collects the maximum $1,000 Option Fee, the Exercise Fee is limited to $5,000 - $1,000 = $4,000. D is correct because it gives the right figure for the right reason (the $5,000 combined cap). B is wrong: the $5,000 cap is combined, not per-fee. C states the right number but the wrong reason - the $4,000 here results from the combined cap given a $1,000 Option Fee, not a standalone $4,000 cap. D invents a rule that does not exist. 中文：OTP两项费用合计上限$5,000；付了$1,000订金后，行使费最多$4,000。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB - Option to Purchase (https://www.hdb.gov.sg/residential/buying-a-flat/buying-procedure-for-resale-flats/plan-source-and-contract/option-to-purchase)

---

**Q3.** In a private (non-HDB) resale conveyancing transaction, what is the conventional deposit structure for an Option to Purchase?

- A. Option Fee of 1% and an Exercise Fee of 4%, totalling 5% of the purchase price
- B. Option Fee of 5% and an Exercise Fee of 1%, totalling 6%
- C. A single fixed deposit of $5,000 capped by regulation
- D. Option Fee of 10% with no further Exercise Fee

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> By private-market convention the Option Fee is about 1% of the purchase price and the Exercise Fee about 4%, giving a 5% total deposit. These are negotiable conventions, not statutory caps. B reverses the figures and inflates the total to 6%. C describes the HDB $5,000 cap, which does not apply to private property. D overstates the deposit; 10% is not the standard OTP convention. 中文：私宅OTP惯例为订金1%+行使费4%，共5%；非法定，仅惯例。
>
> 📎 Source: PropertyGuru OTP Guide (https://www.propertyguru.com.sg/property-guides/option-to-purchase-15959)

---

**Q4.** A buyer exercises a private resale OTP, signing the document and acquiring an interest in the property. Which statement BEST describes the buyer's interest and stamp-duty obligation at this point?

- A. The buyer holds legal title and must pay stamp duty within 30 days
- B. The buyer holds an equitable interest, can lodge a caveat, and must pay Buyer's Stamp Duty within 14 days of exercising
- C. The buyer holds no interest until the conveyance completes, so no caveat may be lodged
- D. The buyer holds legal title immediately and stamp duty is only payable on completion

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> On exercising the OTP / signing the S&P, the buyer acquires an EQUITABLE interest (legal title passes only on registration of the transfer at completion). That equitable interest is caveatable. Stamp duty (BSD, plus ABSD if applicable) is payable within 14 days of the dutiable instrument when signed in Singapore. A and D wrongly state legal title vests now; legal title vests on registration. C is wrong because an equitable interest exists once OTP is exercised, supporting a caveat. The 30-day figure in A is the overseas-signing deadline, not the local one. 中文：行使OTP后买方取得衡平法权益，可登记caveat，须14天内缴印花税；法定产权完成时才转移。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS Stamp Duty payment deadlines (https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/basics-of-stamp-duty-for-property/learning-the-basics-for-properties)

---

**Q5.** A Singapore Citizen buys his SECOND completed resale condominium for $1,200,000, equal to its market value. What is the TOTAL stamp duty (BSD + ABSD) payable on exercising the OTP?

- A. $32,600 (BSD only)
- B. $240,000 (ABSD only)
- C. $272,600 (BSD $32,600 + ABSD $240,000)
- D. $36,000 (flat 3% of price)

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> BSD = 1%×180k + 2%×180k + 3%×640k + 4%×200k = $1,800 + $3,600 + $19,200 + $8,000 = $32,600. ABSD for a Singapore Citizen's 2nd residential property = 20% × $1.2m = $240,000 (rate in force since 27 Apr 2023, current in 2026). Total = $272,600, so C is correct. A forgets ABSD applies on a 2nd property. B forgets BSD always applies. D treats BSD as a flat 3% instead of the progressive tiers. 中文：BSD按累进算$32,600，SC第二套ABSD 20%为$240,000，合计$272,600。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS BSD & ABSD tables (current 2026) (https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/buying-or-acquiring-property/additional-buyer's-stamp-duty-(absd))

---

**Q6.** After being granted an HDB resale OTP, a buyer who intends to use CPF or a housing loan must submit a Request for Value to HDB. When must this be submitted, and how long is the outcome valid?

- A. On the completion date; outcome valid until completion
- B. Within 21 days of the OTP; outcome valid for 21 days
- C. Within 14 days of exercising the OTP; outcome valid for 5 years
- D. By the next working day after the Option date; outcome valid for 3 months

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> The Request for Value (processing fee $120, GST inclusive) must be submitted by the next working day after the Option Date stated in the OTP, and the valuation outcome is valid for 3 months from the day it is made available, within which both parties must lodge the resale application. B confuses it with the option period. C borrows the caveat 5-year validity and the wrong trigger. A is incorrect because the request must precede the resale application, well before completion. 中文：估价申请须在Option Date次个工作日提交，结果有效期3个月。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB - Request for Value (https://www.hdb.gov.sg/residential/buying-a-flat/buying-procedure-for-resale-flats/plan-source-and-contract/request-for-value)

---

**Q7.** Which of the following is the BEST description of the role of an exercised OTP versus a Sale & Purchase Agreement (SPA) in completed-property transactions?

- A. A developer new-launch sale uses a prescribed SPA, whereas a private resale typically uses the exercised OTP itself as the binding contract
- B. Both new-launch and resale transactions always require a separate prescribed SPA in addition to the OTP
- C. An OTP is never legally binding; only an SPA creates a contract
- D. For HDB resale, a separate SPA must always be signed after the OTP is exercised

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> For new launches from a developer, a prescribed SPA governs the sale. For a private resale, the exercised OTP commonly serves as the binding contract itself, with no separate SPA. A captures this correctly. B is wrong: resale typically does not need a separate prescribed SPA. C is wrong: once exercised, an OTP IS a binding contract. D is wrong: HDB resale is governed by the OTP and the HDB resale process, not a separately signed SPA. 中文：新盘用规定的SPA；私宅转售一般以已行使的OTP作为有约束力合同。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS / HDB conveyancing references; CEA RES coursebook P2.3

---

**Q8.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Mr Tan grants an OTP for his private condo to Ms Lim on 1 June 2026. The OTP gives a 14-day option period. Ms Lim pays a 1% Option Fee. On day 10, Ms Lim decides not to proceed and lets the option lapse without exercising it. What is the typical legal consequence?

- A. Mr Tan must refund the Option Fee in full because the option period had not yet expired
- B. Ms Lim forfeits the 1% Option Fee and the OTP lapses; she is under no obligation to complete
- C. Ms Lim is liable for the full purchase price because granting the OTP created a binding sale
- D. Ms Lim forfeits 5% of the price as the standard deposit even though she only paid 1%

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> An OTP gives the buyer the RIGHT but not the obligation to buy.
