If the buyer does not exercise within the option period, the option simply lapses and the buyer forfeits the Option Fee paid (here 1%); there is no obligation to complete. B is correct. A is wrong: the Option Fee is generally forfeited, not refunded, when the buyer walks away. C is wrong: a sale becomes binding only on EXERCISE, not on mere grant of the option. D is wrong: she only paid 1%, so only that 1% is at risk - she cannot forfeit money she never paid. 中文：买方不行使OTP，期权失效并没收已付订金（1%），但无须完成交易。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA RES coursebook P2.3 Option to Purchase

---

**Q9.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY (cont.): Suppose instead Ms Lim EXERCISES the OTP on day 12 by signing and paying the Exercise Fee, bringing her total deposit to 5%. She then changes her mind and refuses to complete the purchase. Which outcome BEST reflects her position?

- A. She may still walk away losing only the 1% Option Fee, as before
- B. The OTP automatically converts to a refundable reservation, so she recovers the full 5%
- C. Having exercised the OTP, she is contractually bound; the seller may forfeit the deposit and pursue remedies for breach
- D. She must pay Seller's Stamp Duty as the penalty for non-completion

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> Once the OTP is EXERCISED, a binding contract of sale exists. If the buyer then defaults, the seller can typically forfeit the deposit paid and may pursue further remedies for breach of contract. C is correct. A is wrong: exercising removes the easy walk-away; the full deposit is now at risk. C invents a refundable-reservation mechanism that does not exist after exercise. D is wrong: SSD is a SELLER'S duty on disposal of property, not a buyer's penalty for failing to complete. 中文：行使OTP后合同成立，违约买方将被没收订金，卖方还可追究违约责任。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA RES coursebook P2.3 Option to Purchase / Breach of Contract

---

**Q10.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: A buyer's RES is assisting a client to buy a completed private resale apartment. After the OTP is exercised, which sequence of conveyancing steps is in the CORRECT order?

- A. Pay full stamp duty on completion, then exercise the OTP, then lodge a caveat
- B. Complete the transaction first, then lodge a caveat, then send legal requisitions
- C. Send legal requisitions, then exercise the OTP, then lodge a caveat
- D. Lodge caveat to protect interest, then conduct legal requisitions to government bodies, then complete by exchanging title and cashier's orders

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> After the OTP is exercised: (1) the buyer's lawyer lodges a caveat to protect the equitable interest; (2) pre-completion legal requisitions are sent to government bodies (e.g. PUB, LTA, NEA, IRAS) to confirm no acquisition/development plans and a good root of title; (3) completion occurs with exchange of title, transfer instrument and cashier's orders. D is correct. B reverses the order - a caveat is lodged BEFORE completion to protect the buyer. C and D place exercising the OTP after steps that logically follow it, and D also wrongly delays stamp duty until completion (it is due within 14 days of exercise when signed in Singapore). 中文：行使OTP后依序为登记caveat→法律查询→完成交易。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA RES coursebook P2.3 Conveyancing & Completion

---

**Q11.** In an HDB resale, when do the Option Fee and the Option Exercise Fee fit into the overall purchase price?

- A. They form part of the resale price and are credited toward the total the buyer pays the seller
- B. They are administrative fees paid to HDB and are separate from the purchase price
- C. They are non-refundable agency commissions paid to the salesperson
- D. They are paid to HDB and refunded to the buyer on completion

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> The Option Fee and Exercise Fee are paid by the buyer to the SELLER and form part of the resale price - they are effectively the deposit credited against the total price. A is correct. B is wrong: they go to the seller, not HDB, and are part of the price. C is wrong: they are not commission. D is wrong: they are not paid to HDB and are not refunded - they are applied to the price. 中文：OTP两项费用付给卖方，构成转售价的一部分（即首期款）。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB - Option to Purchase (https://www.hdb.gov.sg/residential/buying-a-flat/buying-procedure-for-resale-flats/plan-source-and-contract/option-to-purchase)

---

**Q12.** For a completed private resale, what is the typical timeframe from exercising the OTP to legal completion of the sale?

- A. About 21 days
- B. About 10 to 12 weeks
- C. About 8 weeks
- D. Up to 5 years

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> Private resale completion typically takes about 10 to 12 weeks after the OTP is exercised, allowing time for caveat lodgement, requisitions, loan disbursement and conveyancing. A (21 days) is the HDB option period. B (about 8 weeks) is the HDB resale completion timeframe after HDB acceptance, not private. D borrows the caveat validity period and is unrelated. 中文：私宅转售从行使OTP到完成约10–12周；HDB转售约8周。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA RES coursebook P2.3 / Key Timeframes

---

**Q13.** A Singapore Citizen sells a residential property he purchased on 1 September 2025 and disposes of it on 1 December 2026 (holding period more than 1 but not exceeding 2 years), at a price of $1,500,000 which equals market value. What Seller's Stamp Duty (SSD) is payable?

- A. $240,000 (16% - within 1 year)
- B. $120,000 (8% under the prior 3-year regime)
- C. $180,000 (12% under the current 4-year regime)
- D. $0 because SSD only applies to industrial property

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> The property was purchased on 1 Sep 2025, i.e. ON/AFTER 4 Jul 2025, so the CURRENT 4-year SSD regime applies: 16% / 12% / 8% / 4% over four years. A holding period of more than 1 but up to 2 years attracts 12%. 12% × $1,500,000 = $180,000, so C is correct. A applies the 16% (within 1 year) rate to the wrong tier. B applies the prior (11 Mar 2017 - 3 Jul 2025) 3-year regime's 8% rate, which does not apply to a Sep 2025 purchase. D is wrong: residential SSD clearly applies here. 中文：2025年9月购入适用新四年SSD制；持有1–2年税率12%，即$180,000。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS SSD for Residential Property, purchases on/after 4 Jul 2025 (https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/selling-or-disposing-property/seller's-stamp-duty-(ssd)-for-residential-property)

---

**Q14.** During the option period of an HDB resale OTP, once a buyer has submitted a Request for Value for a particular flat, what restriction applies?

- A. The valuation outcome lapses immediately if the buyer does not exercise within 14 days
- B. The seller may grant a second OTP to a back-up buyer at any time
- C. The buyer must exercise the OTP within 7 days of the valuation outcome
- D. HDB will not accept another Request for Value for the same flat (from the same or different buyers) until the OTP expires

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> Once HDB receives a Request for Value for a flat, it will not accept another request for that same flat from the same or any other buyer until the existing OTP expires - this prevents parallel valuations on the same flat. D is correct. B is wrong: the OTP system effectively ties up the flat with one buyer; a seller cannot freely grant a second active OTP. C and D invent deadlines - the valuation outcome is valid for 3 months and the option period is 21 days, not 7 or 14. 中文：HDB收到某单位的估价申请后，OTP到期前不再受理同一单位的其他估价申请。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB - Request for Value (https://www.hdb.gov.sg/residential/buying-a-flat/buying-procedure-for-resale-flats/plan-source-and-contract/request-for-value)

---

**Q15.** Which statement about Buyer's Stamp Duty (BSD) and Additional Buyer's Stamp Duty (ABSD) on a completed-property purchase is correct?

- A. BSD is buyer-profile-independent (same rates for all); only ABSD depends on citizenship and property count
- B. Both BSD and ABSD are charged on the LOWER of purchase price or market value
- C. BSD depends on the buyer's citizenship and number of properties; ABSD is the same for everyone
- D. ABSD applies to all property types including commercial and industrial

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> BSD is profile-independent: the same progressive rates apply to every buyer based on price/value alone. ABSD varies by buyer profile (Citizen/PR/Foreigner/Entity) and the number of residential properties owned. A is correct. C reverses the two duties. B is wrong: both are charged on the HIGHER of price or market value, not the lower. D is wrong: ABSD applies only to RESIDENTIAL property. 中文：BSD对所有买家一致；ABSD视身份与套数而定，且仅适用住宅。两者均按价与市值孰高计。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS BSD & ABSD (current 2026) (https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/buying-or-acquiring-property/buyer's-stamp-duty-(bsd))

---


## P2.4 Sale of Uncompleted/Developer Property: Progressive Payment, SSD, Sales Process

**Q1.** Mr Tan books a new launch condominium unit directly from a licensed developer. Under the standard Progressive Payment Scheme (PPS) for sale of uncompleted private residential property, what booking fee must he pay to obtain the Option to Purchase (OTP)?

- A. 1% of the purchase price
- B. 5% of the purchase price
- C. 10% of the purchase price
- D. 15% of the purchase price

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> Under the Housing Developers Rules, the booking fee for an OTP on an uncompleted developer unit is fixed at 5% of the purchase price (not negotiable like a private resale). Option B is correct. (A) 1% is the typical private RESALE option fee, not the developer booking fee. (C) 10% and (D) 15% are later progressive instalments (the 15% balance of the initial 20% downpayment is paid on/after exercise), not the booking fee. 中文：发展商新盘的购买选择权预订费固定为售价的5%，1%是私人转售的选择费。
>
> 📎 Source: Housing Developers (Control & Licensing) Act / URA Home Buyers Guide; https://www.ura.gov.sg/-/media/Corporate/Property/Home-Buyers-Guide/Home-Buyers-Guide-3-Sep-2025.pdf

---

**Q2.** A buyer pays the 5% booking fee for an uncompleted condo, receives the Sale & Purchase Agreement and title deeds, but then decides NOT to proceed and lets the OTP lapse without exercising it. What happens to his booking fee?

- A. The developer refunds 100% of the booking fee
- B. The developer forfeits 50% and refunds 50%
- C. The developer forfeits 25% of the booking fee and refunds 75%
- D. The developer forfeits 100% of the booking fee

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> Where a buyer does not exercise the OTP for an uncompleted developer unit, the developer is entitled to forfeit 25% (1/4) of the booking fee — equivalent to 1.25% of the purchase price — and must refund the remaining 75%. Option C is correct. (A) full refund is wrong — there is a prescribed forfeiture. (B) 50% and (D) 100% overstate the forfeiture; the prescribed amount is 25%. 中文：未行使发展商OTP，发展商没收预订费的25%（即售价的1.25%），退还75%。
>
> 📎 Source: Housing Developers Rules; URA Home Buyers Guide; https://www.ura.gov.sg/-/media/Corporate/Property/Home-Buyers-Guide/Home-Buyers-Guide-3-Sep-2025.pdf

---

**Q3.** After paying the 5% booking fee and receiving the S&P Agreement and title deeds from the developer, within what period must the buyer exercise the OTP for an uncompleted private residential unit?

- A. 7 calendar days
- B. 14 calendar days
- C. 8 weeks
- D. 3 weeks (21 days)

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> Under the standard developer sale framework, the OTP for an uncompleted unit must be exercised within 3 weeks after the developer delivers the S&P Agreement and title deeds. Option D is correct. (A) 7 days has no application here. (B) 14 days is the developer's deadline to DELIVER the S&P after the OTP is granted, not the buyer's exercise window. (C) 8 weeks is the deadline (from the OTP date) to pay the 15% balance of the downpayment, not the exercise period. 中文：买方须在发展商交付S&P及地契后3周（21天）内行使OTP；14天是发展商交付S&P的期限。
>
> 📎 Source: Housing Developers Rules; URA Home Buyers Guide; https://www.ura.gov.sg/-/media/Corporate/Property/Home-Buyers-Guide/Home-Buyers-Guide-3-Sep-2025.pdf

---

**Q4.** In the standard Progressive Payment Scheme for an uncompleted private condominium, what percentage of the purchase price is payable upon completion of the foundation work?

- A. 10%
- B. 5%
- C. 15%
- D. 25%

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> Completion of the foundation stage triggers a 10% progressive payment. Option A is correct. (B) 5% corresponds to later stages such as brick walls, roofing, electrical/plastering or car park/roads/drains (each 5%), not foundation. (C) 15% is the balance of the initial 20% downpayment (and the final CSC instalment), not the foundation-stage payment. (D) 25% is the payment on obtaining TOP. 中文：地基完成支付10%；TOP时支付25%。
>
> 📎 Source: Housing Developers Rules Schedule (Progressive Payment); https://www.propertyguru.com.sg/property-guides/condo-payment-schedule-97560

---

**Q5.** Under the standard Progressive Payment Scheme, which milestone triggers the LARGEST single progressive payment of 25% of the purchase price?

- A. Completion of the reinforced concrete framework
- B. Issue of the Temporary Occupation Permit (TOP)
- C. Signing of the Sale & Purchase Agreement
- D. Issue of the Certificate of Statutory Completion (CSC)

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> The single largest progressive payment of 25% is due upon issue of the Temporary Occupation Permit (TOP), when the unit becomes ready for occupation. Option B is correct. (A) the reinforced concrete framework stage is 10%. (C) the S&P signing triggers the balance of the 20% downpayment (the 15% portion), not 25%. (D) the CSC stage triggers the FINAL 15% (the last instalment), not 25%. 中文：TOP时支付最大的一笔25%；CSC时支付最后的15%。
>
> 📎 Source: Housing Developers Rules Schedule; https://www.propertyguru.com.sg/property-guides/condo-payment-schedule-97560

---

**Q6.** An uncompleted condominium has a purchase price of $2,000,000 bought under the standard Progressive Payment Scheme. The buyer has paid the 5% booking fee, the 15% balance of the downpayment on signing the S&P, and amounts for foundation (10%) and reinforced concrete framework (10%). When the developer notifies completion of the brick walls (5%) stage, how much is the buyer's cumulative outlay AFTER paying the brick-wall instalment?

- A. $800,000
- B. $1,000,000
- C. $900,000
- D. $700,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> Cumulative percentage = 5% (booking) + 15% (S&P balance) + 10% (foundation) + 10% (framework) + 5% (brick walls) = 45%. 45% × $2,000,000 = $900,000. Option C is correct. (A) $800,000 = 40%, omitting the brick-wall 5%. (B) $1,000,000 = 50%, adding an extra 5%. (D) $700,000 = 35%, omitting one stage. 中文：累计 5+15+10+10+5 = 45%，45% × 200万 = 90万元。
>
> 📎 Source: Housing Developers Rules Schedule (Progressive Payment); https://www.propertyguru.com.sg/property-guides/condo-payment-schedule-97560

---

**Q7.** Madam Lim buys a private resale apartment and the OTP is exercised (date of purchase) on 1 March 2026. She sells and the sale is completed on 1 December 2026. As the property was acquired on/after 4 July 2025, what Seller's Stamp Duty (SSD) rate applies?

- A. 0%
- B. 4%
- C. 12%
- D. 16%

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> For residential property acquired on/after 4 Jul 2025, the SSD holding period is 4 years with rates 16%/12%/8%/4%. A sale within 1 year of purchase (Mar 2026 to Dec 2026 is about 9 months) falls in the 'up to 1 year' tier = 16%. Option D is correct. (C) 12% is the >1–2 year tier (and was the old 1-year rate under the pre-Jul 2025 regime). (B) 4% is the >3–4 year tier. (A) 0% only applies after holding more than 4 years. 中文：2025年7月4日后购入，持有≤1年卖出，SSD为16%。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS SSD for Residential Property; https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/selling-or-disposing-property/seller's-stamp-duty-(ssd)-for-residential-property

---

**Q8.** A residential property was purchased on 10 August 2025 for $1,500,000. The owner sells it for $1,800,000 with the sale completed 2.5 years later (i.e. holding period more than 2 but not more than 3 years). The market value at sale is $1,750,000. How much Seller's Stamp Duty is payable?

- A. $144,000
- B. $140,000
- C. $72,000
- D. $216,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(hard)_
>
> Property acquired on/after 4 Jul 2025, so the current 4-year regime (16%/12%/8%/4%) applies. Holding >2–3 years = 8%. SSD is on the HIGHER of price or market value = higher of $1,800,000 and $1,750,000 = $1,800,000. 8% × $1,800,000 = $144,000. Option A is correct. (B) $140,000 wrongly uses market value $1,750,000 (8% × 1.75m). (C) $72,000 uses 4% (the >3–4 year tier). (D) $216,000 uses 12% (the >1–2 year tier). 中文：2025年7月后购入、持有2–3年=8%，按较高者180万计税 = 14.4万元。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS SSD for Residential Property; https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/selling-or-disposing-property/seller's-stamp-duty-(ssd)-for-residential-property

---

**Q9.** Which statement about Seller's Stamp Duty (SSD) on residential property is CORRECT?

- A. SSD is computed on the lower of the transacted price or market value
- B. SSD is computed on the higher of the transacted price or market value
- C. SSD rates differ depending on the seller's citizenship (SC, SPR, foreigner)
- D. SSD applies only to properties purchased by foreigners

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> Like BSD and ABSD, SSD is charged on the HIGHER of the actual transacted price or the market value as at the date of disposal. Option B is correct. (A) is the classic trap — it is the higher, not the lower. (C) is wrong — unlike ABSD, SSD does NOT depend on citizenship; it depends only on the holding period. (D) is wrong — SSD applies to any seller disposing of residential property within the holding period regardless of citizenship. 中文：SSD按价格与市价中的较高者计算，与卖方国籍无关（这点与ABSD不同）。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS SSD for Residential Property; https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/selling-or-disposing-property/seller's-stamp-duty-(ssd)-for-residential-property

---

**Q10.** A buyer takes a bank loan to finance an uncompleted condominium under the Progressive Payment Scheme. Compared with buying a completed property, what is a key feature of loan disbursement and interest under PPS?

- A. The full loan is disbursed at S&P signing, so the buyer pays interest on the full loan from day one
- B. No interest is payable until TOP is obtained
- C. The loan is disbursed progressively as each construction stage is reached, so interest accrues only on amounts drawn down
- D. Interest is charged at a fixed 4% stress-test rate throughout construction

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> Under PPS the bank disburses the loan in tranches matching each progressive stage, so the borrower pays interest only on the cumulative amount actually drawn down — interest is low early and rises as construction progresses. Option C is correct. (A) describes a lump-sum disbursement, which does not apply to BUC/PPS loans. (B) is wrong — interest accrues on each drawn tranche immediately, not deferred to TOP (deferral applies under a deferred payment scheme, not standard PPS). (D) confuses the TDSR stress-test medium-term floor rate with the actual chargeable interest rate. 中文：PPS下贷款按工程进度分批发放，利息只按已动用金额累计，初期低、后期高。
>
> 📎 Source: MAS housing loan rules; https://mortgagemaster.com.sg/blog/post/progressive-payment-scheme

---

**Q11.** When a salesperson markets an uncompleted unit on behalf of a licensed housing developer, which document must the developer make available to prospective buyers giving prescribed project information?

- A. The Tenancy Agreement
- B. A Letter of Intent
- C. An Estate Agency Agreement Form 5
- D. The Sale & Purchase Agreement in the prescribed form together with required disclosures

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(easy)_
>
> Developers must use the S&P Agreement in the prescribed statutory form and provide prescribed disclosures/information to buyers of uncompleted units. Option D is correct. (A) a Tenancy Agreement is for leasing, irrelevant to a sale. (C) Form 5 is the prescribed exclusive estate agency agreement between a vendor and an EA, not a developer sale document. (B) an LOI is a non-binding pre-document, not used in regulated developer sales. 中文：发展商须使用法定格式的买卖合约（S&P）并提供规定披露；Form 5是独家代理协议。
>
> 📎 Source: Housing Developers (Control & Licensing) Act / Rules; URA Home Buyers Guide; https://www.ura.gov.sg/-/media/Corporate/Property/Home-Buyers-Guide/Home-Buyers-Guide-3-Sep-2025.pdf

---

**Q12.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY — Mr & Mrs Goh (both Singapore Citizens) book a new launch unit at 'Riverbend Residences' for $1,600,000 on 5 May 2026. They pay the 5% booking fee. The developer delivers the S&P and title deeds on 12 May 2026.

What is the booking fee amount they paid, and by when must they exercise the OTP?

- A. $80,000; exercise within 3 weeks of 12 May 2026
- B. $16,000; exercise by 19 May 2026
- C. $80,000; exercise within 8 weeks of 5 May 2026
- D. $160,000; exercise within 14 days of 12 May 2026

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(hard)_
>
> Booking fee = 5% × $1,600,000 = $80,000. The OTP must be exercised within 3 weeks of the developer delivering the S&P and title deeds (12 May 2026). Option A is correct. (B) $16,000 uses 1% (resale option fee, wrong for developer sales) and a 7-day window. (C) has the right fee but 8 weeks is the deadline (from the OTP date) to pay the 15% downpayment balance, not the exercise window. (D) $160,000 is 10% (wrong) and 14 days is the developer's S&P-delivery deadline, not the exercise period. 中文：预订费=5%×160万=8万元；须在发展商交付S&P（5月12日）后3周内行使。
>
> 📎 Source: Housing Developers Rules; URA Home Buyers Guide; https://www.ura.gov.sg/-/media/Corporate/Property/Home-Buyers-Guide/Home-Buyers-Guide-3-Sep-2025.pdf

---

**Q13.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY — Continuing with Mr & Mrs Goh and 'Riverbend Residences' at $1,600,000 (both Singapore Citizens, this is their FIRST residential property).

The standard initial downpayment is 20% of the purchase price, paid as the 5% booking fee plus a balance on exercise of the OTP. How much is the BALANCE payment due on exercise, and what cash/CPF rule applies to the FIRST 5% (booking fee)?

- A. Balance $240,000 (15%); the booking fee may be paid fully from CPF
- B. Balance $240,000 (15%); the first 5% booking fee must be paid in cash
- C. Balance $320,000 (20%); the booking fee must be paid in cash
- D. Balance $80,000 (5%); the booking fee may be paid fully from CPF

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> The standard initial downpayment is 20% of $1,600,000 = $320,000, comprising the 5% booking fee ($80,000) plus a 15% balance on exercise = $240,000. Under MAS LTV rules a minimum 5% of the purchase price must be paid in CASH, and CPF cannot be used for this minimum cash component — so the 5% booking fee must be paid in cash. Option B is correct (right balance + right cash rule). (A) gives the correct balance but wrongly says the booking fee can come fully from CPF — the minimum 5% cash cannot be CPF. (C) overstates the balance as $320,000 (that is the full 20% downpayment, double-counting the booking fee already paid). (D) wrongly states the balance as only $80,000 (5%) and wrongly allows CPF for the booking fee. 中文：首付20%=32万元，扣除5%预订费后余款为15%=24万元；MAS规定最低5%须现金支付（不能用公积金），故预订费须现金。
>
> 📎 Source: MAS LTV / minimum cash downpayment rules; https://www.mas.gov.sg/regulation/explainers/new-housing-loans

---

**Q14.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY — Mr & Mrs Goh take a first housing bank loan for 'Riverbend Residences' ($1,600,000), with loan tenure 25 years and the loan not extending beyond age 65. They satisfy all conditions for the highest LTV.

What is the maximum loan they can obtain, and what is the minimum cash downpayment portion?

- A. Max loan 80% = $1,280,000; min cash 5%
- B. Max loan 75% = $1,200,000; min cash 25%
- C. Max loan 75% = $1,200,000; min cash 5% = $80,000
- D. Max loan 55% = $880,000; min cash 10%

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> For a first housing loan from a bank meeting all conditions (tenure ≤30 years and not extending beyond age 65), the maximum LTV is 75%, i.e. $1,200,000, with a minimum 5% cash downpayment ($80,000); the remaining 20% may come from CPF/cash. Option C is correct. (A) 80% LTV does not apply to bank loans (and the HDB concessionary loan cap was cut to 75% on 20 Aug 2024). (B) 25% cash is not required for a first loan at 75% LTV (only 5% cash is). (D) 55% LTV applies only when tenure >30 years or the loan extends beyond age 65 — not this case. 中文：首套贷款满足条件LTV=75%（120万），最低5%现金（8万元）。
>
> 📎 Source: MAS LTV limits; https://www.mas.gov.sg/regulation/explainers/new-housing-loans

---

**Q15.** A salesperson tells a prospective buyer of an uncompleted unit: 'Under the Progressive Payment Scheme you only pay interest on the disbursed amount, but remember the final instalment is held back until a key milestone.' Which milestone triggers the FINAL 15% instalment of the purchase price?

- A. Issue of the Temporary Occupation Permit (TOP)
- B. Completion of the car park, drains and roads
- C. Signing of the Sale & Purchase Agreement
- D. Issue of the Certificate of Statutory Completion (CSC)

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> The final 15% instalment is payable on issue of the Certificate of Statutory Completion (CSC) / legal completion — the last milestone after TOP. Option D is correct. (A) TOP triggers the 25% instalment, not the final 15%. (B) car park/drains/roads is an earlier 5% stage. (C) the S&P signing triggers an early downpayment-balance instalment, not the final one. 中文：最后的15%在CSC（法定竣工证）/法律交割时支付；TOP时支付25%。
>
> 📎 Source: Housing Developers Rules Schedule (Progressive Payment); https://www.propertyguru.com.sg/property-guides/condo-payment-schedule-97560

---


## P2.5 Conveyancing & Completion Process

**Q1.** In a private resale conveyancing transaction, at what point does the buyer typically acquire an equitable interest in the property that entitles them to lodge a caveat with SLA?

- A. On exercising the Option to Purchase (or signing the Sale & Purchase Agreement)
- B. On signing the Estate Agency Agreement with their RES
- C. Only after legal completion and registration of the transfer
- D. On payment of the Buyer's Stamp Duty to IRAS

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> Correct: A. A buyer acquires an equitable (beneficial) interest the moment they exercise the OTP / sign the S&P, because the contract for sale becomes binding; this caveatable interest is the basis for lodging a caveat. B is wrong: the EAA is merely an agency appointment and creates no interest in the land. C is wrong: legal title vests on registration, but the equitable interest (and right to caveat) arises far earlier, on exercise; waiting until completion would defeat the protective purpose of a caveat. D is wrong: paying BSD is a tax obligation, not the event that creates the proprietary interest. 中文: 买方在行使购买选择权(OTP)/签署买卖合约时取得衡平法权益,即可登记 caveat。
>
> 📎 Source: Land Titles Act 1993; CEA RES syllabus (legal vs equitable interest)

---

**Q2.** Which of the following BEST describes the purpose of pre-completion legal requisitions sent by the buyer's conveyancing lawyer to government bodies such as LTA, PUB, NEA and IRAS?

- A. To register the buyer's caveat against the title
- B. To confirm there are no road, drainage, acquisition or other government plans affecting the property and to establish a good root of title
- C. To obtain approval for the buyer to purchase a restricted residential property
- D. To pay the Buyer's Stamp Duty on behalf of the buyer

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> Correct: B. Legal requisitions are searches lodged with the relevant authorities to confirm the property is not affected by road-widening, drainage reserves, compulsory acquisition or similar plans, and form part of verifying a good root of title before completion. A is wrong: lodging a caveat is a separate STARS/SLA step, not a requisition. C is wrong: approval to buy restricted residential property is an LDAU/SLA function under the Residential Property Act, unrelated to routine requisitions. D is wrong: BSD is paid via IRAS e-Stamping; requisitions are information searches, not tax payment. 中文: 法律查询(requisitions)用于向政府部门确认产业不受道路、征用等计划影响,并确立良好产权来源。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA RES syllabus (Paper 2 - Conveyancing & Completion)

---

**Q3.** A buyer exercises a private resale OTP on 1 June 2026. Within what period must the Buyer's Stamp Duty be paid to avoid a late-payment penalty, and from what value is BSD computed?

- A. 14 days from completion; computed on the lower of purchase price or market value
- B. 30 days from exercise; computed on the purchase price only
- C. 14 days from exercise; computed on the higher of purchase price or market value
- D. 21 days from exercise; computed on the market value only

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> Correct: C. BSD must be paid within 14 days of the document being signed/executed in Singapore (for a resale, the date the OTP is exercised), and is assessed on the HIGHER of the purchase price or market value. B is wrong: 30 days applies only when the document is signed overseas (counted from receipt in Singapore), and BSD is not on price 'only'. A is wrong: the 14-day clock runs from exercise (execution), not completion, and the rule is the HIGHER, never the lower, of the two values. D is wrong: 21 days is the HDB OTP option period, not the stamp-duty deadline, and BSD is the higher of the two values. 中文: 行使 OTP 后14天内缴付 BSD,按成交价与市值中的较高者计算。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS Stamp Duty Basics for Property (14-day deadline, 2026)

---

**Q4.** During an HDB resale, the buyer makes a Request for Value to determine how much CPF and loan can be used. Which statement about this step is correct for 2026?

- A. The valuation is requested by the seller and is valid for 12 months
- B. It must be made before the OTP is granted and replaces the need for legal requisitions
- C. It is optional in all cases and never affects the financing of the purchase
- D. The Request for Value costs $120, takes around 10 working days, and the valuation is valid for 3 months

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> Correct: D. The buyer makes the Request for Value (fee $120 incl. GST) via My Flat Dashboard by the next working day after the Option Date; the outcome is typically available within 10 working days and the valuation is valid for 3 months, anchoring the CPF/loan amount. A is wrong: it is the buyer (not seller) who requests it, and validity is 3 months, not 12. C is wrong: where CPF/loan financing is used, the value directly determines how much CPF and loan can be applied. B is wrong: the Request for Value is made AFTER the OTP is granted, and it does not replace legal requisitions, which serve a different purpose. 中文: HDB 买方在取得 OTP 后申请估价($120,约10个工作日,有效3个月)以确定 CPF 与贷款额。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB Request for Value (2026)

---

**Q5.** Which source of funds can be used to pay the Additional Buyer's Stamp Duty (ABSD) on a residential purchase?

- A. Cash only, although CPF may be reimbursed afterwards subject to CPF rules
- B. CPF Ordinary Account funds, same as for the Buyer's Stamp Duty
- C. The buyer's housing loan from the bank
- D. It cannot be paid until after legal completion

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> Correct: A. ABSD must be paid in cash upfront; CPF cannot be used to pay ABSD directly at the point of stamping (CPF may only reimburse it later, subject to CPF withdrawal rules and sufficient OA balance). B is wrong: while BSD can be paid from CPF OA, ABSD generally cannot be drawn from CPF for upfront payment. C is wrong: stamp duties are not financed by the housing loan, which is for the purchase price. D is wrong: stamp duty (BSD and ABSD) is due within 14 days of exercise, well before completion. 中文: ABSD 须先以现金缴付,CPF 不能直接用于缴 ABSD(BSD 才可用 CPF)。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS ABSD; CPF reimbursement rules (2026)

---

**Q6.** A buyer purchases a residential property for $1,200,000, which is also the market value. Using the 2026 BSD residential rates, what is the Buyer's Stamp Duty payable?

- A. $30,600
- B. $32,600
- C. $36,000
- D. $28,800

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> Correct: B. BSD = 1% x $180,000 + 2% x $180,000 + 3% x $640,000 + 4% x $200,000 = $1,800 + $3,600 + $19,200 + $8,000 = $32,600. A ($30,600) wrongly applies 3% to the top $200,000 instead of 4%. C ($36,000) is a flat 3% of $1.2m, ignoring the tiered structure. D ($28,800) understates the top tiers. The marginal/tiered structure must be applied, not a single flat rate. 中文: BSD 分级计算:1%/2%/3%/4% 各档,$1.2m 的 BSD = $32,600。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS BSD rates (eff. 15 Feb 2023, unchanged in 2026)

---

**Q7.** A Singapore Citizen and her spouse buy a $1,500,000 condominium as their FIRST residential property (price equals market value). Ignoring loan considerations, what is the TOTAL stamp duty (BSD + ABSD) payable at exercise?

- A. $44,600 plus 5% ABSD
- B. $74,600 (BSD plus 20% ABSD)
- C. $44,600 (BSD only; ABSD is 0% for SC's first property)
- D. $89,600 (BSD plus 30% ABSD)

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> Correct: C. BSD = 1% x180k + 2% x180k + 3% x640k + 4% x500k = $1,800 + $3,600 + $19,200 + $20,000 = $44,600. As this is the SC buyers' FIRST residential property, ABSD is 0%, so total = $44,600. B is wrong: 20% ABSD applies to an SC's SECOND property, not the first. A is wrong: 5% is the SPR first-property ABSD rate, not applicable to Singapore Citizens. D is wrong: 30% is the SC third-property ABSD rate. The trap is matching the correct ABSD rate to citizenship AND property count. 中文: SC 首套房 ABSD 为 0%,仅 BSD $44,600;须正确区分公民身份与第几套房。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS BSD + ABSD rates (rates held since 27 Apr 2023, unchanged 2026)

---

**Q8.** In an HDB resale where HDB acts as the solicitor for both parties, which statement about the completion appointment is correct?

- A. Completion is done entirely online and neither party need attend
- B. Completion typically occurs about 21 days after the OTP is exercised
- C. Only the seller must attend; the buyer signs remotely
- D. Both buyer and seller generally attend in person at HDB Hub, where title transfers, the loan is disbursed, CPF refunds are processed and sale proceeds are released

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> Correct: D. When HDB is the solicitor, both parties usually attend the completion appointment in person at HDB Hub, where the transfer is effected, the loan disbursed, CPF refunds processed and proceeds released (a private solicitor's representative may attend on a party's behalf if private lawyers are used). A is wrong: there is a formal completion appointment, not a fully unattended online process when HDB acts. C is wrong: both parties (not just the seller) attend. B is wrong: HDB resale completion is roughly 8 weeks after HDB's acceptance of the resale application, not 21 days (21 days is the OTP option period). 中文: HDB 作为律师时,买卖双方通常须亲临 HDB Hub 办理交易完成手续。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB Resale Completion; CEA RES syllabus

---

**Q9.** Which statement BEST describes the legal nature of a caveat lodged during conveyancing?

- A. It is a precautionary notice protecting the caveator's interest, and the Registrar cannot remove it on his own motion
- B. It is a mandatory step without which the purchase is void
- C. It transfers legal title to the buyer immediately on lodgement
- D. It is valid for only 21 days and cannot be extended

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> Correct: A. A caveat is a precautionary 'freeze' that warns third parties of the caveator's claim; it is not mandatory, and the Registrar cannot remove it of his own motion (where an inconsistent dealing is lodged, the caveator is put on notice and must obtain a court order within 30 days under s127 to maintain it). B is wrong: lodging a caveat is precautionary, not a validity requirement for the sale. C is wrong: a caveat protects an interest but does not transfer legal title, which vests only on registration of the transfer. D is wrong: a caveat is valid for 5 years and may be extended before it lapses. 中文: Caveat 是预防性通知,非强制;Registrar 不能自行删除,有效5年可续期。
>
> 📎 Source: Land Titles Act 1993 Part XII; SLA Land Titles Registry

---

**Q10.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Mr Tan grants an HDB resale OTP to Mr Lee on 5 May 2026, with an Option Fee of $1,000. The OTP states the standard 21-day option period. Mr Lee wants to exercise on the last possible day. What is the latest date and time, and what is the maximum total of Option Fee plus Exercise Fee that can be collected?

- A. 26 May 2026 by 5pm; combined fees must not exceed $1,000
- B. 26 May 2026 by 4pm; combined Option + Exercise Fee must not exceed $5,000
- C. 19 May 2026 by 4pm; combined fees must not exceed $10,000
- D. 2 June 2026 by 4pm; combined fees must not exceed $5,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> Correct: B. The HDB OTP option period is 21 calendar days and expires at 4pm on the last day. Counting 21 calendar days from 5 May (the grant date) gives 26 May 2026, so Mr Lee must exercise by 4pm on 26 May. The Option Fee plus Exercise Fee combined (the deposit) must not exceed $5,000, with the Option Fee itself capped at $1,000. A is wrong: expiry is 4pm, not 5pm, and the cap is $5,000 combined, not $1,000. C is wrong: 19 May is too early (that is 14 days) and $10,000 overstates the cap. D is wrong: 2 June is too late (about 28 days). 中文: HDB OTP 21天,4pm 截止,本案为 2026年5月26日4pm;Option+Exercise Fee 合计不超过 $5,000。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB Option to Purchase (option period & deposit cap, 2026)

---

**Q11.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Madam Ong sells her private condominium. The buyer's lawyer lodges a caveat to protect the buyer's interest. Two weeks later, Madam Ong's earlier mortgagee lodges a transfer that is inconsistent with the buyer's caveat, and the Registrar serves notice on the buyer (caveator). Within what period must the buyer take action, and what action must be taken to maintain the caveat?

- A. 14 days; file a fresh caveat with SLA
- B. 5 years; simply renew the caveat online via STARS
- C. 30 days; obtain a court order to maintain the caveat, failing which it lapses
- D. 21 days; pay an extension fee to SLA

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> Correct: C. Under s127 of the Land Titles Act, where an inconsistent dealing is lodged and the Registrar serves notice on the caveator, the caveator must obtain a court order within 30 days to maintain the caveat, failing which the caveat lapses and the dealing proceeds. A is wrong: the response period is 30 days and the remedy is a court order, not merely re-lodging. B is wrong: the 5-year validity is the general lifespan, but once notice is served under s127 the 30-day court-order rule overrides simple renewal. D is wrong: 21 days and an extension fee do not apply; a court order is required. 中文: 依 LTA s127,Registrar 发出通知后,caveator 须在30天内取得法院命令以维持 caveat,否则失效。
>
> 📎 Source: Land Titles Act 1993 s127

---

**Q12.** A buyer takes a bank loan to purchase an HDB resale flat. Which statement about the conveyancing arrangement is correct?

- A. The buyer may use HDB's in-house legal team to act for the bank as well
- B. The seller's lawyer automatically acts for the buyer's bank
- C. No conveyancing lawyer is required when a bank loan is used
- D. The buyer must appoint a private law firm that is on the bank's approved panel to handle the conveyancing

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> Correct: D. If the buyer takes a bank loan, the conveyancing must be handled by a private law firm on the bank's approved panel; HDB's in-house legal counsel cannot act for the bank's mortgage. A is wrong: HDB's legal team does not act for a bank loan's mortgage requirements. C is wrong: a conveyancing lawyer is required to handle the transfer, mortgage and requisitions. B is wrong: the seller's lawyer represents the seller, not the buyer's financing bank, and there is no automatic dual role. 中文: 用银行贷款买 HDB 时,须委任银行认可名单内的私人律师办理转让与按揭。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB Resale conveyancing (bank loan) 2026

---

**Q13.** In a typical private resale, which sequence correctly reflects the conveyancing and completion process?

- A. Exercise OTP and appoint lawyer -> lodge caveat -> legal requisitions and examine title -> completion (exchange of cashier's orders, keys and transfer instrument)
- B. Completion -> exercise OTP -> lodge caveat -> legal requisitions
- C. Legal requisitions -> completion -> exercise OTP -> lodge caveat
- D. Lodge caveat -> completion -> exercise OTP -> legal requisitions

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> Correct: A. The logical conveyancing flow is: exercise the OTP and appoint a conveyancing lawyer, lodge the buyer's caveat, conduct legal requisitions and examine the Certificate of Title, then complete by exchanging cashier's orders, keys, title and the transfer instrument. B, C and D all place completion or requisitions before the OTP is exercised, which is impossible because the binding contract and equitable interest arise only on exercise, and completion is always the final step. 中文: 正确次序:行使 OTP 并委任律师 -> 登记 caveat -> 法律查询与查验产权 -> 完成交易(交换银行本票、钥匙、转让文件)。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA RES syllabus (Paper 2 - Conveyancing & Completion)

---

**Q14.** What is the approximate timeframe for completion in a typical PRIVATE resale property transaction after the OTP is exercised?

- A. About 21 days
- B. About 10 to 12 weeks
- C. About 8 weeks after HDB acceptance
- D. About 6 months

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> Correct: B. A private resale typically completes about 10 to 12 weeks after the OTP is exercised, allowing time for requisitions, loan documentation and the exchange on completion. A is wrong: 21 days is the HDB OTP option period, not the completion timeframe. C is wrong: about 8 weeks after HDB acceptance is the HDB resale (not private) completion benchmark. D is wrong: 6 months is far longer than the standard private completion period. 中文: 私人产业转售一般在行使 OTP 后约10至12周完成。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA RES syllabus; standard private resale completion timeline (2026)

---

**Q15.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: A foreign buyer (not from an FTA-exempt country) exercises an OTP to buy a $2,000,000 condominium unit as his first residential property in Singapore (price equals market value). His RES must advise on the stamp duties due within 14 days of exercise. What is the ABSD payable, and can the buyer proceed without LDAU approval?

- A. ABSD of $1,300,000 (65%); LDAU approval is required
- B. ABSD of $400,000 (20%); LDAU approval is required for any foreigner buying residential property
- C. ABSD of $1,200,000 (60%); no LDAU approval needed because a condominium unit is non-restricted property
- D. ABSD of $0; foreigners pay no ABSD on their first property

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> Correct: C. A foreigner (non-FTA-exempt) pays 60% ABSD on residential property regardless of count: 60% x $2,000,000 = $1,200,000, due within 14 days of exercise. A unit in an approved condominium development is NON-restricted under the Residential Property Act, so no LDAU approval is needed (LDAU approval is only for restricted property such as landed homes and vacant land). B is wrong: 20% is an SC second-property rate, and condos do not require LDAU approval. A is wrong: 65% is the entity/trustee rate, and condos are non-restricted. D is wrong: foreigners pay 60% ABSD even on the first property. 中文: 非 FTA 豁免外国人买公寓:ABSD 60% = $120万;公寓为非限制产业,无需 LDAU 批准。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS ABSD (60% foreigner, 2026); Residential Property Act 1976; SLA foreign ownership rules

---


## P2.6 Tenancy & Leases: Agreements, Lease Stamp Duty, Deposits, Landlord/Tenant Rights

**Q1.** A tenant signs a 1-year lease at $3,000 per month, executed in Singapore. What is the lease (tenancy) stamp duty payable?

- A. $1,000
- B. $288
- C. $576
- D. $144

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(easy)_
>
> For a lease of 4 years or less, lease duty = 0.4% x total rent. Total rent = $3,000 x 12 = $36,000; 0.4% x $36,000 = $144 (D). $288 wrongly applies 0.8% (or doubles the year count). $576 is not a correct computation here. $1,000 is the Average Annual Rent (AAR) exemption threshold, not a duty amount. 中文：四年以内租约印花税=0.4%×总租金=$36,000×0.4%=$144。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS – Renting a Property (Stamp Duty): https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/renting-a-property

---

**Q2.** A 6-year lease is signed with rent of $4,000 per month throughout. How is the lease stamp duty correctly computed?

- A. 0.4% x 4 x ($4,000 x 12) = $768
- B. 0.4% x ($4,000 x 12 x 6) = $1,152
- C. 0.4% x ($4,000 x 12) = $192
- D. Exempt because the lease exceeds 4 years

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> For a lease exceeding 4 years (or indefinite), duty = 0.4% x 4 x Average Annual Rent (AAR). AAR = $48,000, so 0.4% x 4 x $48,000 = $768 (A). Option B wrongly uses total rent over all 6 years (the >4yr rule caps it at 4 x AAR). Option C charges only one year's AAR. There is no exemption for long leases; the only AAR-based exemption is AAR <= $1,000. 中文：超过四年的租约按0.4%×4×年均租金计=$768。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS – Renting a Property (Stamp Duty): https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/renting-a-property

---

**Q3.** A landlord rents a room to a student at $800 per month on a 1-year lease, executed in Singapore. Regarding lease stamp duty, which statement is correct?

- A. The lease is exempt because the monthly rent of $800 is $1,000 or less
- B. Duty of $38.40 is payable, and by convention the tenant stamps within 14 days of signing
- C. The lease is exempt because the Average Annual Rent does not exceed $1,000
- D. A flat minimum duty of $1 is always payable regardless of rent

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> The exemption is tested on Average Annual Rent (AAR), not monthly rent. AAR = $800 x 12 = $9,600, which EXCEEDS $1,000, so the lease is NOT exempt. Duty = 0.4% x $9,600 = $38.40, and a document signed in Singapore must be stamped within 14 days (the tenant pays by convention) — so B is correct. Option A is the classic trap: it tests the threshold against the $800 monthly figure instead of the annualised AAR. Option C correctly states the exemption rule in the abstract, but the exemption does NOT apply here because AAR is $9,600, so it is the wrong choice for this lease. Option D is wrong: there is no universal $1 minimum; a $1 minimum only applies where duty otherwise computed rounds below $1. 中文：免税按年均租金AAR≤$1,000判定。此处AAR=$9,600超过门槛，须缴税$38.40，并在签署后14天内由租客缴纳；故A正确。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS – Renting a Property (Stamp Duty): https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/renting-a-property

---

**Q4.** A tenancy agreement is signed in Singapore on 1 March. By what date must the lease stamp duty be paid to avoid penalties?

- A. Within 7 days (by 8 March)
- B. Within 21 days (by 22 March)
- C. Within 14 days (by 15 March)
- D. Within 30 days (by 31 March)

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(easy)_
>
> A document signed in Singapore must be stamped within 14 days of signing (C). 7 days and 21 days are not stamp-duty deadlines. 30 days applies only when the document is signed OUTSIDE Singapore (counted from when it is received in Singapore). 中文：在新加坡签署的文件须在14天内缴印花税；境外签署为30天。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS – Renting a Property (Stamp Duty): https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/renting-a-property

---

**Q5.** A salesperson is engaged by a landlord who wants to give one agency the sole right to find a tenant. Which prescribed estate agency agreement form should be used?

- A. Form 3 (Non-exclusive – Lease, landlord)
- B. Form 4 (Non-exclusive – Lease, tenant)
- C. Form 8 (Exclusive – Lease, tenant)
- D. Form 7 (Exclusive – Lease, landlord)

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> The landlord wants an EXCLUSIVE (sole) arrangement, so the exclusive lease-by-landlord form is Form 7 (D). Form 3 is the non-exclusive landlord version — wrong because the landlord wants sole rights. Form 4 and Form 8 are tenant-side forms (non-exclusive and exclusive respectively), not for a landlord. 中文：业主独家委托出租用Form 7（独家-出租-业主）。
>
> 📎 Source: Estate Agents (Estate Agency Work) Regulations / CEA Prescribed Estate Agency Agreements Forms 1–8

---

**Q6.** A tenant signs a 2-year lease at $5,000 per month. Following standard Singapore tenancy convention, what security deposit (excluding any utilities deposit) would the landlord typically require?

- A. $10,000 (two months' rent)
- B. $5,000 (one month's rent)
- C. $15,000 (three months' rent)
- D. $2,500 (half a month's rent)

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> Market convention is one month's rent per year of lease, so a 2-year lease = 2 months = $10,000 (A). $5,000 is the norm for a 1-year lease only. $15,000 (3 months) over-states it. Half a month ($2,500) reflects a common rental commission/co-broke norm, not a security deposit. 中文：押金惯例为每年租期一个月，两年租约=两个月=$10,000。
>
> 📎 Source: Tenancy market convention – security deposit (FACT PACK Paper 2 s11)

---

**Q7.** At the end of a lease, the landlord wants to deduct from the security deposit for: (i) faded paint from sunlight, (ii) a cracked basin caused by the tenant dropping a heavy object, and (iii) carpet worn thin in normal walking paths. Which deduction is properly chargeable to the tenant?

- A. Only (i)
- B. Only (ii)
- C. (i) and (iii)
- D. All three

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> The deposit covers tenant-caused DAMAGE but NOT fair wear and tear. Faded paint (i) and normally worn carpet (iii) are fair wear and tear and cannot be deducted. The cracked basin (ii) results from the tenant's act, so it is chargeable — hence Only (ii) (B). Options A, C and D wrongly include wear-and-tear items. 中文：押金只可扣租客损坏（破裂盆），不可扣自然耗损（褪色油漆、磨损地毯）。
>
> 📎 Source: Tenancy convention – fair wear and tear vs tenant damage (FACT PACK Paper 2 s11–12)

---

**Q8.** A tenant on a 2-year lease finds the air-conditioner needs a $120 servicing repair. The tenancy agreement contains a standard minor-repair clause with a $200 per-item threshold. Who bears this cost?

- A. The landlord, because all repairs are the landlord's duty
- B. Split equally between landlord and tenant
- C. The tenant, because the cost is within the minor-repair threshold
- D. The managing agent under the estate agency agreement

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> Under a minor-repair clause, the tenant bears repair costs up to the stated per-item threshold (commonly ~$150–$300); $120 is below the $200 cap, so the tenant pays (C). The landlord bears only the excess above the threshold and major/structural repairs, so A is wrong. There is no automatic 50/50 split (B). The estate/managing agent has no repair liability (D). 中文：小修条款下，单项低于$200由租客承担，此$120修理由租客付。
>
> 📎 Source: Tenancy agreement – minor repair / diplomatic clauses (FACT PACK Paper 2 s9, s12)

---

**Q9.** An SC owner has fulfilled MOP on a standard 5-room flat and wants to rent out the WHOLE flat. Which statement is correct?

- A. He may rent the whole flat to anyone for any duration without HDB approval
- B. He may rent only individual bedrooms, never the whole flat
- C. He cannot rent the whole flat because whole-flat rental is never permitted for HDB
- D. He must obtain HDB approval, observe a minimum 6-month tenancy, and the Non-Citizen Quota (8% neighbourhood / 11% block) applies, with Malaysians exempt from the quota

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> Whole-flat rental requires HDB approval, a minimum 6-month tenancy, and is subject to the Non-Citizen Quota (8% neighbourhood / 11% block), with Malaysians exempt (D). A is wrong because approval and a minimum tenancy are required. C and B are wrong: standard flats CAN be rented whole after MOP. 中文：满MOP的标准组屋整租需HDB批准、最短6个月，并受非公民配额（8%/11%）限制，马来西亚人除外。
>
> 📎 Source: HDB renting-out rules; Non-Citizen Quota (FACT PACK Paper 2 s16)

---

**Q10.** What is the maximum validity period of an exclusive estate agency agreement for leasing residential property?

- A. 3 months
- B. 1 month
- C. 6 months
- D. 12 months

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(easy)_
>
> A prescribed exclusive estate agency agreement has a maximum validity of 3 months with no automatic renewal (A). 1 month is too short; 6 and 12 months exceed the cap. Note there is a separate 3-month post-expiry commission tail for a tenant/buyer the agent introduced during the validity period. 中文：独家委托协议最长有效期为3个月，不可自动续约。
>
> 📎 Source: CEA Prescribed Estate Agency Agreements – exclusive agreements (FACT PACK Paper 2 s1)

---

**Q11.** Regarding who is liable for lease (tenancy) stamp duty, which statement is most accurate?

- A. Only the landlord is liable by law
- B. The tenant pays by convention, but landlord and tenant are jointly liable
- C. Only the tenant is liable by law
- D. The estate agent is liable as the party who prepared the agreement

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> By market convention the tenant pays the lease duty, but legally both landlord and tenant are jointly and severally liable (B). A and C are wrong because liability is joint, not exclusive to either party. D is wrong — the estate agent is never the liable party for the duty. 中文：习惯上由租客缴纳，但法律上业主与租客共同负责。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS – lease duty liability; CEA conventions (FACT PACK Paper 2 s10)

---

**Q12.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Mr Tan, an SC, owns a private condominium unit. He leases it furnished to an expatriate at $6,000/month (of which $500/month is attributable to movable furniture) on a 3-year lease executed in Singapore. The expatriate's company is GST-registered. QUESTION: What is the lease stamp duty payable on this tenancy?

- A. $792
- B. $288
- C. $864
- D. Exempt as residential leases are GST-exempt

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> Lease duty for a 3-year lease (<=4 years) = 0.4% x total rent. Total rent = $6,000 x 36 = $216,000; 0.4% = $864 (C). The furniture portion is part of the rent (consideration) for stamp-duty purposes, so the full $6,000 is used. Option A ($792) wrongly excludes the $500 furniture and computes on $5,500 x 36 = $198,000. Option C uses only one year's rent. Option D confuses GST (a residential lease is GST-exempt) with stamp duty — they are different taxes; lease duty still applies. 中文：三年租约印花税=0.4%×总租金$216,000=$864；GST免税不等于印花税免税。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS – Renting a Property (Stamp Duty); GST treatment (FACT PACK Paper 2 s10; GST section)

---

**Q13.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Ms Lim signs a 2-year private lease at $4,500/month. The agreement includes a diplomatic clause (minimum 12-month occupation, 2 months' notice) and a security deposit of 2 months' rent. Ten months into the lease, her employer transfers her overseas and she invokes the diplomatic clause. QUESTION: Which outcome is most consistent with a standard diplomatic clause?

- A. She may terminate immediately and forfeit only the deposit
- B. She cannot terminate early because the lease is for a fixed 2-year term
- C. She may terminate at any time after month 1 by giving 2 months' notice
- D. She cannot yet invoke the clause because the 12-month minimum occupation period has not been met, even with notice

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> A typical diplomatic clause permits early termination only AFTER a minimum occupation period (here 12 months) AND with the required notice (here 2 months). At month 10 the 12-month minimum is not yet met, so she cannot validly invoke it yet (D). A is wrong — the clause is not a deposit-forfeiture mechanism; lawful invocation returns the deposit subject to the lease terms. B is wrong because a diplomatic clause is precisely what allows early exit despite a fixed term. D ignores the 12-month minimum occupation requirement. 中文：外交条款需满足最短居住期（12个月）并给予通知，第10个月尚未满足，故不能行使。
>
> 📎 Source: Tenancy agreement – diplomatic clause; security deposit conventions (FACT PACK Paper 2 s9, s11)

---

**Q14.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: A commercial unit is leased for 5 years. Rent is $10,000/month for years 1–2 and $12,000/month for years 3–5, executed in Singapore. QUESTION: What is the lease stamp duty payable (round down to nearest dollar)?

- A. 0.4% x 4 x $134,400 = $2,150
- B. 0.4% x ($10,000x24 + $12,000x36) = $2,688
- C. 0.4% x 4 x $13,520 = $216
- D. Exempt because commercial leases attract GST instead of stamp duty

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> The lease exceeds 4 years, so duty = 0.4% x 4 x Average Annual Rent (AAR). Total rent = ($10,000 x 24) + ($12,000 x 36) = $240,000 + $432,000 = $672,000 over 5 years; AAR = $672,000 / 5 = $134,400. Duty = 0.4% x 4 x $134,400 = $2,150.40, rounded down to $2,150 (A). Option B wrongly charges 0.4% on the FULL 5-year rent, ignoring the 4 x AAR cap for >4yr leases. Option C uses a monthly figure as the AAR. Option D wrongly treats GST as replacing stamp duty — both can apply to a commercial lease. 中文：超过四年用0.4%×4×AAR；AAR=$672,000/5=$134,400，印花税=$2,150。不可按全期租金计（B错），GST不替代印花税（D错）。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS – lease duty for leases exceeding 4 years (https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/renting-a-property)

---

**Q15.** Under a standard Singapore tenancy agreement, which obligation correctly belongs to the LANDLORD rather than the tenant?

- A. Paying the monthly utility bills
- B. Carrying out major or structural repairs to the property
- C. Paying the lease stamp duty by convention
- D. Keeping the interior in good and tenantable repair (fair wear and tear excepted)

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(medium)_
>
> Major and structural repairs are the landlord's responsibility (B). Utilities (A) are paid by the tenant. Lease stamp duty (C) is paid by the tenant by convention. Keeping the interior in good and tenantable repair (D) is a tenant obligation. The landlord's core duties centre on structural/major repairs and returning the deposit (less lawful deductions). 中文：大型/结构性维修属业主责任；水电、印花税、室内日常保养属租客。
>
> 📎 Source: Landlord/tenant obligations (FACT PACK Paper 2 s12)

---


## P2.7 Calculations Master Set: BSD/ABSD/SSD, LTV, Loan, Commission, Property Tax, Lease Stamp Duty, GST

**Q1.** A Singapore Citizen buying his FIRST residential property for $900,000 (market value $880,000) asks his RES how much Buyer's Stamp Duty (BSD) he must pay. Which statement is the BEST basis for the calculation?

- A. BSD is computed on $880,000 because IRAS uses the lower of price or market value
- B. No BSD is payable because it is his first property
- C. BSD is computed on $900,000, the higher of price or market value
- D. BSD depends on his citizenship, so as an SC first-timer he pays 0%

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(easy)_
>
> BSD is always charged on the HIGHER of the purchase price or market value, so $900,000 is used. Option A inverts the rule. Option B confuses BSD with ABSD — BSD is buyer-profile-independent and payable by everyone including first-timers. Option D wrongly applies the ABSD first-timer 0% to BSD; BSD does not vary with citizenship or property count. 中文：BSD按成交价与市价中较高者征收，与买家身份无关，首套也要付。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS Buyer's Stamp Duty (BSD) — https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/buying-or-acquiring-property/buyer's-stamp-duty-(bsd)

---

**Q2.** A residential property is bought for $1,200,000 (above market value). What is the correct Buyer's Stamp Duty (BSD) payable?

- A. $30,600
- B. $28,800
- C. $36,000
- D. $32,600

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> Tiered residential BSD: 1%×$180,000=$1,800; 2%×$180,000=$3,600; 3%×$640,000=$19,200; 4%×$200,000 (portion above $1m up to $1.2m)=$8,000. Total=$32,600. Option A under-counts the top tier. Option C wrongly applies a flat 3% to the whole $1.2m. Option B applies a blended 2.4% guess. 中文：住宅BSD分级1%/2%/3%/4%，$1.2m的BSD为$32,600。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS BSD rates (residential, top rate 6% since 15 Feb 2023) — https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/buying-or-acquiring-property/buyer's-stamp-duty-(bsd)

---

**Q3.** A Singapore Permanent Resident (SPR) is buying her SECOND residential property for $1,500,000 (market value $1,520,000). What ABSD amount applies?

- A. $456,000 (30% of $1,520,000)
- B. $450,000 (30% of $1,500,000)
- C. $76,000 (5% of $1,520,000)
- D. $304,000 (20% of $1,520,000)

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> An SPR buying a 2nd residential property pays 30% ABSD (rates eff. 27 Apr 2023), charged on the HIGHER of price or market value = $1,520,000, giving $456,000. Option B uses the lower price base. Option C applies the SPR first-property rate of 5%. Option D applies the SC second-property rate of 20% (wrong profile). 中文：SPR第二套房ABSD为30%，按较高者$1,520,000计算=$456,000。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS ABSD rates (eff. 27 Apr 2023): SPR 5%/30%/35% — https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/buying-or-acquiring-property/additional-buyer's-stamp-duty-(absd)

---

**Q4.** A US citizen (not an SPR) is buying his FIRST residential property in Singapore for $2,000,000. Under the current ABSD framework, what is his ABSD liability?

- A. $1,200,000 — foreigners pay 60% ABSD
- B. $0 — under the relevant Free Trade Agreement he is accorded Singapore Citizen treatment, and an SC's first property attracts 0% ABSD
- C. $100,000 — he pays the SPR first-property rate of 5%
- D. $400,000 — he pays 20% as a second-tier buyer

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> Under the US-Singapore FTA, US nationals are accorded the same ABSD treatment as Singapore Citizens; an SC buying a first residential property pays 0% ABSD, so $0. Option A applies the general foreigner 60% rate, ignoring the FTA remission. Option C misapplies the SPR 5% rate. Option D applies the SC 2nd-property 20% rate, but this is his first property. The same treatment covers nationals/PRs of Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway and Switzerland under the ESFTA. 中文：根据美新自贸协定，美国公民按SC待遇，首套房ABSD为0%。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS Foreigners Eligible for ABSD Remission under FTAs (US, Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway, Switzerland) — https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/appeals-refunds-reliefs-and-remissions/common-stamp-duty-remissions-and-reliefs-for-property/foreigners-eligible-for-absd-remission-under-free-trade-agreements-(ftas)

---

**Q5.** An investor purchased a residential condominium on 1 September 2025 for $1,800,000 and sells it on 1 December 2026 for $2,000,000 (market value $1,950,000). What Seller's Stamp Duty (SSD) is payable?

- A. $160,000 — 8% on $2,000,000
- B. $0 — the holding period exceeds the SSD window
- C. $240,000 — 12% on $2,000,000
- D. $156,000 — 8% on $1,950,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> The property was bought on/after 4 Jul 2025, so the current SSD regime applies (4-year window; 16/12/8/4%). Holding period is ~1 year 3 months, i.e. more than 1 year up to 2 years = 12%. SSD is on the HIGHER of price or market value = $2,000,000, giving $240,000. Options A/D wrongly use the >2-3 year rate of 8%. Option B wrongly assumes the holding period exceeded the (now 4-year) window. 中文：2025年7月4日后购入适用新SSD（4年期），持有>1至2年为12%，按较高者$2m=$240,000。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS SSD for Residential Property (purchases on/after 4 Jul 2025; rates 16/12/8/4%) — https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/selling-or-disposing-property/seller's-stamp-duty-(ssd)-for-residential-property

---

**Q6.** A homeowner bought a residential flat on 1 February 2024 and is considering selling it. Under the SSD rules applicable to her purchase date, how long must she hold the property to avoid any SSD?

- A. More than 4 years
- B. More than 1 year
- C. More than 2 years
- D. More than 3 years

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> Her purchase (1 Feb 2024) falls in the 11 Mar 2017–3 Jul 2025 window, where SSD applies over a 3-year holding period (12/8/4/0%). Holding beyond 3 years means 0% SSD. Option A is the NEW 4-year window for purchases on/after 4 Jul 2025 — a date trap. Options C and B are intermediate tiers, not the zero-SSD threshold. 中文：2024年2月购入适用旧制（3年期），持有超过3年即0% SSD。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS SSD for Residential Property (purchases 11 Mar 2017–3 Jul 2025; 3-year window) — https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/selling-or-disposing-property/seller's-stamp-duty-(ssd)-for-residential-property

---

**Q7.** A buyer is taking his FIRST housing loan from a bank for a private condo. The loan tenure is 25 years and will be fully repaid before he turns 65. What is the maximum loan-to-value (LTV) and minimum cash down payment?

- A. 75% LTV, 5% minimum cash
- B. 55% LTV, 10% minimum cash
- C. 80% LTV, 5% minimum cash
- D. 75% LTV, 25% minimum cash

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> First housing loan with tenure ≤30 years AND not extending beyond age 65 qualifies for the 75% LTV limit, requiring a minimum 5% cash down (the remaining 20% may be CPF/cash). Option B is the reduced 55% limit applying only when tenure >30 years or loan extends beyond age 65. Option C uses the outdated 80% figure. Option D applies the 2nd-loan 25% cash rule. 中文：首套贷款符合条件可达75% LTV，最低现金首付5%。
>
> 📎 Source: MAS LTV limits for housing loans — https://www.mas.gov.sg/regulation/explainers/new-housing-loans

---

**Q8.** A buyer with an existing outstanding housing loan applies for a SECOND bank housing loan (tenure ≤30 years, not extending beyond age 65) to buy a property valued at $1,000,000. What is the maximum loan and the minimum cash component of the down payment?

- A. Max loan $350,000; minimum cash $250,000
- B. Max loan $450,000; minimum cash $250,000
- C. Max loan $750,000; minimum cash $50,000
- D. Max loan $450,000; minimum cash $50,000

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(hard)_
>
> A second housing loan (conditions met) is capped at 45% LTV = $450,000. The minimum cash down payment for a 2nd loan is 25% = $250,000 (the remaining 30% may be CPF/cash). Option B uses the 3rd-loan LTV of 35%. Option C wrongly applies first-loan terms (75%/5%). Option D keeps the correct loan but uses the first-loan 5% cash figure. 中文：第二套贷款上限45%（$450k），最低现金首付25%（$250k）。
>
> 📎 Source: MAS LTV limits for 2nd housing loan (45% LTV, 25% min cash) — https://www.mas.gov.sg/regulation/explainers/new-housing-loans

---

**Q9.** A salaried couple earns a combined gross monthly income of $12,000 with no other debts, buying an HDB resale flat with a bank loan. Applying the binding ratio for HDB purchases (and the residential stress-test floor), what is the approximate maximum monthly housing instalment the regulations permit?

- A. $4,800 — a 40% blended cap applies to HDB
- B. $6,600 — TDSR at 55% is the binding cap
- C. $3,600 — MSR at 30% is the binding cap for HDB flats
- D. $3,000 — MSR at 25% applies to HDB flats

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(hard)_
>
> For HDB flats (and ECs from a developer), MSR caps the monthly housing instalment at 30% of gross monthly income = $3,600, computed at the 4.0% p.a. stress-test floor (the medium-term interest rate floor since 30 Sep 2022). MSR is more restrictive than TDSR (55% = $6,600), so MSR binds. Option B ignores that MSR applies to HDB. Option C invents a 40% blended cap. Option D uses a wrong 25% MSR figure. 中文：HDB购房适用MSR 30%上限（$3,600），比TDSR 55%更严。
>
> 📎 Source: MAS MSR/TDSR rules (MSR 30%, TDSR 55%, 4% stress-test floor) — https://www.mas.gov.sg/regulation/explainers/new-housing-loans/msr-and-tdsr-rules

---

**Q10.** A landlord signs a 2-year residential tenancy at $3,500 per month. Total rent over the term is $84,000. What lease stamp duty is payable?

- A. $84
- B. $168
- C. $1,344
- D. $336

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(medium)_
>
> For a lease of 4 years or less, stamp duty = 0.4% × total rent = 0.4% × $84,000 = $336. Option B halves it (one year only). Option C wrongly applies the >4-year formula (0.4% × 4 × AAR). Option A is a random low figure. 中文：≤4年租约印花税=0.4%×总租金=0.4%×$84,000=$336。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS Lease/Tenancy Stamp Duty — 0.4% of total rent for leases ≤4 years — https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/renting-a-property

---

**Q11.** A commercial unit is leased for 6 years at an Average Annual Rent (AAR) of $60,000. What is the lease stamp duty?

- A. $960
- B. $1,440
- C. $96
- D. $2,400

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(medium)_
>
> For leases exceeding 4 years (or indefinite), stamp duty = 0.4% × 4 × AAR = 0.4% × 4 × $60,000 = $960 (the multiplier is capped at 4 years). Option B wrongly uses the full 6 years (0.4% × 6 × AAR). Option C is off by a factor of 10 (misplaced decimal). Option D applies a flat 4% rate. The AAR here exceeds the $1,000 exemption threshold so duty applies. 中文：超过4年租约，印花税=0.4%×4×AAR=$960（封顶在4年）。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS Lease Stamp Duty — leases >4 years: 0.4% × 4 × AAR — https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/renting-a-property

---

**Q12.** An RES negotiates an agreed seller's commission of 2% (before GST) on a residential resale at $850,000. Including 9% GST, what total commission will the seller pay?

- A. $17,000
- B. $18,530
- C. $18,700
- D. $15,300

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: B**  _(easy)_
>
> Base commission = 2% × $850,000 = $17,000. GST = 9% × $17,000 = $1,530. Total = $18,530. Option A omits GST. Option C applies a flat 10% GST. Option D applies 1.8% by error. GST is charged on the agency SERVICE (standard-rated) even though the sale of residential property itself is an exempt supply. 中文：佣金$17,000加9% GST（$1,530）=$18,530；代理服务收9% GST。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS GST rate 9% (since 1 Jan 2024); residential sale exempt but agency service standard-rated — https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/goods-services-tax-(gst)/basics-of-gst/current-gst-rates

---

**Q13.** Which statement about GST on Singapore property transactions in 2026 is CORRECT?

- A. Residential property sales are zero-rated, so the seller can claim input tax
- B. All property sales attract 9% GST regardless of property type
- C. The sale and lease of residential property is an exempt supply, while sale/lease of commercial and industrial property is standard-rated at 9%
- D. Commercial property is exempt from GST while residential is standard-rated at 9%

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: C**  _(medium)_
>
> Residential property sale and lease are EXEMPT supplies; commercial and industrial property are standard-rated at 9% (rate since 1 Jan 2024). Option B is wrong because residential is exempt. Option A confuses exempt with zero-rated — residential is exempt (no input tax recovery), not zero-rated. Option D inverts the treatment. 中文：住宅买卖/出租为免税供应；商业及工业物业按9%标准税率。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS GST Real Estate — residential property exempt; commercial/industrial standard-rated 9% (since 1 Jan 2024) — https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/goods-services-tax-(gst)/specific-business-sectors/real-estate

---

**Q14.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: Mr and Mrs Tan are both Singapore Citizens. Mr Tan owns one residential property in his sole name. The couple now wish to jointly buy a second residential condo for $2,200,000 (market value $2,150,000). Considering ABSD profiling rules for joint purchases, what ABSD rate and amount apply BEFORE any remission?

- A. 20% on $2,150,000 = $430,000 (charged on market value)
- B. 0% because Mrs Tan personally owns no property
- C. 30% on $2,200,000 = $660,000 (treated as a 3rd property)
- D. 20% on $2,200,000 = $440,000 (highest-rate profile among joint buyers applies; a 2nd property for the household)

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: D**  _(hard)_
>
> For a joint purchase, ABSD is assessed on the profile attracting the HIGHEST rate. Mr Tan already owns one property, so for him this is a 2nd property; as SCs the 2nd-property rate is 20%, applied to the HIGHER of price/market value = $2,200,000 = $440,000. Option B wrongly looks only at Mrs Tan. Option C treats it as a 3rd property (30%) — neither spouse owns two. Option D uses 20% but applies the lower market value. A married-couple ABSD remission may later apply if the first property is sold within the timeline. 中文：联名购买按最高税率身份计税，丈夫第二套SC税率20%，按较高者$2.2m=$440,000。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS ABSD — joint purchase assessed at highest applicable profile; higher of price/market value — https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/stamp-duty/for-property/buying-or-acquiring-property/additional-buyer's-stamp-duty-(absd)

---

**Q15.** *(Case study)* CASE STUDY: An owner-occupier's private condominium has an Annual Value (AV) of $60,000 for 2026. Using the owner-occupier residential property tax rates effective 1 Jan 2025 (before any rebate), what is the property tax payable?

- A. $2,720
- B. $6,000
- C. $3,600
- D. $7,200

> ✅ **Answer / 答案: A**  _(hard)_
>
> Owner-occupier tiers (eff. 1 Jan 2025): first $12,000 @ 0% = $0; next $28,000 (>$12k–$40k) @ 4% = $1,120; next $10,000 (>$40k–$50k) @ 6% = $600; next $10,000 (the $50k–$60k portion, within the >$50k–$75k 10% band) @ 10% = $1,000. Total = $0 + $1,120 + $600 + $1,000 = $2,720. Option B applies a flat 10% to the whole AV. Option C uses a wrong 6% blended figure. Option D applies 12% (the non-owner-occupier first tier). 中文：自住分级：0%+4%+6%+10%=$2,720；统一10%为非住宅/地皮税率。
>
> 📎 Source: IRAS owner-occupier residential property tax rates (eff. 1 Jan 2025) — https://www.iras.gov.sg/taxes/property-tax/property-owners/property-tax-reliefs/lower-property-tax-rates-for-owner-occupied-residential-properties

---
